Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
advanced
8 min
Weak Qalb: Qalb al-Taswiyah and the Nawafil-Wudu Analogy
Explaining weak qalb: qalb al-taswiyah and the nawafil-wudu example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the weak form of qalb (qalb al-taswiyah) and distinguish it from valid qalb that produces true contradiction (munaqadah).

Core Idea
Qalb al-taswiyah is weak because it forces equality without true contradiction; proper qalb must produce munaqadah.

This passage introduces a third method of qalb known as qalb al-taswiyah (inversion by equalization). Unlike the strong form of qalb that generates a direct contradiction (munaqadah), this method only creates opposition (mu'aradah) by equalizing two rulings. The example involves the dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is over whether a supererogatory act becomes binding upon commencement. By understanding why this form of qalb is weak, you will sharpen your ability to evaluate qiyas arguments and recognise when a rebuttal is insufficient.

Guided Path
1
Identify the weak form of qalb
Recognize that qalb al-taswiyah is the third method described and note its characteristic: it seeks to equalize two aspects (here vow and commencement) but fails to produce contradiction.
The text labels it weak (da'if).
2
Understand the Shafi'i position and their analogy
The Shafi'is analogize supererogatory acts to wudu: since breaking wudu does not require completion, commencing wudu does not bind; similarly, supererogatory acts are not binding upon commencement.
The common property is 'not completed when invalidated'.
3
Trace the Hanafi response
The Hanafis respond by requiring equality (istawa') between vow and commencement in both wudu and supererogatory acts. Since supererogatory acts are binding by vow (consensus), equality demands they also be binding upon commencement.
This response is qalb al-taswiyah.
4
Evaluate why this response is weak
The Hanafi response only achieves mu'aradah (opposition) by introducing a new ruling; it does not directly contradict the Shafi'i's cause (non-necessity upon invalidation). Thus, the original qiyas remains unchallenged in its core.
The text states 'ذهب المناقضة' (the contradiction disappeared).
5
Apply the lesson to evaluate qalb
In evaluating qalb, always check if the rebuttal produces munaqadah or merely mu'aradah. Only the former is valid.
Valid qalb requires both opposition and contradiction.

Source Text

وَقَدْ تَقْلب الْعِلَّةُ مِنْ وَجْهِ أَخَرَ وَهُوَ ضَعِيفٌ مِثَالُهُ قَوْلُهُمْ هَذِهِ عِبَادَةٌ لَا تُمْضَى فِي فَاسِدِهَا فَوَجَبَ أَنْ لَا يَلْزَمَ بِالشُّرُوعِ كَالْوُضُوْءِ فَيُقَالُ لَهُمْ لَمَّا كَانَ كَذَلِكَ وَجَبَ أَنْ يَسْتَوِى فِيْهِ عَمَلُ النَّذْرِ وَالشُّرُوعِ كَالْوُضُوْءِ وَهُوَ ضَعِيفٌ مِنْ وُجُوْهِ الْقَلْبِ لِاَنَّهُ لَمَا جَاءَ بِحُكُم أَخَرَ ذَهَبَتِ الْمُنَاقَضَةً وَلاَنَ الْمَقْصُودُ مِنَ الْكَلَام مَعْنَاهُ وَالْاِسْتِوَاءُ مُخْتَلِفٌ فِى الْمُعْنَى ثُبُوتٌ مِنْ وَجْهِ وَسُقُوطٌ مِنَ وَجْهِ عَلَى وَجْهِ التَّضَادِ وَذَلِكَ مُبْطِلٌ لِلْقِيَاسِ ۔
ترجمہ :۔ اور کبھی قلب علت ہوتا ہے دوسرے طریقہ پر ، اور وہ ضعیف ہے، اس کی مثال شوافع کا قول ہے کہ یہ نوافل ایسی عبادت ہے جس کے فاسد کو پورا نہیں کیا جاتا تو ضروری ہے کہ شروع کرنے سے بھی لازم نہ ہو، جیسے وضو،
پس ان سے کہا جائے گا کہ جب ایسا ہے تو واجب ہے کہ نفل میں نذر اور شروع کا حکم برابر ہو جیسے وضو، اور یہ قلب کے طریقوں میں سے ضعیف طریقہ ہے، اس لئے کہ سائل جب دوسرا حکم لے آیا تو مناقضہ ختم ہو گیا، اور اس لئے کہ کلام سے مقصود اس کے معنی ہوتے ہیں، اور برابری معنی میں مختلف ہے من وجہ ثبوت ہے اور من وجہ سقوط ہے تضاد کے طریقہ پر ، اور یہ قیاس کو باطل کرنے والا ہے۔ تشریح : ۔ مصنف عالی فرماتے ہیں کہ قلب کا ایک تیسرا طریقہ بھی ہے ، جس کو قلب تسو یہ کہتے ہیں لیکن یہ طریقہ ضعیف اور فاسد ہے، کیونکہ اس میں صرف معارضہ ہے، مناقضہ نہیں ہے، جب کہ قلب میں معارضہ کے ساتھ مناقضہ بھی ہوتا ہے۔ اس کی مثال شوافع کے نزدیک نفلی عبادت شروع کرنے سے لازم نہیں ہوتی لہذا اگر شروع کر کے توڑ دی تو قضا واجب نہیں ، اور احناف کے نزدیک شروع کرنے سے لازم ہو جاتی ہے، اور شروع کر کے اگر فاسد کر دیا تو قضا واجب ہوتی ہے۔ شوافع نفلی عبادت کو وضو پر قیاس کرتے ہیں کہ جس طرح وضو درمیان میں فاسد ہو جائے تو اتمام لازم نہیں ، اور نہ وضو شروع کرنے سے اتمام لازم ہوتا ہے، اسی طرح نفلی عبادت بھی نہ شروع کرنے سے لازم ہوگی اور نہ فاسد کرنے سے اس کی قضاء وا تمام لازم ہوگا، الغرض شوافع نے عدم لزوم بالشروع کے لئے عدم لزوم فی الفساد کو علت قراردیا، یعنی فاسد کرنے سے لازم نہ ہو نا علت ہے شروع کرنے سے لازم نہ ہونے کی اور اس کو وضو پر قیاس کیا۔ لیکن اس پر معارضہ احناف کی طرف سے اس طرح ہوگا کہ ٹھیک ہے، آپ نے نوافل کو وضو پر قیاس کیا ہے، مگر دیکھو وضو میں نذر اور شروع دونوں کا حکم برابر ہے ، تو اسی طرح نفلی عبادت میں بھی نذر و شروع کا حکم برابر ہونا چاہیے۔ یعنی وضو نذر ماننے سے لازم نہیں ہوتا اور نہ شروع کرنے سے لازم ہوتا ہے، تو اس طرح مساوات نفلی عبادت میں بھی ہونی چاہیے، کہ نہ نذر سے لازم ہو اور نہ شروع کرنے سے لازم ہو، کیونکہ وضو مقیس علیہ ہے اور اس میں مساوات ہے تو نفلی عبادت جو مقیس ہے اس میں بھی مساوات ہونی چاہیے ۔۔ حالانکہ نفلی عبادت نذر سے بالا جماع لازم ہو جاتی ہے ،تو دونوں میں برابری پیدا کرنے کا تقاضہ تو یہ ہے کہ نفلی عبادت شروع کرنے سے بھی لازم ہو جائے، جیسے نذر سے بالا جماع لازم ہو جاتی ہے۔ غرض احناف نے کہا کہ عدم اتمام فی الفساد عدم لزوم بالشروع کی علت نہیں بلکہ استواء کی علت ۔ ں ہے، اور یہ مساوات وضو میں عدم لزوم سے متحقق ہوتی ہے کہ وضو نہ نذر سے لازم ہوتا ہے نہ شروع کرنے سے ۔۔اور نوافل میں لزوم سے متحقق ہوتی ہے کہ نوافل نذر سے بھی لازم ہو جاتے ہیں اور شروع کر نے سے بھی ۔۔ تو اس طرح یہاں قلب ہوا۔
And sometimes the cause is inverted in another way, and it is weak. Its example is their statement: 'This is an act of worship that is not completed when invalidated, so it should not be binding upon commencement, like wudu.' So it will be said to them: 'Since that is the case, it is necessary that in supererogatory acts, the effect of vow and commencement be equal, like wudu.' And this is weak among the methods of qalb, because when he brought another ruling, the contradiction disappeared, and because the purpose of speech is its meaning, and equality in meaning differs: it is proven from one aspect and nullified from another, in a contradictory manner, and that invalidates the analogy.
Translation: Sometimes the inversion of the cause occurs in another way, and it is weak. Its example is the Shafi'is' statement: 'This supererogatory act of worship is not completed when invalidated, so it must not be binding upon commencement, like wudu.' So it will be said to them: 'Since that is the case, it is necessary that in supererogatory acts, the ruling of vow and commencement be equal, like wudu.' And this is a weak method among the methods of qalb, because when the questioner brings another ruling, the contradiction ceases, and because the purpose of speech is its meaning, and equality in meaning differs: it is established from one aspect and void from another in a contradictory way, and that invalidates the analogy.
Explanation: The author states that there is a third method of qalb, called qalb al-taswiyah (inversion by equalization), but it is weak and invalid, because it contains only opposition (mu'aradah), not contradiction (munaqadah), whereas qalb involves both opposition and contradiction. Its example: According to the Shafi'is, a supererogatory act is not binding upon commencement; so if one starts and then breaks it, qada' is not obligatory. According to the Hanafis, it becomes binding upon commencement, and if broken, qada' is obligatory. The Shafi'is analogize supererogatory acts to wudu: just as wudu, if invalidated midway, does not require completion, and starting wudu does not make it binding, similarly a supererogatory act is not binding upon starting, nor does its invalidation require qada' or completion. In short, the Shafi'is made 'non-necessity upon invalidation' the cause for 'non-necessity upon commencement' and analogized it to wudu. However, the Hanafi response is: Agreed, you analogized to wudu, but note that in wudu, the rulings of vow and commencement are equal: wudu is not binding by vow nor by commencement. Therefore, in supererogatory acts, the rulings of vow and commencement should also be equal: it should not be binding by vow nor by commencement, because wudu is the analogized-to (maqis alayh) and it has equality. However, supererogatory acts are binding by vow by consensus. Therefore, to achieve equality, supererogatory acts must also be binding upon commencement, just as they are binding by vow. In short, the Hanafis said that non-completion upon invalidation is not the cause for non-necessity upon commencement, but rather the cause for equalization (istawa'). This equalization is realized in wudu by non-necessity (neither from vow nor from commencement), and in supererogatory acts by necessity (binding from both vow and commencement). Thus, here is the inversion.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage discusses a weaker form of qalb al-illa known as 'qalb al-taswiyah' (inversion by equalization). The author explains that unlike the strong form of qalb which maintains contradiction (munaqadah), this form only achieves opposition (mu'aradah) without resolving the conflict. The example concerns supererogatory acts (nawafil): Shafi'is argue that such acts are not binding upon commencement, analogizing to wudu. Hanafis respond by requiring equality between vow and commencement in both supererogatory acts and wudu, but since supererogatory acts are binding by vow (by consensus), the equality demanded by the analogy actually requires that they also be binding upon commencement. This inversion is deemed weak because it introduces a new ruling (binding upon commencement) that the Shafi'i argument did not intend, and the equality sought is contradictory. The author notes that this method fails to properly rebut the original analogy.

Key Terms
قلب تسویہ (qalb al-taswiyah): A weak form of qalb that equalizes two rulings (vow and commencement) to force a contradiction, but only achieves opposition (mu'aradah) without true contradiction (munaqadah).
نفلی عبادت (nafli 'ibadah): Supererogatory act of worship, such as a voluntary prayer or fast.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why is qalb al-taswiyah considered weak?
A) It relies on a defective analogy.
B) It only achieves opposition (mu'aradah) without contradiction (munaqadah).
C) It uses wudu as a model, which is not a valid act of worship.
D) It requires consensus on vows.

Key Takeaway
Qalb al-taswiyah is a weak form of qalb because it introduces a new ruling, failing to produce true contradiction (munaqadah); valid qalb requires both opposition and contradiction.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
Essential vs. Accidental Attributes: The Fasting Intention Dispute
Explaining tarjih of essential attribute over accidental with a fasting dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that essential attributes (wasf dhati) are preferred over accidental attributes (wasf aridi) in tarjih, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the fasting intention case.

Core Idea
Essential attributes (like time parts) are inseparable and thus override accidental attributes (like being an act of worship) in determining a ruling.

Tarjih (preference) between conflicting attributes is a key tool in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. When an essential attribute (wasf dhati) conflicts with an accidental one (wasf aridi), the essential takes precedence because it is inseparable from the essence. This lesson applies that principle to a classic dispute between the Hanafis and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the validity of a Ramadan fast when intention (niyyah) is made after dawn but before noon. By examining both sides, you will learn how the principle of tarjih by essential attribute operates in practice.

Guided Path
1
State the principle of tarjih
Identify the core Hanafi rule: when two attributes conflict, the essential attribute (wasf dhati) is preferred over the accidental (wasf aridi). Understand that the essential is inseparable from the essence, while the accidental can be absent without destroying the essence.
Essential attributes are constitutive; accidental are contingent.
2
Present the disputed case
Set up the scenario: A person observing a Ramadan fast makes intention (niyyah) after dawn but before noon. According to the Hanafis, a missed intention can be made up before noon. Here, part of the day had intention, part did not. Since fasting admits no division (tab'id), either the whole fast is valid or invalid. Both schools agree on this, but differ on which part to prefer.
The disputed element is whether the valid or invalid part should govern the whole.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i argument
Examine Imam al-Shafi'i's reasoning: fasting is an act of worship (accidental attribute), so caution requires the whole to be invalid because part lacked intention. He gives priority to the accidental attribute (being worship) over time parts.
Shafi'i uses the accidental attribute (worship) to prefer invalidity.
4
Analyze the Hanafi argument
Examine the Hanafi reasoning: the majority of time parts (essential attribute) had intention. By the principle 'al-akthar hukm al-kull' (the majority gives the ruling to the whole), the fast is valid. The essential attribute (time parts, which are constitutive) is given preference over the accidental (being worship).
Time parts are essential because the day cannot exist without them; intention being an act of worship is accidental.
5
Conclude with tarjih
Determine which position is preferred according to Hanafi usul: the essential attribute is more fundamental and inseparable, so it takes precedence. Thus the fast is valid. Note that this is a legitimate ikhtilaf where the Hanafi position is mufta bihi.
The principle of tarjih by essential attribute is applied here.

مصنف یہ فرماتے ہیں تعارض کی صورت میں وصف ذاتی کی وجہ سے ترجیح دینا وصف عارضی کے مقابلہ میں افضل وارحج ہے، کیونکہ حال یعنی وصف عارضی ذات کے ساتھ قائم ہوتا ہے، ذات کے تابع ہوتا ہے، اور تابع اصل کو باطل نہیں کر سکتا ہے۔ بقول صاحب نامی مصنف کی عبارت میں نظر ہے، کیونکہ عبارت سے ذات کی وصف پر ترجیح مفہوم ہورہی ہے ،اور اس میں کوئی کلام نہیں ہے، کلام تو ایسے دو صفوں میں ہے کہ ایک وصف ذاتی ہو،اور دوسر اوصفِ عارضی ہو لہذا یہ کہنا انسب ہے کہ وصف عارض کبھی ذات سے جدا ہو جاتا ہے، ذات اس کے بغیر بھی پائی جاتی ہے، اور وصف ذاتی ذات سے کبھی جدا نہیں ہوتا اور ذات اس کے بغیر نہیں پائی جاتی لہذا وصف ذاتی کی وجہ سے ترجیح اولی ہے وصفِ عارض سے۔ اسی اصل پر ہمارے اور امام شافعی اہلیہ کے درمیان ایک مسئلہ میں اختلاف ہو گیا، مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر رمضان کے روزہ میں کسی نے شروع سے نیت نہ کی ، نصف النہار سے پہلے پہلے نیت کی تو شوافع کے نزدیک روزہ نہ ہوگا اور ہمارے نزدیک روزہ ہو جائے گا کیوں کہ یہاں دن کا بعض حصہ بغیر نیت کے ہوا اور بعض حصہ نیت کے ساتھ گویا آدھا صحیح اور آدھا فاسد ہوا اور روزہ میں تجربی نہیں ہے، لہذا یا تو پورا صیح ہو گا یا پورا فاسد ہوگا، فاسد حصہ کو ترجیح دیں گے تو پورا روزہ فاسد ہوگا اور صحیح حصہ کو ترجیح دیں گے تو پورا روزہ صحیح ہوگا ، دونوں طرح وجہ ترجیح ہے، امام شافعی نے فاسد حصہ کو ترجیح دی ، وہ اس طرح -- کہ روزہ عبادت ہے جس کی حقیقت مفطرات ثلثہ سے امساک ہے لیکن محض امساک عبادت نہیں ، جب تک اس کے ساتھ نیت نہ ہو ، تو جب دن کے ایک حصہ میں نیت نہیں پائی گئی تو عبادات کے باب میں احتیاط کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ روزہ معتبر نہ ہو، کیوں کہ آدھا فاسد ہوا اور آدھا صحیح ، تو عبادت کے باب میں پورے کو فاسد کہنا احوط ہے، لیکن ہم کہتے ہیں کہ جب دن کے اکثر حصہ میں نیت پائی گئی اور بعض حصہ میں نیت نہیں پائی گئی ، تو دن کے اکثر اجزا جونیت کے ساتھ ہیں اس کو بعض اجزا پر جو بغیر نیت کے ہیں ترجیح دیں گے، لاکثر حکم الکل کے قاعدے سے، کیونکہ روزہ ایک عبادت ہے جس میں تجربی نہیں ہے، یا تو پورا صحیح ہوگا یا پورا فاسد، الغرض امام شافعی نے عبادت ہونے کے پہلو کو اختیار کرتے ہوئے فاسد کو صحیح پر ترجیح دی، (یعنی دن کے جس حصہ میں نیت نہیں تھی اس میں روزہ فاسد ہے اور جس حصہ میں نیت پائی گئی اس میں روزہ صحیح ہوا ) اور روزہ کا عبادت ہونا وصف عارضی ہے، کیوں کہ یہ عبادت بنتا ہے نیت سے نفس امساک عبادت نہیں ہے، تو عبادت ہو نا امساک کے لئے وصف عارض ہے جو کبھی امساک سے جدا بھی ہوتا ہے ، جیسے کوئی صرف بھوکا رہا تو امساک ہے عبادت نہیں ،غرض عبادت ہونا روزہ کا وصف عارضی ہے اور ہم نے دن کے اجزاء کے اعتبار سے ترجیح دی، کیوں کہ اکثر اجزاء میں نیت تھی ، بعض میں نہ تھی تو اکثر کو تر جیح دیتے ہوئے روزہ کو صحیح قرار دیا، اور وقت کے اجزاء کل وقت کا وصف ذاتی ہے، بلکہ مقوم ہے، کیونکہ کثرت امر وجودی ہے، لہذا وہ وصف ذاتی ہوگا، تو ہم نے وصف ذاتی کو ترجیح دی وصف عارضی پر ، اور ہم نے کہا کہ کثرت اجزاء کی وجہ سے روزہ صحیح ہوگا، اور عبادت ہونے کی وجہ سے فساد کو ترجیح نہیں دی کیونکہ عبادت ہونا وصف عارض ہے۔
The author says: In case of conflict, giving preference due to an essential attribute over an accidental attribute is superior and more preponderant, because the state (i.e., accidental attribute) subsists with the essence, is subordinate to the essence, and the subordinate cannot nullify the principal. According to the owner of the name, there is a consideration in the author's expression, because from the expression, preference of the essence over the attribute is understood, and there is no disagreement in that; the disagreement is between two attributes, one essential and the other accidental. So it is more appropriate to say that the accidental attribute sometimes separates from the essence, the essence can exist without it, while the essential attribute never separates from the essence, and the essence cannot exist without it. Hence, preference due to the essential attribute is more appropriate than due to the accidental. On this principle, a disagreement occurred between us and Imam al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, in a certain issue: If someone did not make the intention (niyyah) from the beginning for the fast of Ramadan, but made it before midday, then according to the Shafi'is the fast will not be valid, but according to us the fast will be valid. Because here a part of the day passed without intention and a part with intention, so it is as if half is valid and half invalid. And the fast does not admit of division (tab'id), so either the whole is valid or the whole is invalid. If we give preference to the invalid part, the whole fast is invalid; if we give preference to the valid part, the whole fast is valid. There is a basis for preference in both ways. Imam al-Shafi'i gave preference to the invalid part in this way: The fast is an act of worship whose reality is abstention (imsak) from the three nullifiers, but mere abstention is not worship unless accompanied by intention. When intention was absent in a part of the day, then in the chapter of acts of worship, caution requires that the fast not be considered valid, because half is invalid and half valid, so declaring the whole invalid is more cautious. But we say: When intention was present in the majority of the day and absent in a part, we give preference to the majority of parts that have intention over the few parts without intention, by the principle of 'the majority takes the ruling of the whole' (al-akthar hukm al-kull), because the fast is an act of worship that does not admit division; either the whole is valid or the whole is invalid. In short, Imam al-Shafi'i, considering the aspect of being an act of worship, gave preference to the invalid over the valid (i.e., the part without intention is invalid, the part with intention is valid). And the fast's being an act of worship is an accidental attribute, because it becomes worship by intention; the mere abstention is not worship. So being worship for abstention is an accidental attribute that sometimes separates from abstention, like a person who merely remains hungry: he has abstention but not worship. Thus, being worship for fasting is an accidental attribute. And we gave preference based on the parts of the day, because intention existed in the majority of parts, not in some, so giving preference to the majority we declared the fast valid. And the parts of time are an essential attribute of the whole time, indeed constitutive (muqawwim), because multiplicity (kathrah) is an existential matter, so it is an essential attribute. So we gave preference to the essential attribute over the accidental, and we said that due to the multiplicity of parts the fast is valid, and we did not give preference to invalidity due to being an act of worship because being an act of worship is an accidental attribute.
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This passage is a dispute (ikhtilaf) between the Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding the application of a usul principle: when two attributes conflict, the essential (dhati) is preferred over the accidental (aridi). The author explains that the essential attribute is inseparable from the essence, while the accidental can be absent. He then applies this to the fasting issue: if a person makes intention after dawn but before noon in Ramadan, is the fast valid? The Shafi'is say no, because fasting is an act of worship requiring intention for its validity; since a part of the day lacked intention, caution dictates the whole fast is invalid. They rely on the accidental attribute (being worship) to prefer invalidity. The Hanafis say the fast is valid because the majority of the day had intention; they prefer the essential attribute (the parts of time being constitutive of the day) over the accidental attribute (being worship). They invoke the principle 'al-akthar hukm al-kull' (the majority gives the ruling to the whole). This illustrates that in Hanafi usul, essential attributes (like time parts) take precedence over accidental ones (like being worship) in determining a ruling when they conflict.

Key Terms
وصف ذاتی (wasf dhati): An attribute that is inseparable from the essence; the essence cannot exist without it.
وصف عارض (wasf aridi): An attribute that can be separated from the essence; the essence can exist without it.
ترجیح (tarjih): Giving preference to one ruling or attribute over another when there is conflict.
نیت (niyyah): Intention made for an act of worship, essential for its validity in fasting.
الاکثر حکم الکل (al-akthar hukm al-kull): The principle that the majority gives the ruling to the whole.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis for the Hanafi preference of the essential attribute over the accidental in the fasting intention dispute?
A) Caution in acts of worship
B) The principle that the majority of time parts with intention gives the ruling to the whole
C) The fact that fasting is a physical act that cannot be split
D) The hadith that intention is required from night

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, when essential and accidental attributes conflict, the essential attribute (inseparable from the essence) is given precedence in tarjih, as demonstrated in the fasting intention dispute.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

12 min
Yamin as a Metaphorical Cause (Sabab Majazi)
Dispute on whether oaths are real or metaphorical causes in usul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi classification of yamin as a sabab majazi to determine the ruling on tanjiz (immediate execution) nullifying ta'liq (suspension).

Core Idea
An oath is a metaphorical cause because it legislates righteousness, not penalty.

This lesson delves into a fundamental usul dispute: is an oath (yamin) a real cause that directly triggers a ruling, or a metaphorical cause that leads to it indirectly? The answer shapes how we understand suspensive conditions. We will unpack the Hanafi position using the source text, focusing on why the oath's primary purpose (birr) makes it a sabab majazi and how this plays out in the tanjiz vs. ta'liq issue.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested issue
Recognize that the dispute centers on the nature of yamin (oath) as a cause (sabab) in usul al-fiqh. Is it haqiqi, fi ma'na al-illa, or majazi?
This sets the stage for the entire argument.
2
State the two positions
The Hanafi school holds that yamin is a sabab majazi (metaphorical cause). Imam al-Shafi'i holds that it is sabab fi ma'na al-illa (a cause in the meaning of an effective cause).
Memorize these classifications.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof (dalil)
The key proof: 'al-yamin shuri'at li al-birr' (the oath was legislated for righteousness). Therefore, the penalty (jaza) is secondary, only occurring upon breaking (hanth). This makes it a metaphorical cause, not a real one.
Note the focus on purpose (maqsad) as a determinant.
4
Examine the tanjiz example
The text uses the example of tanjiz (immediate execution) vs. ta'liq (suspension). Hanafis say that an immediate divorce nullifies a suspended divorce because the locus (mahall) is lost. The metaphorical cause only 'exists' as long as the mahall exists.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence).
5
Distinguish from the ownership condition
The text contrasts with a case where divorce is conditioned on ownership. That condition acts like a real illa, so it can be valid even without a current mahall (e.g., a triply divorced wife). This shows the limit of the sabab majazi concept.
Important nuance: not all suspensive conditions are metaphorical.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالشَّافِعِي عَلَى جَعَلَهُ سَبَبًا هُوَ فِي مَعْنَى الْعِلَّةِ وَعِنْدَنَا لِهَذَا الْمَجَازِ شُبْهَةُ الْحَقِيقَةِ حُكْمًا خِلَافًا لِلزُفَرِ وَيَتَبَيَّنُ ذَلِكَ فِي مَسْأَلَةِ التَّنْجِيزِ هَلْ يُبْطِلُ التَّعْلِيقَ فَعِنْدَنَا يُبْطِلُهُ لِأَنَّ الْيَمِينَ شُرِعَتْ لِلْبِرِّ فَلَمْ يَكُنْ [بُدٌّ؟] مِنْ أَنْ يَصِيرَ الْبِرُّ مَضْمُونًا بِالْجَزَاءِ وَإِذَا صَارَ الْبِرُّ مَضْمُونًا بِالْجَزَاءِ صَارَ لِمَا ضُمِّنَ بِهِ الْبِرُّ لِلْحَالِ شُبْهَةُ الْوُجُوبِ كَالْمَغْصُوبِ مَضْمُونٌ بِقِيمَتِهِ فَيَكُونُ لِلْغَصَبِ حَالَ قِيَامِ الْعَيْنِ شُبْهَةُ إِيجَابِ الْقِيمَةِ وَإِذَا كَانَ كَذَلِكَ لَمْ تَبْقَ الشُّبْهَةُ إِلَّا فِي مَحَلِّهِ كَالْحَقِيقَةِ لَا تَسْتَغْنِي عَنِ الْمَحَلِّ فَإِذَا فَاتَ الْمَحَلُّ بَطَلَ بِخِلَافِ تَعْلِيقِ الطَّلَاقِ بِالْمِلْكِ فَإِنَّهُ يَصِحُّ فِي مُطَلَّقَةِ الثَّلَاثِ وَإِنْ عُدِمَ الْمَحَلُّ لِأَنَّ ذَلِكَ الشَّرْطَ فِي حُكْمِ الْعِلَلِ فَصَارَ ذَلِكَ مُعَارِضًا لِهَذِهِ الشُّبْهَةِ السَّابِقَةِ عَلَيْهِ
And al-Shafi'i made it a cause that is in the meaning of the effective cause (illa), and according to us, this metaphorical (majaz) has the doubt (shubha) of the real (haqiqah) in terms of ruling, contrary to al-Zufar. And that becomes apparent in the issue of immediate execution (tanjiz): does it nullify the suspension (ta'liq)? According to us, it nullifies it, because the oath (yamin) was legislated for righteousness (birr). It was inevitable that righteousness becomes guaranteed (madmun) by the consequence (jaza). And when righteousness becomes guaranteed by the consequence, there arises for that which guarantees righteousness an immediate doubt of obligation (shubhat al-wujub), like the usurped object (maghsab) is guaranteed by its value, so for the usurpation (ghasb) while the object exists, there is a doubt of obligation of the value (shubhat ijab al-qimah). And when it is so, the doubt remains only in its locus (mahall), like the real (haqiqah) does not dispense with the locus. So when the locus is lost, the suspension becomes void. Unlike the suspension of divorce on ownership, for it is valid in the case of a woman triply divorced even if the locus is absent, because that condition is in the status of effective causes (ilal). So that becomes opposed to this preceding doubt.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the nature of oaths (yamin) and suspensive conditions (ta'liq) as causes (asbab) in Islamic law. The Hanafi position, as stated, is that an oath is a metaphorical cause (sabab majazi), not a real cause (sabab haqiqi) nor a cause in the sense of an effective cause (sabab fi ma'na al-illa). The reason is that oaths are legislated to encourage fulfilling the oath (birr), not to cause the penalty (jaza). The penalty only arises when one breaks the oath (hanth), which is the opposite of what the oath intends. Therefore, the oath only leads to the penalty indirectly, through a ma'al (ultimate outcome) consideration, which makes it a metaphorical cause. Imam al-Shafi'i, however, considers the oath a cause that is in the meaning of an effective cause (fi ma'na al-illa), meaning it directly brings about the ruling. The difference has practical consequences, as illustrated in the issue of tanjiz (immediate execution) vs. ta'liq. For example, if someone says 'If I enter the house, my wife is divorced' and then immediately says 'I divorce you', does the immediate divorce nullify the suspended one? According to the Hanafis, it does, because the oath (which is the suspensive condition) is only a metaphorical cause and its locus (mahall) is the actual divorce. Once an immediate divorce occurs, the locus for the suspended clause is lost, so it becomes void. The Shafi'is disagree, because they see the oath as akin to a real cause. Imam Zufar within the Hanafi school also holds a different opinion. The passage further explains that the doubt (shubhah) of the real cause exists in the metaphor, similar to how a usurped object creates a doubt of obligation of its value even while the object exists. So the suspended oath has a momentary effect until the locus is lost. Then the analogy of suspending divorce on ownership is mentioned: if a man says to his triply divorced wife 'If you own property, you are divorced' and she later owns, it is valid even if at the time of suspension she was not owned (since ownership of self is impossible). This is because the condition (marriage) is like an effective cause, and it overrides the doubt about the locus.

Key Terms
سَبَب مَجَازِي (sabab majāzī): A metaphorical cause that leads to a ruling indirectly via ultimate outcome, not directly.
سَبَب فِي مَعْنَى الْعِلَّة (sabab fī ma‘nā al-‘illah): A cause that is in the meaning of an effective cause, directly bringing about the ruling.
يَمِين (yamīn): An oath sworn by God, legislated to encourage righteousness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is an oath (yamin) considered a sabab majazi rather than a sabab fi ma'na al-illa?
A) Because the oath always leads to the penalty directly.
B) Because the oath was legislated for righteousness, and the penalty only occurs if it is broken.
C) Because the oath is like an effective cause in all respects.
D) Because the Hanafis do not recognize metaphorical causes.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school classifies an oath as a metaphorical cause (sabab majazi) because it is legislated for righteousness, and its penal effect is only a secondary consequence dependent on the existence of a proper locus.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

Yamin and Ta'liq: Are They Sabab, Illa, or Sabab fihi Ma'na al-Illa?
Dispute on the causal nature of oath and suspension

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between sabab, illa, and sabab fihi ma'na al-illa, and apply the Hanafi classification to determine the validity of conditional divorce when the subject is removed.

Core Idea
An oath is not a pure cause nor an efficient cause, but a cause with the meaning of efficacy — sabab fihi ma'na al-illa.

This passage presents a nuanced dispute about the nature of oath and conditional suspension in Hanafi usul. Understanding this classification is crucial for determining legal effects when the subject of the suspension is removed. We will explore three positions and their practical consequences, focusing on the Hanafi middle path.

Guided Path
1
Identify the object of dispute
What legal entities are being classified? Yamin (oath) and ta'liq (conditional suspension) are under scrutiny. The question is whether they are sabab (cause), illa (efficient cause), or something in between.
Focus on the causal nature, not the rulings themselves.
2
Contrast Shafi'i's view with the Hanafi response
Imam Shafi'i argues that yamin and ta'liq are pure sabab because the consequence (kafarah/divorce) does not occur immediately. The Hanafis respond that they have ta'thir (efficacy) because they make the consequence wajib upon breach/condition, thus they are sabab fihi ma'na al-illa.
The key is whether 'delayed effect' negates causal efficacy.
3
Contrast Zufar's view with the Hanafi view
Both agree they are sabab majazi (metaphorical cause), but Zufar says it is pure metaphor with no resemblance to real causality, while the Hanafis say there is mushahabah (similarity) to real causality.
This difference affects whether a mahall (subject) is required at the time of ta'liq.
4
Analyze the hypothetical case
A husband says 'If you enter the house, you are thrice divorced.' He then gives unconditional triple divorce before the condition. Later, after halala and remarriage, the wife enters the house. Apply the Hanafi position: the unconditional divorce removed the mahall, so the suspension is void.
Compare with Zufar's ruling: suspension remains valid.
5
Examine the Hanafi rebuttal of Zufar's analogy
Zufar analogizes to 'in nakhattu fanti taliq' (if I marry you, you are divorced) where no mahall at suspension is needed. The Hanafis distinguish: marriage is illat al-illa (cause of the cause), not a direct sabab like the triple divorce case.
This shows the importance of precise causal classification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفيضُ الحجازي
۳۱۶
شرح اردو المنتخب الحسامي
امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یمین اور تعلیق فی الحال حکم کے لئے یعنی کفارہ اور جزا کا صرف سبب ہیں ، علت نہیں ہیں، کیونکہ اگر علت ہوتے تو یمین یعنی قسم کھاتے ہی کفارہ واجب ہو جاتا ، اور تعلیق کرتے ہی جزا مرتب ہو جاتی ، حالانکہ کفارہ اور جزا حانث ہونے اور شرط کے پائے جانے تک مؤخر ہیں، معلوم ہوا کہ یمین اور تعلیق علت نہیں ، صرف سبب ہیں کیونکہ یمین کفارہ کی طرف مفضی ہے اور تعلیق جزا یعنی حکم کی طرف مفضی ہے، تو صرف سبب بنے مگر چونکہ یمین حنث کے وقت کفارہ کو واجب کرتی ہے اور تعلیق وجود شرط کے وقت حکم یعنی جزا کو واجب کرتی ہے ، تو یمین کا موجب کفارہ ہونا اور تعلیق کا موجب جزا ہونا یہ علامت ہے علت ہونے کی ، کیونکہ علت اس کو کہتے ہیں جس کی حکم میں تاثیر ہوتی ہے، اور یہاں یمین مؤثر ہے وجوب کفارہ میں اور تعلیق مؤثر ہے وجوب جزا میں ، لہذا یمین اور تعلیق صرف سبب نہیں ہوئے بلکہ سبب فیہ معنی العلۃ ہوئے۔ یہاں تک تو ہمارے اور امام شافعی اللہ کے درمیان اختلاف بیان ہوا، آگے ہمارے اور امام زفر کے درمیان اختلاف بیان کر رہے ہیں ، ہمارے اور امام زفر کے درمیان یہاں تک تو اتفاق ہے کہ یمین اور تعلیق سبب مجازی ہیں ،علی العلی یعنی سبب فیہ معنی العلہ نہیں ہیں، البتہ پھر اس میں اختلاف ہے کہ سبب مجازی کس نوعیت کا ہے۔؟ امام زفر اللہ فرماتے ہیں کہ سبب محض ہیں ، اور ہم کہتے ہیں کہ یمین و تعلیق سبیت میں مجاز محض نہیں ہیں، بلکہ ان میں حقیقت سبیت کے ساتھ مشابہت ہے، تو امام شافعی کے مذہب میں افراط ہے، امام زفر کے مذہب میں تفریط ہے کہ انہوں نے اس کو سبیت سے ہی خارج کر دیا ، اور فرمایا کہ مجازاً اس کو سبب کہا گیا ہے اور ہمارا مذہب دونوں کے درمیان ہے۔
ويتبين ذلك : - ہمارے اور امام زفر اللہ کے درمیان ثمره اختلاف اس صورت میں ظاہر ہوگا کہ کسی نے اپنی بیوی کو اس طرح طلاق دی ان دخلت الدار فانت طالق ثلاثاً ، یعنی تین طلاقوں کو دخول دار کے ساتھ معلق کیا ، پھر وجود شرط سے پہلے شوہر نے منجز تین طلاقیں دیدی، بیوی عدت پوری کر کے حلالہ کر کے پھر زوج اول کے نکاح میں آگئی ، پھر دخول دار کی شرط پائی گئی تو کیا پہلے نکاح والی تعلیق سے طلاق پڑے گی یا وہ تعلیق باطل ہوگئی ؟۔ ہمارے نزدیک تنخیز اطلاق کی وجہ سے تعلیق باطل ہوگئی ، لہذا اب شرط پائے جانے پر طلاق واقع نہ ہوگی ،اور امام زفر اللہ فرماتے ہیں کہ تعلیق باطل نہ ہوگی، بلکہ وجود شرط کے وقت تعلیق سابق کی وجہ سے طلاق پڑے گی۔ ان کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ انت طالق ثلاثا تعلیق کے وقت محض مجاز اسبب ہے، حقیقت کا کوئی شبہ نہیں ہے، لہذا انت طالق “ جب حقیقة سبب نہیں ہے تو اس کے لئے ابھی محل کی بھی ضرورت نہیں ہے محل کی ضرورت پڑے گی وجود شرط کے وقت ، پس تنخجیز اطلاق سے جب محل زائل ہو گیا ، تو اس کی وجہ سے سابقہ تعلیق باطل نہ ہوگی۔ پھر جب وہ عورت دوبارہ عدت گزار کر حلالہ کر کے زوج اول کے نکاح میں آگئی اور دخول دار پایا گیا تو وجود شرط کے وقت محل یدار موجود ہے، لہذا سابقہ تعلیق سے طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی، یہ مسئلہ بالکل ایسا ہی ہے جیسے جب کسی نے اجنبیہ سے کہا ان نكحتك فانت طالق ، یہاں تعلیق کی ابتدا ہی میں محل نہیں ہے، اس کے باوجود تعلیق باطل نہیں ہوتی بلکہ جب شرط پائی جائے گی تو بالا تفاق طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی ، اس طرح زیر بحث مسئلہ میں بھی درمیان میں محل فوت ہونے سے تعلیق باطل نہ ہوگی ، یہ تو امام زفر اس کی دلیل ہوئی۔
فنعد نایبطله : - ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ یمین اور تعلیق پر یعنی اس کو پورا کرنے کے لئے مشروع ہوا ہے یعنی کسی کام کے کرنے کی قسم کھائی تو اس کو کرے اور نہ کرنے کی قسم کھائی تو نہ کرے، اسی طرح تعلیق میں بھی منشاء یہی ہے کہ جس چیز پر طلاق و عتاق کو معلق کیا گیا ہے وہ کام نہ کیا جائے ، جیسے اگر تو گھر میں داخل ہوئی تو تجھے تین طلاق ، کہنے والے کا منشا یہ ہے کہ عورت گھر میں داخل نہ ہو، بہر حال یمین اور تعلیق پر کے لئے مشروع ہوئے ہیں ، اب اگر بر فوت ہو گیا تو اس کی وجہ سے جزا لازم ہوگی یعنی یمین کی صورت میں جزا، پس جب فوات پر مضمون بالجزاء ہے، یعنی پر فوت ہونے سے جزا کا ضمان آتا ہے تو جزاء کے لئے فی الحال ثابت ہونے کا شبہ پیدا ہو گیا ، کیونکہ ضمان اصلِ شی کی طرح موجود مانا جاتا ہے ، پس یہاں یمین اور تعلیق سے اصل مقصود پر ہے، اور فوات پر کی صورت میں ضمان یعنی کفارہ اور جزاء لازم ہے تو ضمان بھی پڑ کی طرح موجود ہو گا اس کی مثال ایسی ہے جیسے مال مغصوب میں اصل حکم تو یہ ہے کہ عین مال واپس کیا جائے ، پھر اس کے ہلاک ہونے کی صورت میں قیمت یا مثل سے ضمان واجب ہے لیکن عین مغصوب کے ہوتے ہوئے بھی قیمت واجب کرنے کا شبہ ہے، اسی لئے عین مغصوب کی موجودگی میں اس کی قیمت معاف کر دی گئی ، تو عین مغصوب کو لوٹانا واجب نہیں ہے، اسی طرح دوسرے آدمی کا غاصب کی طرف کو سے قیمت کی ذمہ داری لینا درست ہے، معلوم ہوا جو چیز منمان بنتی ہے اس میں اصل کے مانند موجود ہونے کا شبہ رہتا ہے، اسی طرح ہم کہتے ہیں کہ تعلیق طلاق کا ایسا سبب مجازی ہے جو حقیقت سبب کے مشابہ ہے، لہذا حقیقتہ سبب ہونے کی صورت میں جیسے محل کا ہونا ضروری ہے جیسے انت طالق کہا تو یہ طلاق کا سبب حقیقی ہے، اس کے لئے محل کا ہونا ضروری ہے، ایسے ہی سبب مجازی ہونے کی صورت میں بھی محل کا ہونا ضروری ہے کیونکہ اس کو حقیقت سبب کے ساتھ مشابہت ہے، اور جب طلاق منجز سے محل فوت ہو گیا تو تعلیق باطل ہو جائے گی۔
66
بخلاف تعليق الطلاق بالملک - - امام زفر اللہ کے قیاس کا جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ ان نکحتک فانت طالق “ پر قیاس درست نہیں ہے ، اس لئے کہ اس میں نکاح حقیقتہ طلاق کا سبب نہیں ہے، بلکہ علت العلہ ہے، اس طرح کہ نکاح ملک کی علت ہے، اور ملک طلاق کی علت ہے، تو نکاح طلاق کے لئے علت العلة
Al-Faiz al-Hijazi 316. Urdu commentary of al-Muntakhab al-Husami. Imam Shafi'i's proof is that oath (yamin) and conditional suspension (ta'liq) are only causes (sabab) for the ruling in the immediate sense, i.e., for expiation and penalty; they are not the efficient cause (illa). Because if they were the illa, then upon swearing the oath, expiation would become obligatory immediately, and upon making the suspension, the penalty would attach immediately. However, expiation and penalty are deferred until the occurrence of breaking the oath and the fulfillment of the condition. Hence, it became known that oath and suspension are not illa, only sabab, because the oath leads to expiation and the suspension leads to the penalty (i.e., the ruling). So they are merely sabab. But since the oath makes expiation obligatory at the time of breaking, and the suspension makes the ruling (i.e., penalty) obligatory at the time of the condition's occurrence, then the fact that the oath is the cause (mujib) of expiation and the suspension is the cause of penalty is a sign of being illa, because illa is that which has efficacy (ta'thir) in the ruling. And here the oath is effective in the obligation of expiation, and the suspension is effective in the obligation of penalty. Therefore, oath and suspension are not merely sabab, but rather sabab fihi ma'na al-illa (a cause having the meaning of the efficient cause). Up to here the disagreement between us and Imam Shafi'i has been explained. Next, we are explaining the disagreement between us and Imam Zufar. Between us and Imam Zufar there is an agreement up to here that oath and suspension are metaphorical causes (sabab majazi), 'ala al-'ali, meaning they are not sabab fihi ma'na al-illa. However, then there is disagreement as to what type of metaphorical cause they are. Imam Zufar says they are mere causes (sabab mahd), and we say that oath and suspension are not pure metaphor in causality; rather they have similarity to real causality. So in Imam Shafi'i's school there is excess (ifrat), and in Imam Zufar's school there is deficiency (tafrit) because he excluded them from causality altogether and said they are called cause metaphorically. Our school is between the two. And that becomes evident: The practical difference (thamarah) between us and Imam Zufar appears in a case where a man divorces his wife by saying: 'If you enter the house, you are thrice divorced'—i.e., he suspends three divorces on entering the house. Then before the condition occurs, the husband gives three unconditional divorces. The wife completes her waiting period, marries another (halala), and then remarries the first husband. Then the condition of entering the house occurs. Will the divorce fall from the earlier suspension, or will that suspension become void? In our view, due to the unconditional divorce, the suspension becomes void, so now upon the occurrence of the condition, divorce will not occur. Imam Zufar says the suspension does not become void; rather, at the time of the condition's occurrence, divorce will occur due to the previous suspension. His proof is that at the time of the suspension 'You are thrice divorced' it is a mere metaphorical cause; there is no suspicion of reality. So when 'You are divorced' is not a real cause, it does not require a subject (mahall) at that time; the subject will be needed at the time of the condition's occurrence. Then when the unconditional divorce removed the subject, the previous suspension does not become void due to that. Then when the woman again completes the waiting period, does halala, and enters the first husband's marriage, and the condition of entering the house occurs, then at the time of the condition's occurrence the subject is present, so divorce occurs from the previous suspension. This case is exactly like when someone says to a non-marriageable woman (ajnabiyya): 'If I marry you, you are divorced.' Here, at the beginning of the suspension, there is no subject, yet the suspension is not void; rather, when the condition occurs, by consensus divorce will occur. Similarly, in the case under discussion, the subject being lost in between does not void the suspension. That is Imam Zufar's proof. Then our proof: Oath and suspension are legislated for the purpose of fulfilling the oath (birr), meaning if one swears to do something, he should do it, and if swears not to do something, he should not do it. Similarly, in suspension, the intention is that the thing on which divorce or freeing is suspended should not be done. For example, if one says 'If you enter the house, you are thrice divorced,' the speaker's intention is that the woman should not enter the house. In any case, oath and suspension are legislated for birr. Now if birr is lost (i.e., the oath is broken), then the penalty becomes necessary, i.e., in the case of oath, expiation. So when the consequence of birr being lost is that one is liable for the penalty, then for the penalty there arises a semblance (shubhah) of being established at the present moment, because liability (daman) is considered like the existence of the original thing. So here the intended original from oath and suspension is birr, and when birr is lost, the liability (daman) of expiation and penalty becomes necessary, so the liability will be like birr existing. An example is usurped property (mal maghsab): the original ruling is that the specific object ('ayn) should be returned; then in case of its destruction, the liability (daman) of its value or equivalent is obligatory. But while the specific usurped object is still present, there is a semblance of making the value obligatory. For this reason, during the existence of the specific usurped object, its value is waived, so returning the specific object is not obligatory? Similarly, it is valid for another person to take on the liability of the value from the usurper. So it is learned that whatever is a substitute (badal) has the semblance of being present like the original. Similarly, we say that the suspension of divorce is such a metaphorical cause that resembles the real cause. Therefore, just as in the case of being a real cause, the presence of a subject is necessary—for example, when one says 'You are divorced,' it is a real cause of divorce, and it requires a subject—similarly, in the case of being a metaphorical cause, the presence of a subject is also necessary because it has similarity to the real cause. And when the subject is lost due to unconditional divorce, the suspension becomes void. 66. Opposite of suspension of divorce on ownership (ta'liq al-talaq bil-milk) – responding to Imam Zufar's analogy (qiyas): the analogy with 'If I marry you, you are divorced' is not correct because in that case marriage is not really a cause of divorce; rather it is the cause of the cause (illat al-illa), such that marriage is the cause of ownership (milk), and ownership is the cause of divorce. So marriage is the cause of the cause for divorce.
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage presents a three-way dispute on the nature of oath (yamin) and conditional suspension (ta'liq) in Hanafi usul. The passage first contrasts the Hanafi position with Imam Shafi'i: Shafi'i argues that oath and suspension are mere sabab (causes) for expiation and divorce, not 'illa (efficient causes), because the consequences do not arise immediately. The Hanafi scholars respond that while they cause the consequence only upon breach or condition, they have efficacy (ta'thir) in making the consequence wajib, so they are 'sabab fihi ma'na al-illa'—causes that contain the meaning of efficient cause. Then the passage compares the Hanafi view with Imam Zufar: both agree they are metaphorical causes (sabab majazi) not real causes, but Zufar says they are pure metaphor with no resemblance to real causality, while the Hanafis say they bear similarity (mushabahah) to real causality. The practical difference appears in a specific scenario: a man suspends triple divorce on his wife's entry into the house, then gives unconditional triple divorce before the condition, and later after halala and remarriage, the condition occurs. The Hanafis rule the suspension void because the unconditional divorce removed the subject (mahall) of the marriage, which was necessary for the suspension to be effective even as a metaphorical cause. Zufar rules the suspension remains valid, analogizing to the case of suspending divorce on a future marriage (in nakhattu fanti taliq), where there is no subject at suspension but the condition later validates it. The Hanafi response distinguishes: in the marriage case, marriage is not the direct cause but the cause of the cause (illat al-illa), whereas in the triple divorce case, the subject existed at the time of suspension and was removed by the unconditional divorce. The Hanafis also use an analogy with usurped property: just as liability (daman) for the value is treated as a substitute for the original and has a semblance of being present like the original, so too the penalty (kafarah or divorce) as a substitute for the violated oath has a semblance of present effect. Thus, the requirement of a subject at the time of the conditional suspension is maintained. The Hanafi position is presented as the middle path between Shafi'i's excess (considering them real causes in all respects) and Zufar's deficiency (denying any causality).

Key Terms
سبب (sabab): A cause that leads to a ruling but does not have immediate efficacy; it merely provides the occasion for the ruling to attach upon fulfillment of a condition.
علة (illa): The efficient cause that directly and immediately produces the ruling.
سبب فیہ معنی العلۃ (sabab fihi ma'na al-illa): A cause that, while not producing the ruling immediately, has within it the meaning of efficacy (ta'thir) such that it is treated as an illa for certain legal purposes, e.g., requiring a mahall at the time of ta'liq.
مانع (mani'): A preventer that blocks the operation of the cause; here the unconditional divorce acts as a mani' by removing the subject.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, why does the conditional suspension become void when the husband gives unconditional triple divorce before the condition occurs?
A) Because the unconditional divorce is a stronger cause that overrides the weaker conditional one.
B) Because the unconditional divorce removes the mahall (subject) which is required at the time of ta'liq due to the nature of the cause as sabab fihi ma'na al-illa.
C) Because the unconditional divorce changes the intention of the husband, voiding the original suspension.
D) Because the wife's halala and remarriage automatically cancel all previous conditional divorces.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi classification of yamin and ta'liq as 'sabab fihi ma'na al-illa' requires that the subject (mahall) be present at the time of the conditional pronouncement, leading to the suspension becoming void if the subject is removed before the condition occurs.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
advanced
10 min
Ta'liq al-Talaq: Hanafi Rebuttal of Imam Zufar's Qiyas
Hanafi usul dispute on conditional talaq causation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi distinction between ta'liq bi al-shart and ta'liq bi al-milk to evaluate the validity of conditional talaq when the mahall is lost.

Core Idea
A conditional talaq requires the mahall at the time of ta'liq; loss of mahall voids the ta'liq, unlike conditional talaq on ownership.

This lesson delves into a classic usul dispute within the Hanafi school. Imam Zufar, a prominent disciple, argued that a conditional talaq (ta'liq bi al-shart) remains valid even if the marital bond (mahall) is lost before the condition occurs, analogizing it to ta'liq bi al-milk. The Hanafi majority refutes this, demonstrating that the two types of ta'liq operate on different causal structures. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly deriving rulings in conditional divorce cases.

Guided Path
1
Frame the dispute
Identify the contested ruling: does a conditional talaq (ta'liq bi al-shart) become invalid if the mahall (marriage) is destroyed (e.g., by three divorces) before the condition occurs? State both Hanafi and Imam Zufar's views.
Imam Zufar is a Hanafi, so this is intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.
2
Examine Imam Zufar's qiyas
Imam Zufar analogizes to 'in nakahtuki fa-anti taliq' where the mahall does not exist initially but ta'liq is valid. Understand his reasoning: if ta'liq can start without mahall, it can survive temporary loss.
This is a qiyas based on ta'liq bi al-milk.
3
Trace the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafi majority distinguishes the causal roles: in ta'liq bi al-shart, the condition is a metaphorical cause (sabab majazi) that resembles a real cause, requiring mahall at the outset. In ta'liq bi al-milk, marriage is a cause of cause (illat al-illa), so mahall is not initially needed.
The key usul concept: sabab vs illat al-illa.
4
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
Given a scenario: a husband says 'if you enter the house, you are divorced', then divorces her three times. She later enters. Imam Zufar says talaq occurs; Hanafi majority says no. Confirm the Hanafi ruling with the causal analysis.
The practical consequence hinges on whether the ta'liq is bi al-shart or bi al-milk.

الفيضُ الحجازي ۳۱۷ شرح اردو المنتخب الحسامي ،، ۔ عورت دوبارہ عدت گزار کر حلالہ کر کے زوج اول کے نکاح میں آگئی اور دخول دار پایا گیا تو وجود شرط کے وقت محل یدار موجود ہے، لہذا سابقہ تعلیق سے طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی، یہ مسئلہ بالکل ایسا ہی ہے جیسے جب کسی نے اجنبیہ سے کہا ان نكحتك فانت طالق ، یہاں تعلیق کی ابتدا ہی میں محل نہیں ہے، اس کے باوجود تعلیق باطل نہیں ہوتی بلکہ جب شرط پائی جائے گی تو بالا تفاق طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی ، اس طرح زیر بحث مسئلہ میں بھی درمیان میں محل فوت ہونے سے تعلیق باطل نہ ہوگی ، یہ تو امام زفر اس کی دلیل ہوئی۔ فنعد نبطله : - - امام زفر اللہ کے قیاس کا جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ ان نکحتک فانت طالق “ پر قیاس درست نہیں ہے ، اس لئے کہ اس میں نکاح حقیقتہ طلاق کا سبب نہیں ہے، بلکہ علت العلہ ہے، اس طرح کہ نکاح ملک کی علت ہے، اور ملک طلاق کی علت ہے، تو نکاح طلاق کے لئے علت العلة ہوا ، اور علت العلۃ علت کے حکم میں ہوتا ہے، اور علت کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ حکم ( طلاق ) معدوم ہو اس لئے کہ نکاح نہیں ہے جو علت ہے تو حکم بھی نہ ہوگا کیونکہ حکم علت سے پہلے موجود نہیں ہوتا ، اور جب حکم معدوم ہے تو یہ عدم حمل کا تقاضا کرتا ہے، اور چونکہ یہ تعلیق ہے اس لئے اس کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ سبب مجازی ہو جس کو سبب حقیقی کے ساتھ مشابہت ہے، تو اس کا تقاضہ یہ ہے کہ محل باقی ہو تو علت کا تقاضہ سبب مجازی ( جو مشابہ حقیقت ہے ) کے تقاضے سے معارض ہوا ، اس طرح کہ شرط ( ان نکحت ) کا علت کے حکم میں ہونا عد م محمل کا تقاضا کرتا ہے، اور سبب مجازی میں جو شبہ محقق شرط سے پہلے ہے یعنی تحقق شرط سے پہلے ثبوت سبیت ، اس کا تقاضا ہے کہ محل موجود ہو، جب دونوں کے تقاضوں میں تعارض ہو گیا ، تو شبہ حقیقت کا اعتبار ساقط ہو جائے گا اور وجود محل کی شرط نہ ہوگی، اور تعلیق علی حالہ باقی رہے گی ، پھر جب شرط (نکاح) پائی جائے گی تو طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی، خلاصہ یہ کہ امام زفر کا زیر بحث مسئلہ کو ان نكحتك فانت طالق “ پر قیاس کرنا درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہ سبب کو علت پر قیاس کرنا ہے۔ برخلاف تعلیق بالشرط کے کہ وہ حقیقی سبب کے مشابہ ہونے کی وجہ سے محل کا تقاضہ کرتی ہے، اور تعلیق کے بعد تخیز تین طلاقیں دے دی تو محل فوت ہو گیا اور محل کے فوت ہونے سے تعلیق ہی باطل ہو جائے گی ، لہذا امام زفر کا تعلیق بالشرط کا تعلیق بالملک پر قیاس درست نہیں ، دونوں میں بہت بڑا فرق ہے۔
Al-Fayd al-Hijazi 317 Sharh Urdu al-Muntakhab al-Husami. A woman, after completing her waiting period and performing halalah, came back into the marriage of her first husband, and intercourse was found, so at the time of the condition's existence, the locus (mahall) exists. Therefore, the talaq will occur by the previous ta'liq. This issue is exactly like when someone said to a foreign woman 'If I marry you, you are divorced'. Here, at the beginning of the ta'liq, there is no mahall, yet the ta'liq is not invalid; rather, when the condition occurs, talaq will occur by agreement. Similarly, in the issue under discussion, the loss of mahall in the interim will not invalidate the ta'liq. This is Imam Zufar's proof. Then we argue to nullify it: Our proof is that yamin and ta'liq were legislated for fulfillment of actions. If one swears to do something, he should do it; if he swears not to do something, he should not do it. Similarly, in ta'liq, the intention is that the thing on which talaq or manumission is suspended should not be done. For example, if one says 'If you enter the house, you have triple divorce', the speaker intends that the woman should not enter the house. In any case, yamin and ta'liq were legislated for fulfillment. Now, if the action (bar) is missed, then a penalty (jaza) becomes necessary, i.e., in the case of yamin, the penalty. So, since the consequence (jaza) is attached to missing the action, then when the action is missed, a guarantee of the consequence comes. Then there arises a doubt about the immediate establishment of the consequence, because a guarantee is considered to exist like the original thing. So here, from yamin and ta'liq, the original intention is about fulfillment, and in case of missing the action, the guarantee (i.e., expiation or penalty) becomes necessary. So the guarantee will exist like the action. An example of this is in the case of usurped property: the original ruling is that the specific property must be returned. Then, if it is destroyed, the guarantee of value or similar is obligatory. But there is a doubt about obligating the value while the specific property exists, so the value is waived while the specific property exists. It is not obligatory to return the specific property. Similarly, it is valid for another person to take responsibility for the value from the usurper. It is known that what becomes a substitute has a doubt of existing like the original. Similarly, we say that ta'liq of talaq is such a metaphorical cause (sabab majazi) that resembles a real cause. Therefore, in the case of being a real cause, the existence of the mahall is necessary, like when one says 'you are divorced', that is a real cause of talaq, and for it the mahall is necessary. Similarly, in the case of a metaphorical cause, the existence of the mahall is also necessary because it resembles the real cause. And when by an immediate talaq the mahall is lost, then the ta'liq will become invalid. 66 Contrary to ta'liq of talaq by ownership (ta'liq bi al-milk) — Imam Zufar is responding to the qiyas: the analogy to 'if I marry you, you are divorced' is not correct, because in that, marriage is not the real cause (sabab haqiqi) of talaq; rather, it is the cause of the cause (illat al-illa). That is, marriage is the cause of ownership, and ownership is the cause of talaq. So marriage is the cause of the cause for talaq. And a cause of the cause is in the ruling of a cause. The requirement of a cause is that the ruling (talaq) is non-existent because the marriage, which is the cause, does not exist. So the ruling will also not exist because the ruling does not exist before the cause. And when the ruling is non-existent, it requires the non-existence of the mahall. And since this is ta'liq, its requirement is that it is a metaphorical cause that resembles a real cause. Its requirement is that the mahall remains. So the requirement of the cause (illat) conflicted with the requirement of the metaphorical cause (which resembles a real cause). That is, the condition (if I marry) being in the ruling of a cause requires non-existence of the mahall, and in the metaphorical cause, there is a doubt before the realization of the condition, i.e., before the condition's realization, the existence of the cause is doubtful. Its requirement is that the mahall exists. When the two requirements conflicted, the consideration of the real (doubt) falls, and the condition of existence of mahall is not required, and the ta'liq remains as is. Then, when the condition (marriage) occurs, talaq will occur. Summary: Imam Zufar's analogy of the issue under discussion to 'if I marry you, you are divorced' is not correct because it is an analogy of a cause to a cause-of-cause. Contrary to ta'liq by condition (ta'liq bi al-shart), which, due to resembling a real cause, requires the mahall. And after ta'liq, if the husband gave three divorces, the mahall is lost, and by the loss of mahall, the ta'liq itself becomes invalid. Therefore, Imam Zufar's analogy of ta'liq bi al-shart to ta'liq bi al-milk is not correct; there is a great difference between the two.
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage presents a Hanafi usul al-fiqh dispute on conditional talaq. The issue is whether a conditional pronouncement of talaq (ta'liq bi al-shart) remains valid if the mahall (the marital bond) is lost before the condition occurs. Imam Zufar, a leading Hanafi disciple, analogizes to the case of 'in nakahtuki fa-anti taliq' (If I marry you, you are divorced), where the mahall (marriage) does not exist at the time of pronouncement but talaq occurs upon marriage. He argues that similarly, even if the mahall is temporarily lost, the ta'liq revives upon its return. The Hanafi majority rebuts: (1) Ta'liq is like an oath (yamin) meant to ensure or prevent an action; if the mahall is lost, the ta'liq becomes frustrated. (2) The analogy fails because in 'in nakahtuki', marriage is not a direct cause (sabab) of talaq but a cause of cause (illat al-illa). In ta'liq bi al-shart, the condition is a metaphorical cause resembling a real cause, so the mahall must exist at the time of ta'liq. If the mahall is later destroyed (e.g., by three divorces), the ta'liq is void. This preserves the distinction between direct and metaphorical causes.

Key Terms
تعلیق بالشرط (ta'liq bi al-shart): A conditional pronouncement of talaq where the condition is an event (e.g., entry into the house). The ta'liq resembles a real cause.
تعلیق بالملک (ta'liq bi al-milk): A ta'liq where the condition is ownership, e.g., 'if I marry you'. Here marriage is a cause of cause, not a direct cause.
سبب مجازی (sabab majazi): A metaphorical cause that resembles a real cause in ta'liq.
علت العلۃ (illat al-illa): The cause of the cause, e.g., marriage is the cause of ownership, which is the cause of talaq.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man says to his wife 'If you enter the house, you are divorced' and then gives her three divorces, and later she enters the house, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) Talaq occurs because the condition was fulfilled.
B) Talaq does not occur because the mahall was lost.
C) Talaq occurs only if she remarries him first.
D) Talaq occurs but is suspended until the end of the waiting period.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi distinction between ta'liq bi al-shart and ta'liq bi al-milk rests on whether the condition is a direct cause or a cause of cause; the former requires mahall, the latter does not.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
advanced
8 min
Refutation of Imam Zufar's Analogy on Conditional Divorce
Refuting Imam Zufar's analogy between conditional divorce and property-based divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi majority rejects Imam Zufar's analogy between conditional divorce (ta'liq al-talaq bi al-shart) and conditional ownership (ta'liq al-milk), and distinguish between a metaphorical cause (sabab majazi) and a real cause (sabab haqiqi) in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Conditional divorce needs the subject to exist; conditional ownership does not — a key distinction that invalidates the analogy.

In this lesson, we examine an intra-Hanafi usul dispute: Imam Zufar's attempt to analogize conditional divorce to conditional ownership. The majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) reject this qiyas because the two involve different types of causes. By understanding the distinction between a real cause (sabab haqiqi) and a metaphorical cause (sabab majazi), you will grasp a fundamental principle in Hanafi usul that governs the validity of analogies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the analogy
State the analogy Imam Zufar proposes: conditional divorce (e.g., 'If you marry, you are divorced') is similar to conditional ownership (e.g., 'If you buy, you own'). He argues that once the condition is met, the ruling applies regardless of prior dissolution of the subject.
2
Distinguish the causes
In Hanafi usul, a real cause (sabab haqiqi) directly produces the ruling without requiring subject continuity. A metaphorical cause (sabab majazi) resembles a real cause but requires the subject (mahall) to remain at the time of condition fulfillment. Classify each: ownership condition uses a real cause; divorce condition uses a metaphorical cause.
The passage uses 'علت' for cause and 'سبب مجازی' for metaphorical cause.
3
Apply the principle of subject continuity
A metaphorical cause demands that the subject exist when the condition occurs. If the subject (marriage) is already extinguished before the condition is fulfilled, the conditional clause becomes void. The ruling (divorce) cannot arise because its basis is gone.
4
Evaluate the analogy
Since the two causes have different requirements, the analogy fails. The Hanafi majority therefore rules that if a man says 'If you marry, you are divorced' and then divorces his wife, the conditional is void and does not trigger upon remarriage. Imam Zufar's analogy would give a different result but is rejected.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf: the practical difference in legal outcome.

هوا ، اور علت العلۃ علت کے حکم میں ہوتا ہے، اور علت کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ حکم ( طلاق ) معدوم ہو اس لئے کہ نکاح نہیں ہے جو علت ہے تو حکم بھی نہ ہوگا کیونکہ حکم علت سے پہلے موجود نہیں ہوتا ، اور جب حکم معدوم ہے تو یہ عدم حمل کا تقاضا کرتا ہے، اور چونکہ یہ تعلیق ہے اس لئے اس کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ سبب مجازی ہو جس کو سبب حقیقی کے ساتھ مشابہت ہے، تو اس کا تقاضہ یہ ہے کہ محل باقی ہو تو علت کا تقاضہ سبب مجازی ( جو مشابہ حقیقت ہے ) کے تقاضے سے معارض ہوا ، اس طرح کہ شرط ( ان نکحت ) کا علت کے حکم میں ہونا عد م محمل کا تقاضا کرتا ہے، اور سبب مجازی میں جو شبہ محقق شرط سے پہلے ہے یعنی تحقق شرط سے پہلے ثبوت سبیت ، اس کا تقاضا ہے کہ محل موجود ہو، جب دونوں کے تقاضوں میں تعارض ہو گیا ، تو شبہ حقیقت کا اعتبار ساقط ہو جائے گا اور وجود محل کی شرط نہ ہوگی، اور تعلیق علی حالہ باقی رہے گی ، پھر جب شرط (نکاح) پائی جائے گی تو طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی، خلاصہ یہ کہ امام زفر کا زیر بحث مسئلہ کو ان نكحتك فانت طالق “ پر قیاس کرنا درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہ سبب کو علت پر قیاس کرنا ہے۔ برخلاف تعلیق بالشرط کے کہ وہ حقیقی سبب کے مشابہ ہونے کی وجہ سے محل کا تقاضہ کرتی ہے، اور تعلیق کے بعد تخیز تین طلاقیں دے دی تو محل فوت ہو گیا اور محل کے فوت ہونے سے تعلیق ہی باطل ہو جائے گی ، لہذا امام زفر کا تعلیق بالشرط کا تعلیق بالملک پر قیاس درست نہیں ، دونوں میں بہت بڑا فرق ہے۔
It is, and the cause of the cause is in the ruling of the cause, and the requirement of the cause is that the ruling (divorce) be non-existent because there is no marriage which is the cause, so the ruling will also not be because the ruling does not exist before the cause. And when the ruling is non-existent, it requires non-continuation [of subject]. And since this is a conditional (ta'liq), its requirement is that the cause be metaphorical having resemblance to a real cause, so its requirement is that the subject remains. Then the requirement of the cause conflicts with the requirement of the metaphorical cause (which resembles the real). Thus the condition 'if you marry' being in the ruling of the cause requires non-subject, and in the metaphorical cause there is doubt of actualization before the condition, i.e., before actualization of the condition a relation is established; this requires that the subject exist. When the two requirements conflict, the consideration of the similitude of reality falls and the existence of the subject is not a condition, and the conditional remains as it is. Then when the condition (marriage) occurs, divorce will take place. Summary: Imam Zufar's analogy of the issue under discussion to 'If you marry, you are divorced' is incorrect because it is analogy of cause to effect. Contrary to conditional divorce, which because it resembles a real cause requires subject continuity, and after the conditional, if he gives three divorces then the subject is extinguished and with the extinction of the subject the conditional itself becomes void. Therefore, Imam Zufar's analogy of conditional divorce to conditional ownership is not correct; there is a great difference between the two.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute regarding the validity of Imam Zufar's analogy (qiyas) in a case of conditional divorce. Imam Zufar had compared a conditional divorce (e.g., 'If you marry, you are divorced') to a conditional ownership (e.g., 'If you buy, you own') and argued that once the condition is fulfilled, the ruling applies even if the subject (the marriage) was already dissolved. The author rebuts this by clarifying the difference: conditional divorce involves a metaphorical cause (sabab majazi) that requires the subject (the marriage) to remain at the time of condition fulfillment, whereas conditional ownership is a real cause (sabab haqiqi) that does not require pre-existence of the subject. The author shows that the two requirements conflict: the cause (the divorce condition) demands non-existence of the ruling until the condition, while the metaphorical cause demands existence of the subject; when they conflict, the metaphorical aspect falls away and the condition remains operative until the subject later arises. Thus, Imam Zufar's analogy is rejected because it confuses cause with effect.

Key Terms
علت ('illa): That to which the obligation of a ruling is attributed initially.
سبب مجازی (sabab majazi): A metaphorical cause that resembles a real cause but is not intrinsically effective.
تعلیق (ta'liq): Suspension of a ruling upon a future condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the author reject Imam Zufar's analogy between conditional divorce and conditional ownership?
A) Because conditional divorce is a metaphorical cause requiring subject to remain, while conditional ownership is real and does not.
B) Because divorce cannot be conditional.
C) Because Imam Zufar was not a Hanafi scholar.
D) Because the condition in divorce must be past tense.

Key Takeaway
Imam Zufar's analogy is invalid because conditional divorce is a metaphorical cause requiring subject continuity, unlike conditional ownership which is a real cause.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
Imam Muhammad's Dissent on Liability for Opening a Birdcage
Presenting the ikhtilaf between Shaykhayn and Imam Muhammad on a conditional liability case

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi position on liability when a condition precedes a free agent's act, and evaluate the reasoning of Shaykhayn versus Imam Muhammad.

Core Idea
A condition that removes an obstacle does not make one liable if a free agent's voluntary act intervenes.

This passage presents an internal Hanafi dispute on whether opening a birdcage, causing the bird to fly away, creates liability. The majority (Shaykhayn) apply the principle that a condition is distinct from a cause, and since the bird's flight is a voluntary act, the opener is not liable. Imam Muhammad dissents, viewing the flight as generated by the condition. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly attributing liability in cases of indirect causation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Recognize that the core question is whether opening a birdcage makes one liable for the bird's loss.
2
State the Shaykhayn position
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf rule that the opener is not liable because opening the cage is a condition (shart) that removes an obstacle, not a cause that generates the bird's flight. The bird's flight is a voluntary act of a free agent.
3
Address the well analogy
The text anticipates an objection: why is the digger of a well liable? The answer is that falling into a well is typically involuntary, unlike the bird's voluntary flight.
4
State Imam Muhammad's position
Imam Muhammad holds the opener liable because he considers the bird's flight a generated effect of the opening, not a free act; thus the condition has the meaning of a cause.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: in cases where an animal or bird acts voluntarily, Shaykhayn exempt the opener, while Imam Muhammad imposes liability. The relied-upon view is that of Shaykhayn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ابوحنيفة وابويوسف :- اسی مذکورہ اصول پر اگر کسی نے پرندے کے پنجرہ کا دروازہ کھول دیا جس کی وجہ سے پرندہ اڑ گیا، تو شیخین کے نزدیک دروازہ کھولنے والا پرندے کی قیمت کا ضامن نہ ہوگا، کیونکہ دروازہ کھولنا شرط ہے اس لیے کہ یہ پرندے کے اڑنے سے مانع تھا، اور ازالہ مانع کا نام شرط ہے، مگر یہ شرط علت پر یعنی پرندے کے فعل پر مقدم ہے، لہذا اس شرط میں سبب کے معنی ہوں گے، اور اس شرط میں علت کے معنی نہیں ہیں، کیونکہ علت یعنی پرندہ کا اڑنا اس شرط سے یعنی دروازہ کھولنے سے پیدا نہیں ہوا، کیونکہ دروازہ کھولنے سے پرندہ کا اڑنا ضروری نہیں ہے، لہذا جب شرط فی معنی السبب ہے نہ کہ فی معنی العلت تو پرندہ کے تلف ہونے کا حکم اس شرط کی طرف منسوب نہ ہو گا یعنی دروازہ کھولنے والا ضامن نہ ہوگا۔ لیکن سوال یہ پیدا ہوتا ہے کہ پھر کنویں میں گرنا بھی فاعل مختار کا فعل ہے جو شرط سے یعنی کنواں کھودنے سے پیدا نہیں ہوا، اور کنواں کھودنے میں علت کے معنی بھی نہیں تو کھودنے والے پر ضمان نہ آنا چاہیے۔ اس کا جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ گرنے والا ہے تو فاعل مختار مگر گرنے میں اس کا اختیار نہیں ہے، ہاں اگر گرنے میں اس کا اختیار ثابت ہو جائے اور یہ بات ثابت ہو جائے کہ اس نے جان بوجھ کر اپنے آپ کو گرایا ہے تو پھر حافر پر ضمان نہ ہو گا۔ اور امام محمد علیہ فرماتے ہیں کہ دروازہ کھولنے والے پر ضمان آئے گا، کیونکہ پرندہ کا فعل فاعل مختار کا فعل نہیں ہے بلکہ یہ شرط یعنی دروازہ کھولنے سے پیدا ہوا ہے، لہذا یہ شرط فی معنی العلہ ہوگی تو دروازہ کھولنے والے پر ضمان آئے گا۔
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf said: Based on this same principle, if someone opened the door of a bird's cage causing the bird to fly away, then according to the two Shaykhs, the one who opened the door will not be liable for the bird's value, because opening the door is a condition, since it was an obstacle to the bird flying, and removing an obstacle is called a condition. But this condition precedes the cause, i.e., the bird's act, so this condition has the meaning of a cause (sabab), and does not have the meaning of the real cause, because the cause, i.e., the bird's flying, was not generated by this condition, i.e., opening the door, since opening the door does not necessitate the bird flying. So when the condition is in the meaning of a cause (sabab) and not in the meaning of the real cause, the judgment of the bird's destruction will not be attributed to this condition, i.e., the one who opened the door will not be liable. But a question arises: then falling into a well is also an act of a free agent that was not generated by the condition of digging the well, and digging the well does not have the meaning of cause, so the digger should not be liable. The answer is: the fallen is indeed a free agent, but he has no choice in falling. Yes, if his choice in falling is established, and it is proven that he intentionally threw himself, then the digger will not be liable. And Imam Muhammad (peace be upon him) says: The one who opened the door will be liable, because the bird's act is not the act of a free agent; rather it was generated by the condition, i.e., opening the door. Therefore, this condition is in the meaning of the real cause, so the one who opened the door will be liable.
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute (ikhtilaf) within the Hanafi madhhab on the liability for opening a birdcage. The majority opinion of Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) applies the same rule as the earlier example: opening the cage is a condition that removes an obstacle, but the bird's flight is an act of a free agent. Since the bird chooses to fly (unlike a person falling involuntarily), the opener is not liable. They differentiate the well example: a person falling into a well usually does so involuntarily, so the digger is liable. But if the faller intentionally jumps, the digger is not liable. Imam Muhammad dissents: he considers the bird's flight not a free act because it is generated by the opening; the bird has no real choice. Hence, the condition is in the meaning of the cause, and liability attaches. This dispute highlights a subtle difference: whether the intervening act of a bird is considered a free agent's act or merely a natural consequence.

Key Terms
شیخین (Shaykhayn): The two shaykhs: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf; their joint opinion is cited as the majority view.
امام محمد (Imam Muhammad): Muhammad al-Shaybani, a leading disciple of Abu Hanifa, known for his independent juristic views and contributions to the Hanafi school.
شرط (shart): Condition; here it refers to an act that removes an obstacle, not a cause that produces an effect.
سبب (sabab): Cause; here it refers to an act that may lead to a legal judgment but is not the direct generator of the effect.
علت (illa): Real cause; the direct generator of an effect.
ضمان (daman): Liability; financial responsibility for loss or damage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, why is the person who opens a birdcage liable for the bird's loss?
A) Because opening the cage is a forbidden act
B) Because the bird's flight is generated by the opening, not a free act
C) Because the bird is like a slave
D) Because the cage door is property

Key Takeaway
The Shaykhayn hold that opening a birdcage does not create liability because the bird's flight is a voluntary act, while Imam Muhammad considers it a generated effect; the relied-upon view is that conditions that remove obstacles do not attract liability when a free agent's voluntary act intervenes.
