The Hanafi Position on Intellect and Legal Obligation
Stating the Hanafi position on the role of intellect in taklif and rebutting opposing views.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi-Maturidi position on the role of intellect in taklif and apply it to identify the errors of the Mu'tazili and Ash'ari/Shafi'i extremes.

Core Idea
Intellect is necessary for obligation but insufficient without revelation—the Hanafi middle path.

This passage from Sharh al-Muntakhab al-Husami presents the Hanafi-Maturidi equilibrium on the role of intellect in legal responsibility. The author defines intellect as a divine light, explains it as a condition (shart) rather than a cause (sabab) of obligation, and supports this with fiqhi examples. He then critiques both the Mu'tazila who make intellect an independent cause and the Ash'aris/Shafi'is who nullify it entirely. This lesson unpacks that argument and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three theological positions on intellect
Recognize the Mu'tazili extreme (intellect as illa mujiba), the Ash'ari/Shafi'i extreme (intellect as irrelevant), and the Hanafi-Maturidi middle path (intellect as shart).
This is a classic usul dispute about the epistemological foundation of obligation.
2
Define intellect as presented by the author
Extract the definition: 'a light in the body by which the heart perceives, but not independent; it needs revelation.'
The author uses both rational and textual arguments.
3
Examine the fiqhi examples
Work through the rulings on the child (not obligated), the murahiqa (not apostate until puberty), the person not reached by da'wa (excused if lacking capacity to reflect), and the safih (trial period of 25 years).
These examples demonstrate that intellect alone does not create obligation.
4
Analyze the rebuttal of opposing views
Understand why the Mu'tazili position is baseless (no proof) and why the Ash'ari/Shafi'i position is contradictory (uses intellect to nullify intellect).
The author highlights the inconsistency of Imam al-Shafi'i's ruling on blood money.
5
Synthesize the Hanafi-Maturidi position
Conclude that intellect is an attribute of eligibility (ahliyyah) but not a proof in itself; rulings come from revelation and some are ta'abbudi.
This is the 'middle path' upheld by the verifiers among the Hanafis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفيضُ الحجازي
۳۳۹
شرح اردو المنتخب الحسامي
ہیں، ان کے مذہب میں افراط ہے۔
(۲) اور اشاعرہ ان کے مقابلہ میں عقل کو بالکل بیکار اور ہدر قرار دیتے ہیں، چنانچہ وہ کہتے ہیں کہ بغیر ورود شرع کے عقل کا کوئی اعتبار نہیں ہے، لہذا اگر کوئی آدمی کفر و شرک کا عقیدہ رکھے ، اور اس کو اسلام کی دعوت نہ پہنچی ہو تو با وجود
عقل کے وہ معذور قرار دیا جائے گا، اشاعرہ کے مذہب میں تفریط ہے کہ وہ عقل کو بالکل ہی بدر قرار دیتے ہیں ۔ (۳) افراط و تفریط کے درمیان محققین کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ عقل بذات خود نہ احکام کی موجب ہے اور نہ مُحرم، بلکہ احکام کی تعیین شریعت کا کام ہے، لہذا ان میں ایسے احکام بھی ہوں گے جو عقل کی پرواز سے بالا تر ہوں گے مگر ان کو ماننا پڑے گا کیونکہ شریعت سے ثابت ہیں ، اسی لئے فقہاء ایسے احکام کو امر تعبدی کہتے ہیں، اور عقل بالکل بر کار بھی نہیں ہے کیونکہ بغیر عقل کے احکام شرع کی تکلیف کا وقوع نہیں ہوتا ہے، بلکہ تو جہ خطاب کا مبنی عقل ہے اس کے بغیر بندہ احکام شرع کا اہل نہیں بنتا، یہی مسلک ہے ماتریدیہ محققین احناف کا۔
وهونور فى بدن الارمى : - عقل ہے کیا چیز؟ مصنف " فرماتے ہیں کہ عقل انسانی بدن میں اللہ کا عنایت کردہ ایک نور ہے جس سے قلب کو وہ جلا حاصل ہوتا ہے جس میں انسان بتوفیق ایزیدی مطلوب کو حاصل کر لیتا ہے، عقل کا دائرہ کار بہت وسیع ہے، اس کے کام کا آغاز وہاں سے ہوتا ہے جہاں حواس کے کام کا اینڈ ہوتا ہے۔ عالم ظاہر میں عقل کی مثال ایسی ہے جیسے سورج، جب وہ طلوع ہوتا ہے تو عالم کو روشن کر دیتا ہے اور اس کی چمک اور روشنی سے آنکھ مرئیات کو دیکھتی ہے، ورنہ اندھیرے میں یہی آنکھ بیکار ہو جاتی ہے، بہر حال تامل عقل کے بعد قلب کو مطلوب حاصل ہو جاتا ہے، تبو قیق الہی نہ کہ بطریق تولید یعنی عقل اگر چہ ادراک کا آلہ اور اشیاء کے حسن و فتح کی معرفت کا ذریعہ ہے مگر عقل اس سلسلہ میں مستقل نہیں ہے، بلکہ ورو د شرع کی محتاج ہے، تنہا عقل کافی نہیں ہے۔ وَلِهَذَا قُلْنَا إِنَّ الصَّبِيَّ غَيْرُ مَكَلَّفٍ بِالْإِيْمَانِ حَتَّى إِذَا عَقَلَتِ الْمُرَاهِقَةُ وَهِيَ تَحْتَ مُسْلِمٍ بَيْنَ أَبَوَيْنِ مُسْلَمِيْنِ وَلَمْ تَصِفِ الْإِسْلَامَ لَمْ تُجْعَلُ مُرْتَدَةً وَلَمْ تَبِنْ مِنْ زَوْجِهَا وَلَوْ بَلَغَتْ كَذَلِكَ لَبَانَتْ مِنْ زَوْجِهَا وَكَذَا نُقُولُ فِي الَّذِئ لَمْ تَبْلُغُهُ الدَّعْوَةُ إِنَّهُ غَيْرُ مُكَلِّفٍ بِمُجَرَّدِ الْعَقْلِ وَإِنَّهُ إِذَا لَمْ بِصَفْ اِيْمَانًا وَلَا كُفْرًا وَلَمْ يَعْتَقِدُ عَلَى شَيْءٍ كَانَ مَعْدُورًا وَإِذَا دَعَانَهُ اللهُ بِالتَّجْرِبَةِ وَامْهَلَهُ لِدَرْكِ الْعَوَاقِب فَهُوَ لَمْ يَكُنْ مَعْدُورًا وَإِنْ لَمْ تَبْلُغُهُ الدَّعْوَةُ عَلَى نِحْوِمَا قَالَ أَبُو حَنِيْفَةَ فِي السَّفِيْهِ إِذَا بَلَغَ خَمْسًا وَعِشْرِيْنِ سَنَةً لَمْ يُمْنَعْ مَالُهُ مِنْهُ لِأَنَّهُ قَدْ اسْتَوْفَى
الفيضُ الحجازي
شرح اردو المنتخب الحسامي
مُدَةَ التَّجْرِبَةِ وَالْاِمْتِحَان فَلَابُدَ مِنْ أَنْ يَزْدَادَ بِهِ رُشْدًا وَلَيْسَ عَلَى الْحَدِ فِي هَذَا الْبَابَ دَلِيلٌ قَاطِعْ فَمَنْ جَعَلَ الْعَقْلَ عِلَّةً مَوْجِبَةً يَمْتَنِعُ الشَّرْعَ بِخِلَافِهِ فَلَا دَلِيْلِ لَهُ يَعْتَمِدُ عَلَيْهِ وَمَنْ اَلْغَاهُ مِنْ كُلِّ وَجْهِ فَلَادَلِيْلَ لَهُ أَيْضًا وَهُوَ مَذْهَبْ الشَّافِعِي الله فَإِنَّهُ قَالَ فِي قَوْمَ لَمْ تَبْلُغُهُمُ الدَّعْوَةُ إِذَا قُتِلُوا ضَمِنُوْ فَجَعَلَ كُفْرَهُمْ عَفُوًا وَذَلِكَ لِأَنَّهُ لَا يَجِدُ فِي الشَّرْعِ أَنَّ الْعَقْلَ غَيْرُ مُعْتَبَرٍ لِلْاهْلِيَةِ فَإِنَّمَا يُلْغِيْهِ بِدَلَالَةِ الْعَقْلِ وَالْإِجْتَهَادِ فَيَتَنَاقَضُ مَذْهَبُهُ وَإِنَ الْعَقْلَ لَا يَنْفَكُ عَنِ الْهَوى فَلَا يَصْلَحْ حُجَّةً بِنَفْسِهِ بِحَالٍ وَإِذَا ثَبَتَ اَنَّ الْعَقْلَ مِنْ صِفَاتِ الْاَهْلِيَةِ قُلْنَا
الْكَلَامُ فِي هَذَا يَنْقِسَمْ عَلَى قِسْمَيْنِ الْاَهْلِيَةِ وَالْأُمُورِ الْمُعْتَرِضَةِ عَلَيْهَا۔ ترجمہ :۔ اور اسی وجہ سے ہم نے کہا کہ بچہ ایمان کا مکلف نہیں ہے، یہانتک کہ جب مراہقہ سمجھدار ہو جائے اور یہ کسی مسلمان کے نکاح میں ہو دو مسلمان والدین کے درمیان، اور وہ اسلام کو بیان نہ کر سکے ، تو اس کو مرتدہ نہیں قرار دیا جائے گا، اور وہ اپنے شوہر سے بائنہ نہ ہوگی ، اور اگر وہ اسی حال میں بالغہ ہو جائے تو وہ اپنے شوہر سے بائنہ ہو جائے گی ، اور ایسے ہی ہم کہتے ہیں اس شخص کے بارے میں جس کو دعوت نہ پہنچی ہو کہ وہ محض عقل کی وجہ سے مکلف نہیں ہے، اور جب وہ ایمان اور کفر کو بیان نہ کر سکے اور کسی چیز کا معتقد نہ ہو تو وہ معذور ہوگا، اور جب تجربہ کے ذریعہ اللہ نے اس کی مدد کی ، اور عواقب ( انجام ) کو دریافت کرنے کے لئے اس کو مہلت دی تو وہ معذور نہ ہوگا اگر چہ اس کو دعوت نہ پہنچی ہو ، اسی طریقہ کے مثل جو امام ابو حنیفہ عالیہ نے سفیہ کے بارے میں فرمایا ہے کہ جب وہ پچیس سال کا ہو جائے تو اس سے اس کا مال نہیں روکا جائے گا، اس لئے کہ وہ تجربہ اور آزمائش کی مدت کو حاصل کر چکا ہے، تو ضروری ہے کہ اس سے اس کا رشد بڑھ جائے۔
اور اس باب میں ( کہ زمان تامل کے لئے کتنے دن ہوں ) کسی معین حد پر کوئی قطعی دلیل نہیں ہے، پس جس نے عقل کو علت موجبہ قرار دیا ہے تو وہ عقل کے خلاف ورود شرع کو ممنوع قرار دیتا ہے (جیسے معتزلہ )، پس اس کے پاس کوئی قابل اعتماد دلیل نہیں ہے، اور جس نے عقل کو بالکل لغو قرار دیا ہے، اس کے پاس بھی کوئی دلیل نہیں ہے، اور یہی امام شافعی کا مذہب ہے، اس لئے کہ امام شافعی اللہ نے ایسی قوم کے بارے میں فرمایا جس کو دعوت نہیں پہنچی کہ جب وہ قتل کئے گئے تو قاتل ان کے ضامن ہوں گے ، تو ان کے کفر کو عفو قرار دیا ، اور یہ ( دلیل کا نہ ہونا ) اس لئے کہ یہ (جو عقل کو لغو قرار دیتا ہے ) نہیں پائے گا شریعت میں کوئی دلیل کہ عقل اہلیت کے لئے غیر معتبر ہے، تو وہ عقل کو دلالتِ
The Fayd al-Hijazi
339
Urdu commentary on al-Muntakhab al-Husami
... (first part discusses extremes of Mu'tazila and Ash'aris). (3) Between excess and negligence, the school of the verifiers is that intellect by itself is neither necessitator of rulings nor prohibitor, rather determination of rulings is the work of Shari'ah. Therefore among them there will be rulings that are beyond the flight of intellect, but they must be accepted because they are established by Shari'ah. For this reason jurists call such rulings 'ta'abbudi matters'. And intellect is not entirely useless because without intellect, the obligation of Shari'ah rulings does not occur; rather the direction of address is based on intellect; without it a servant does not become qualified for Shari'ah rulings. This is the madhhab of the Maturidi verifiers among the Hanafis.
And it is a light in the body of the human: What is intellect? The author says that intellect is a light granted by Allah in the human body by which the heart obtains such brightness that a person, with divine assistance, attains the desired goal. The scope of intellect is very vast; its work begins where the work of the senses ends. In the external world, the example of intellect is like the sun: when it rises it illuminates the world, and by its brightness and light the eye sees visible things; otherwise in darkness the same eye becomes useless. In any case, after reflection of intellect, the heart attains the desired goal, by divine verification not by way of generation. That is, intellect is an instrument of perception and a means of knowing the beauty and goodness of things, but intellect is not independent in this matter; rather it is in need of revelation. Intellect alone is not sufficient. And for this we said that the child is not obligated regarding faith until when the adolescent girl becomes intelligent and she is under a Muslim between two Muslim parents and she does not describe Islam, she is not deemed an apostate and she does not separate from her husband. But if she reaches puberty in that state, she would separate from her husband. And similarly we say concerning the one whom the call has not reached that he is not obligated by mere intellect, and if he does not express faith nor disbelief and does not believe anything, he is excused. And when Allah aids him by trial and gives him respite to understand consequences, then he is not excused even if the call has not reached him, similar to what Abu Hanifa said about the foolish person: when he reaches twenty-five years, his wealth is not withheld from him because he has completed the period of trial and testing, so it is necessary that his discernment increases thereby. And in this chapter (concerning the specific period for reflection) there is no decisive proof on a specific limit. So whoever made intellect a necessitating cause, then he prohibits revelation contrary to it (like the Mu'tazila), so he has no reliable proof. And whoever completely nullified it, he also has no proof, and this is the madhhab of Imam al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, because Imam al-Shafi'i said concerning a people whom the call did not reach: if they are killed, the killer owes blood money, thus he considered their disbelief as pardoned. And that is because he does not find in the Shari'ah that intellect is not considered for eligibility; rather he nullifies it by indication of intellect and ijtihad, so his madhhab is contradictory. And indeed intellect is never free from desires, so it is not fit as a proof by itself in any case. And when it is proven that intellect is among the attributes of eligibility, we say: The discourse on this divides into two parts: eligibility and the obstacles that oppose it.
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion on the role of intellect (aql) in Islamic legal theory, specifically its relationship to legal obligation (taklif). The author presents the Hanafi-Maturidi position as the middle path between two extremes: the Mu'tazila who make intellect the sole cause of obligation (excessive), and the Ash'aris who completely disregard intellect (negligent). The correct view, according to the verifiers of the Hanafis, is that intellect is a necessary condition for obligation but not sufficient by itself; divine revelation (Shari'ah) determines rulings. Some rulings may be beyond intellectual grasp (ta'abbudi), but they must be accepted. Intellect is described as a divine light enabling perception, but it requires revelation's guidance. The author then gives furoo' (branches) to illustrate: a child is not obligated for faith until reason develops; an adolescent girl (murahiqa) under Muslims who cannot express Islam is not judged apostate until she reaches puberty; a person who never received da'wa is not obligated solely by intellect, but if granted capacity to reflect, becomes accountable. The example of the safih (foolish person) from Abu Hanifa shows that after a period of trial (25 years), he is trusted with his wealth. The passage concludes that there is no decisive proof for a specific time limit for reflection, and criticizes both extremes. It particularly critiques Imam Shafi'i's position that those not reached by da'wa are completely excused (blood money is due if killed), arguing that Shafi'i inconsistently nullifies intellect using intellectual reasoning itself, and that intellect is not free from desires, so it cannot be a proof by itself.

Key Terms
العقل (al-'aql): A divine light in the human body enabling perception and cognition; an attribute of eligibility for taklif but insufficient without revelation.
المراهقة (al-murāhiqa): An adolescent girl who has reached the age of discernment but not yet puberty.
السفيه (al-safīh): A person lacking prudent judgment in financial matters; Abu Hanifa ruled that after 25 years he is trusted with his wealth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi-Maturidi position presented, which of the following best describes the role of intellect (aql) in legal obligation?
A) Intellect is the sole cause of obligation; revelation is unnecessary.
B) Intellect is completely irrelevant; only revelation matters.
C) Intellect is a necessary condition but not sufficient; revelation determines rulings.
D) Intellect and revelation are independent sources; one can override the other.

Key Takeaway
Intellect is a necessary condition for legal obligation, but only revelation determines what is obligatory; the Hanafi-Maturidi position is the balanced middle path.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
The Role of Reason in Legal Obligation: Hanafi/Maturidi Middle Path
Dispute on whether reason alone obligates faith and legal capacity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi/Maturidi position on the role of reason in legal obligation and distinguish it from the Mu'tazili and Ash'ari positions.

Core Idea
Reason is the basis of legal eligibility but not an independent source of obligation.

The question of whether reason alone obligates a person to believe and act is a foundational dispute in usul al-fiqh. The Hanafi school, following the Maturidi theological tradition, takes a moderate position: reason is the basis for legal eligibility (ahlīyah) but obligation arises only through divine address (khitab). This lesson unpacks this position against the extremes of the Mu'tazila, who treat reason as an independent source of obligation, and the Ash'aris, who deny reason any role in obligation. Understanding this dispute is crucial for grasping the Hanafi theory of taklif and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
State the Mu'tazili, Ash'ari, and Hanafi/Maturidi views on whether reason alone obligates a person to believe in God and follow Shariah.
Mu'tazila: reason is sufficient for obligation. Ash'aris: only divine address obligates. Hanafis: reason is basis for eligibility but obligation requires address; however, once address is possible (even indirectly), the person becomes obligated.
2
Examine the Hanafi proofs from the text
Analyze the examples given: (a) child's faith is valid if it occurs but not obligatory; (b) a minor girl near puberty is not apostate until adulthood; (c) a person not reached by da'wah is excused only if he had no time to reflect.
These examples illustrate that reason alone does not create obligation, but it is a condition for the validity of acts and for eligibility.
3
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Consider the blood money (diyah) example: if a sane adult not reached by da'wah is killed, Ash'aris/Shafi'i say diyah is due because the person was not obligated; Hanafis say no diyah because the person was obligated to believe and reflect.
This difference shows the real-world impact: liability for homicide depends on whether the victim was mukallaf.
4
Evaluate the Ash'ari contradiction
The passage argues that Ash'aris use reason to prove that reason is irrelevant, which is self-contradictory (they rely on rational proofs and ijtihad).
This critique is methodological: if reason is utterly invalid, one cannot use it to argue anything.
5
Conclude the Hanafi middle path
Reason is the basis (madār) of eligibility (ahlīyah) but not an independent proof. Obligation stems from divine address, but the capacity to receive that address depends on reason.
This leads to the next topic: the two divisions of speech about eligibility.

عقل اور اجتہاد کی وجہ سے لغو قرار دیتے ہیں، تو ان کا مذہب متناقض ہو جائے گا ، اور بیشک عقل نفسانی خواہشات سے جدا نہیں ہوتی ، تو عقل بنفسہ کسی حال میں حجت بنے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھے گی ، اور جب یہ بات ثابت ہو گئی کہ عقل اہلیت کی صفات میں سے ہے ، تو ہم کہیں گے کہ کلام بیان اہلیت کے سلسلہ میں منقسم ہے دو قسموں پر ، ایک اہلیت اور دوسرے وہ امور جو اہلیت پر عارض ہوتے ہیں۔
تشریح:- مصنف مصنف االلہ ماقبل میں بیان کردہ اصول پر کچھ جزئیات پیش فرمارہے ہیں، پہلی تفریع کہ بچہ ایمان کا مکلف نہیں ہے، اس لئے کہ احکام شرع خطاب سے ثابت ہوتے ہیں، محض عقل سے ثابت نہیں ہوتے اور بچہ غیر مکلف اور غیر مخاطب ہے، ہاں اگر وہ ایمان لے آیا تو وجود عقل کی وجہ سے اس کا ایمان صحیح اور معتبر ہوگا، اور اشاعرہ صرف ورود شرع کا اعتبار کرتے ہیں،اس لئے ان کے نزدیک بچہ کا ایمان معتبر نہیں کیونکہ بچہ درود شرع کا مکلف نہیں ہے، اور معتزلہ چونکہ صرف عقل کو سب کچھ مانتے ہیں اس لئے ان کے نزدیک بچہ عاقل ہو تو اس پر ایمان لانا واجب ہے اگر چہ وہ درود شرع کا
مکلف نہیں ہے ۔
دوسری تفریح ایک مراہقہ یعنی قریب البلوغ لڑکی کسی مسلمان کی منکوحہ ہو، اور حکما یہ لڑکی بھی مسلمان ہو یعنی اس کے والدین مسلمان ہوں لیکن یہ لڑکی اسلام کو بیان نہ کر سکے ، اس کو معلوم نہیں کہ اسلام کیا چیز ہے، تو اس کو مرتدہ نہ قرار دیں گے اور وہ اپنے شوہر سے بائنہ نہ ہوگی لیکن اگر وہ بالغہ ہوگئی اور اب بھی وہ اسلام کو بیان کرنے پر قادر نہیں ہے، تو وہ مرتدہ کہلائے گی، کیونکہ بالغ ہونے کے بعد اس پر اسلام لانا واجب تھا، اور اپنے شوہر سے بائنہ ہو جائے گی، کیونکہ مرتدہ مسلمان کے نکاح میں اختلاف دین کی وجہ سے نہیں رہ سکتی ۔
اسی طرح اگر کوئی بالغ لڑکا ہو اور اس کو اسلام کی دعوت نہیں پہنچی تو وہ محض عقل کی وجہ سے ایمان کا مکلف نہ ہوگا ، اور اگر بالغ ہونے کے بعد اس کو اتنا موقع نہیں ملا کہ وہ غور و فکر کر کے خالق کو پہنچانتا بلکہ بالغ ہوتے ہی مرگیا تو وہ معذور قرار دیا جائے گا، پس اگر وہ بالغ ہونے کے بعد ایمان اور کفر کو بیان نہ کر سکے اور کسی چیز پر اس کا اعتقاد نہ ہو تو یہ معذور اور غیر معذب ہوگا، لیکن اگر بالغ ہونے کے بعد اتنا زندہ رہا کہ غور و فکر کر کے اسلام قبول کرتا مگر اس نے اسلام قبول نہیں کیا تو اس زمان تامل کو دعوت کے قائم مقام کر کے اس کو معذور نہیں قرار دیا جائے گا۔۔ جیسے امام ابوحنیفہ سے فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر کوئی بچہ بالغ ہو جائے تو بالغ ہوتے ہی اس کا مال اس کے حوالہ کیا جائے گا لیکن اگر وہ شخص سفیہ اور کم عقل ہے تو اس کا مال اس کو اس وقت حوالہ کیا جائے گا جب وہ مقام رشد کو پہنچ جائے یعنی اس میں نفع اور نقصان کی تمیز پیدا ہو جائے ، جو بقول امام صاحب پچیس سال ہیں، لہذا پچیس سال کے بعد اس کا مال اس کے حوالہ کیا جائے گا ، اسی طرح بلوغ کے بعد زمان تامل کو دعوت کے قائم مقام قرار دے کر اس کو مکلف قرار دیا جائے گا، لہذا

وہ معذور نہ ہو گا ، اب بالغ ہونے کے بعد تامل اور غور وفکر کے لئے کتنی مدت ہو تو اس سلسلہ میں تحدید تعیین پر کوئی قطعی دلیل نہیں ہے، اگر چہ قیاس کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ تین دن کی مہلت دیجائے مگر لوگوں کی عقلوں کے تفاوت کی وجہ سے تین دن کی مہلت صحیح نہیں ہے پس بہتر یہی ہے کہ اس کی تحدید تعیین اللہ کے سپر د کر دی جائے۔ فنن جعل العقل : بهر حال خلاصہ کلام یہ کہ باب عقل میں ماتریدیہ کا مذہب بین بین ہے، اور معتزلہ به اور اشاعرہ کے مذہب میں افراط و تفریط ہے، معتزلہ نے سارا مدار عقل پر رکھدیا ، اور عقل کو علت موجبہ اور علت مستقلہ قرار دیا، اور عقل کے خلاف شریعت ہو تو انکار کر دیتے ہیں، ان کے پاس اس مذہب کے لئے کوئی قابل اعتماد دلیل نہیں ہے، ان کے بالمقامل اشاعرہ نے عقل کو بالکل ہی لغو قرار دیا، ان کے پاس بھی کوئی قابل اعتماد دلیل نہیں ہے، امام شافعی نے بھی اشاعرہ کا مذہب اختیار کیا ہے کیونکہ وہ اس آدمی کو بالکل معذور قرار دیتے ہیں جس کو دعوت نہ پہنچی ہو، لہذا ایسے شخص کو اگر کوئی قتل کرے تو قاتل پر ضمان دیت واجب ہوگا کیونکہ مقتول کے پاس دعوت نہیں پہنچی اگر چہ وہ عاقل بالغ ہے، لہذا اس کو کافر نہ کہا جائے گا، اور احناف کے نزدیک چونکہ اس کو غور و فکر کا زمانہ مل گیا تو وہ معذور نہیں ہوگا بلکہ اس پر ایمان لانا واجب ہوگا، لہذا اس کو قتل کرنے والے پر ضمان دیت واجب نہ ہوگا ، بہر حال اشاعرہ اور امام شافعی وغیرہ جو عقل کو لغو قرار دیتے ہیں، تو ان کے پاس کوئی دلیل نہیں ہے کیونکہ شریعت میں کہیں بھی یہ بات نہیں ہے کہ عقل اہلیت کے لئے غیر معتبر ہے، پھر عقل کا غیر معتبر ہونا انہوں نے دلالت عقل اور اجتہاد ہی سے ثابت کیا تو ایک طرف تو انہوں نے کہا کہ عقل غیر معتبر ہے اور دوسری طرف عقل کا غیر معتبر ہونا عقل و اجتہاد ہی سے ثابت کیا تو گویا انہوں نے عقل کو معتبر مانا تو ان کے مذہب میں تناقض ہے، لہذا عقل کو لغو قرار دینا بھی صحیح نہیں ہے پھر عقل کے ساتھ خواہشات نفسانی کا اختلاط رہتا ہے تو عقل کو حجت بنفسہ اور علت مستقلہ قرار دینا بھی غلط ہے، لہذا اعتدال کی راہ یہی ہوئی کہ معقل مدار اہلیت ہے، لہذا اب اہلیت کا بیان شروع کر رہے ہیں، فرماتے ہیں کہ بیانِ اہلبیت کے سلسلہ میں کلام دو قسموں پر منقسم ہے، ایک اہلیت، اور دوسرے وہ امور جو اہلیت پر عارض ہوتے ہیں۔
Al-Fayd al-Hijazi 341 Commentary in Urdu on al-Muntakhab al-Husami. They consider [reason] null due to intellect and ijtihad, so their doctrine becomes contradictory. And indeed intellect is not separate from carnal desires, so reason by itself cannot be a proof in any case. And when it is proven that reason is among the attributes of eligibility, we say that speech about the explanation of eligibility is divided into two parts: one is eligibility, and the other is the things that affect eligibility. Explanation: The author (may Allah have mercy on him) is presenting some details based on the principles mentioned earlier. First detail: A child is not obligated to have faith, because the rulings of Shariah are established by address, not by mere reason, and the child is not obligated nor addressed. However, if he does come to faith, his faith is valid and acceptable due to the presence of reason. The Ash'aris only consider the arrival of divine law, so according to them a child's faith is not valid because the child is not obligated by the divine law. The Mu'tazila, because they consider reason everything, say that if a child is rational, he is obligated to believe, even if he is not obligated by divine law. Second detail: A girl near puberty married to a Muslim, and her parents are Muslim, but she cannot express Islam, she is not considered an apostate and does not become separated from her husband. But if she reaches adulthood and still cannot express Islam, she is called an apostate, because after adulthood it was obligatory to accept Islam, and she becomes separated from her husband, because an apostate cannot remain in a Muslim's marriage due to difference of religion. Similarly, if an adult boy has not received the call to Islam, he is not obligated to believe by mere reason. If after adulthood he had no opportunity to reflect and know the Creator, but died immediately, he is excused. If after adulthood he cannot express belief or disbelief and has no conviction, he is excused and not punished. But if he lived long enough to reflect and accept Islam but did not, then that period of reflection is considered as the call, and he is not excused. As Imam Abu Hanifa says: If a child reaches adulthood, his property is handed over to him immediately, but if he is foolish and weak-minded, his property is handed over when he reaches the level of maturity, i.e., when he distinguishes benefit and harm, which according to Imam Sahib is twenty-five years. So after twenty-five years his property is handed over. Similarly, after adulthood, the period of reflection is considered as the call and he is deemed obligated. So he is not excused. As for how long the time for reflection after adulthood should be, there is no definitive evidence. Qiyas requires a three-day grace period, but due to differences in people's intellects, a three-day grace is not correct. So it is better to leave its determination to Allah. 'فنن جعل العقل' In summary, the Maturidi doctrine regarding reason is moderate, while the Mu'tazila and Ash'aris are extreme. The Mu'tazila made everything dependent on reason, making it a necessary cause and independent cause, and deny Shariah if it contradicts reason. They have no reliable evidence for this doctrine. In contrast, the Ash'aris declared reason completely null. They also have no reliable evidence. Imam Shafi'i also adopted the Ash'ari doctrine because they deem a person completely excused if the call did not reach him. So if someone kills such a person, blood money is obligatory because the call did not reach him, even if he is a sane adult, so he is not called a disbeliever. According to the Hanafis, since he had time for reflection, he is not excused but rather obligated to believe, so the killer does not have to pay blood money. In any case, the Ash'aris and Imam Shafi'i who declare reason null have no evidence, because Shariah nowhere states that reason is invalid for eligibility. Moreover, they proved reason's invalidity by rational evidence and ijtihad, so on one hand they say reason is invalid, and on the other they use reason and ijtihad to prove it, thus they have recognized reason, so their doctrine is contradictory. Therefore, declaring reason null is also incorrect. Also, since reason mixes with carnal desires, making reason an independent proof and cause is also wrong. The moderate path is that reason is the basis of eligibility. Therefore, we begin the explanation of eligibility. He says: The discourse on the explanation of eligibility is divided into two parts: one is eligibility, and the other is the things that affect eligibility.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage presents the Maturidi/Hanafi position on the role of reason (aql) in legal obligation (taklif). It is a polemical discussion refuting both the Mu'tazili extreme (reason as independent source of obligation) and the Ash'ari extreme (reason as irrelevant). The author uses specific examples: (1) a child's faith is valid if it occurs, but not obligatory due to lack of address; (2) a minor girl near puberty is not considered apostate until adulthood; (3) a person not reached by da'wah is excused only if he had no time to reflect; (4) the example of blood money for killing a person not reached by da'wah: according to Ash'aris/Shafi'i, blood money is due; according to Hanafis, not due because the person was obligated. The author argues that the Ash'ari position is self-contradictory because they use reason to prove reason is irrelevant. The Maturidi middle path is that reason is the basis of eligibility (ahlīyah) but not an independent source of obligation. The passage then transitions to the topic of ahliyah.

Key Terms
عقل (aql): Reason/intellect, which is a basis for eligibility (ahlīyah) but not an independent source of obligation.
اہلیت (ahlīyah): Legal capacity/eligibility, which is the ability to have rights and obligations and to perform acts.
مکلف (mukallaf): A person who is addressed by divine law and obligated to act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi/Maturidi position, what is the status of a minor girl (murahiqah) who is married to a Muslim and cannot express Islam?
A) She is immediately considered an apostate and the marriage is dissolved.
B) She is not considered an apostate until she reaches adulthood.
C) Her marriage is invalid because she cannot express Islam.
D) She is considered a Muslim only if her parents are Muslim.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that reason is the basis of legal eligibility, but obligation arises only through divine address or its substitute (opportunity to reflect).

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

The Authority of Reason in Legal Capacity: Hanafi Middle Path
Dispute on the authority of reason in taklif

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi-Maturidi position on the role of reason in legal capacity, critique the Ash'ari contradiction, and apply the ruling to the case of diyya for an unreached adult.

Core Idea
Reason is the basis of legal capacity; the Hanafi middle path avoids both over-reliance and dismissal of 'aql.

This passage addresses a fundamental usul dispute: Is reason an autonomous source of obligation? The Hanafi school, following the Maturidi theological path, steers between the Mu'tazili overemphasis and the Ash'ari denial. Understanding this position is key to grasping the Hanafi theory of taklif and capacity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions on 'aql
Distinguish the Mu'tazili (over-reliance), Ash'ari (dismissal), and Maturidi/Hanafi (middle path) views on the role of reason in legal capacity.
2
Analyze the Hanafi evidence
The Hanafis argue that capacity is based on dhimma, which is inherent in every human, and that Shari'a never invalidates reason. Reason is a necessary condition for taklif.
3
Critique the Ash'ari contradiction
The Ash'aris invalidate reason but use rational argument to prove its invalidity, creating a performative contradiction.
4
Derive the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: for a sane adult who has not received the call, the Hanafis say belief is obligatory (no diyya), while the Ash'aris say he is excused (diyya required).
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is preferred because it avoids internal contradiction and aligns with the Shari'a's recognition of reason as a basis for capacity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وہ معذور نہ ہو گا، اب بالغ ہونے کے بعد تامل اور غور وفکر کے لئے کتنی مدت ہو تو اس سلسلہ میں تحدید تعیین پر کوئی قطعی دلیل نہیں ہے، اگر چہ قیاس کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ تین دن کی مہلت دیجائے مگر لوگوں کی عقلوں کے تفاوت کی وجہ سے تین دن کی مہلت صحیح نہیں ہے پس بہتر یہی ہے کہ اس کی تحدید تعیین اللہ کے سپرد کر دی جائے۔ فإن جعل العقل [؟] : بہرحال خلاصہ کلام یہ کہ باب عقل میں ماتریدیہ کا مذہب بین بین ہے، اور معتزلہ اور اشاعرہ کے مذہب میں افراط و تفریط ہے، معتزلہ نے سارا مدار عقل پر رکھدیا، اور عقل کو علت موجبہ اور علت مستقلہ قرار دیا، اور عقل کے خلاف شریعت ہو تو انکار کر دیتے ہیں، ان کے پاس اس مذہب کے لئے کوئی قابل اعتماد دلیل نہیں ہے، ان کے بالمقابل اشاعرہ نے عقل کو بالکل ہی لغو قرار دیا، ان کے پاس بھی کوئی قابل اعتماد دلیل نہیں ہے، امام شافعی نے بھی اشاعرہ کا مذہب اختیار کیا ہے کیونکہ وہ اس آدمی کو بالکل معذور قرار دیتے ہیں جس کو دعوت نہ پہنچی ہو، لہذا ایسے شخص کو اگر کوئی قتل کرے تو قاتل پر ضمان دیت واجب ہوگا کیونکہ مقتول کے پاس دعوت نہیں پہنچی اگر چہ وہ عاقل بالغ ہے، لہذا اس کو کافر نہ کہا جائے گا، اور احناف کے نزدیک چونکہ اس کو غور و فکر کا زمانہ مل گیا تو وہ معذور نہیں ہوگا بلکہ اس پر ایمان لانا واجب ہوگا، لہذا اس کو قتل کرنے والے پر ضمان دیت واجب نہ ہوگا، بہر حال اشاعرہ اور امام شافعی وغیرہ جو عقل کو لغو قرار دیتے ہیں، تو ان کے پاس کوئی دلیل نہیں ہے کیونکہ شریعت میں کہیں بھی یہ بات نہیں ہے کہ عقل اہلیت کے لئے غیر معتبر ہے، پھر عقل کا غیر معتبر ہونا انہوں نے دلالت عقل اور اجتہاد ہی سے ثابت کیا تو ایک طرف تو انہوں نے کہا کہ عقل غیر معتبر ہے اور دوسری طرف عقل کا غیر معتبر ہونا عقل و اجتہاد ہی سے ثابت کیا تو گویا انہوں نے عقل کو معتبر مانا تو ان کے مذہب میں تناقض ہے، لہذا عقل کو لغو قرار دینا بھی صحیح نہیں ہے پھر عقل کے ساتھ خواہشات نفسانی کا اختلاط رہتا ہے تو عقل کو حجت بنفسہ اور علت مستقلہ قرار دینا بھی غلط ہے، لہذا اعتدال کی راہ یہی ہوئی کہ عقل مدار اہلیت ہے، لہذا اب اہلیت کا بیان شروع کر رہے ہیں،
He will not be excused. After reaching adulthood, regarding the period for reflection and contemplation, there is no definitive evidence for specifying a fixed duration. Although analogical reasoning requires giving a three-day respite, due to the variation in people's intellects, a three-day respite is not correct. So it is better to delegate its specification to Allah. As for 'aql (reason): In any case, the conclusion is that in the chapter of 'aql, the school of the Maturidiyya is the middle path, whereas the schools of the Mu'tazila and the Ash'ariyya contain excess and deficiency. The Mu'tazila placed the entire basis on 'aql, and made 'aql a necessitating cause and an independent cause, and if the Shari'a contradicts 'aql, they reject it. They have no reliable proof for this school. In contrast, the Ash'ariyya declared 'aql completely irrelevant; they also have no reliable proof. Imam al-Shafi'i also adopted the Ash'ari school because they consider a person to be absolutely excused if the call (da'wa) did not reach him. Therefore, if someone kills such a person, blood money (diyya) is obligatory upon the killer because the call did not reach the slain, even though he was a mature sane adult. Thus he will not be called an unbeliever. According to the Hanafis, since he obtained time for reflection, he is not excused; rather, belief (iman) becomes obligatory upon him. Therefore, blood money is not obligatory upon the one who kills him. In any case, the Ash'aris and Imam al-Shafi'i etc. who declare 'aql irrelevant have no proof, because nowhere in the Shari'a is it stated that 'aql is invalid for capacity. Moreover, they proved the invalidity of 'aql through rational evidence and ijtihad itself. So on one hand they said 'aql is invalid, and on the other hand they proved the invalidity of 'aql through 'aql and ijtihad, thus they have acknowledged 'aql as valid. Hence there is a contradiction in their school. Therefore, declaring 'aql irrelevant is also incorrect. Furthermore, since carnal desires mingle with 'aql, making 'aql an independent proof and independent cause is also wrong. So the path of moderation is that 'aql is the basis of capacity. Hence, now we begin the explanation of capacity.
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This passage is a usul al-fiqh dispute concerning the authority of reason ('aql) in matters of legal capacity and taklif. The author begins by addressing a specific issue: after a person reaches adulthood, how much time should be given for reflection? The author states there is no fixed duration; it is delegated to Allah. He then summarizes the theological positions on 'aql. The Maturidiyya (the Hanafi theological school) adopt a middle path between the extremes of the Mu'tazila and the Ash'ariyya. The Mu'tazila make 'aql an independent and necessitating cause, rejecting any revelation that contradicts it. The Ash'ariyya (including Imam al-Shafi'i) declare 'aql completely irrelevant and consider a person excused if the call of Islam did not reach them, even if they are rational adults. The Hanafis respond by pointing out the internal contradiction in the Ash'ari position: they invalidate 'aql but use 'aql to prove its invalidity. Moreover, the Shari'a does not anywhere state that 'aql is invalid for capacity. Rather, the middle path is that 'aql is the basis (madar) for capacity. The text then transitions to the topic of ahliyyah (capacity).

Key Terms
العقل (al-'aql): Reason or intellect, considered by the Hanafis as the basis for legal capacity (ahliyyah) and a valid tool for understanding obligations when revelation is absent or ambiguous.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the ruling on blood money (diyya) for killing a sane adult who has not received the call of Islam?
A) It is obligatory because the killer must pay for a life.
B) It is not obligatory because the slain had time to reflect and should have believed, so he is not excused.
C) It is half the full diyya.
D) It is subject to qisas (retaliation).

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi-Maturidi position affirms reason as the basis of capacity, avoiding the extremes of the Mu'tazila and Ash'ariyya.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

Rulings on a Minor’s Agency, Will, and Apostasy
Applying ahliyyah qasirah to agency, will, inheritance, and apostasy with inter-madhhab differences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle of ahliyyah qasirah to derive rulings on a minor’s agency, will, and apostasy, and distinguish the Hanafi positions from opposing views.

Core Idea
A minor’s deficient capacity makes his acts binding only with guardian consent, and apostasy carries no death penalty.

This passage demonstrates how the Hanafi usul principle of deficient legal capacity (ahliyyah qasirah) governs a minor’s validity in various transactions. The text addresses agency, will, and apostasy, showing that the minor’s lack of full intent prevents full liability. It also highlights key intra-madhhab and inter-madhhab differences with Imam al-Shafi’i and Abu Yusuf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the underlying usul principle
Recognize that the minor’s deficient capacity (ahliyyah qasirah) is the core principle driving the rulings. This principle means the minor’s actions are not fully binding without guardian approval.
Ahliyyah qasirah is a key concept in Hanafi usul for explaining limitations on a minor’s legal acts.
2
Apply the principle to agency
Note that if a minor acts as an agent, liability does not bind him unless the guardian permits. This shows that capacity to accept liability is incomplete without guardian consent.
3
Apply the principle to will
The text states a minor’s will is void even for acts of righteousness. This is based on qiyas with divorce, manumission, etc., which are not legislated for minors.
Contrast with al-Shafi’i who validates a minor’s will for good deeds.
4
Apply the principle to apostasy
A minor’s apostasy does not incur capital punishment according to Abu Hanifah and Muhammad. Worldly rulings apply as a consequence of validity, not as intentional punishment.
Abu Yusuf disagrees; this is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
5
Trace the legal reasoning (qiyas)
The text uses analogy: just as divorce, manumission, gift, and loan are not legislated for minors, so too will and full agency liability are not valid without full capacity. This is a talil (reasoning) based on shared illa.
Understanding the qiyas chain is essential for usul al-fiqh analysis.

وَعَلَى هَذَا قُلْنَا فِي الْمَرِ إِذَا تَوَكَّلَ لَمْ تَلْزَمْهُ الْعُهْدَةُ وَبِاذْنِ الْوَلِي تَلْزَمَهُ وَأَمَا إِذَا أَوْصَى الصَّبِيُّ بِشَيْءٍ مِنْ أَعْمَالِ الْبِرِّ بَطَلَتْ وَصِيَّتُهُ عَنْدَنَا خِلَافًا لِلشَّافِعِي وَإِنْ كَانَ فِيْهِ نَفْعٌ ظَاهِرْلِاَنَ الْإِرْثَ شُرِعَ نَفْعًا لِلْمُوْرِثِ أَلَا تَرَىٰ أَنَّهُ شُرِعَ فِي حَقَّ الصَّبِيَّ وَفِي الْأَنْتِقَالِ عَنْهُ إِلَى الْإِيْصَاءِ تَرْكَ الْأَفْضَلِ لَا مُحَالَةَ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ شُرِعَ فِي حَقَّ الْبَالِغِ كَمَا شُرِعَ لَهُ الطَّلَاقُ وَالْعَتَاقُ وَالْهِبَةُ وَالْقَرْضُ وَلَمْ يُشْرَعُ ذَلِكَ فِي حَقَّ الصَّبِى وَلَمْ يَمْلِكُ ذَلِكَ عَلَيْهِ غَيْرُهُ مَا خَلَا الْقَرْضِ فَإِنَّهُ يَمْلِكُهُ الْقَاضِي لِوُقُوعِ الْأَمْنِ عَنِ التَّوَىٰ بِوِلَايَةِ الْقَضَاءِ وَأَمَّا الرِّدَةُ فَلَا تَحْتَمِلُ الْعَفْوَ فِي أَحْكَامِ الْآخِرَةِ وَمَا يَلْزَمْهُ مِنْ أَحْكَامِ الدُّيْنَا عِنْدَهُمَا خِلَافًا لِأَبِي يُوسُفَ فَإِنَّمَا يَلْزَمُهُ حُكْمًا لِصِحَتِهِ لَا قَصْدًا إِلَيْهِ فَلَمْ يَصِحَ الْعَفْوَ عَنْ مِثْلِهِ كَمَا إِذَا ثَبَتَ تَبْعَالِأَبَوَيْهِ۔
ترجمہ:۔ اور اسی بنیاد پر ہم نے کہا صبئ مہجور کے بارے میں کہ جب وہ وکیل ہو گیا تو اس پر ذمہ داری لازم نہ ہوگی ، اور ولی کی اجازت سے اس کو ذمہ داری لازم ہو جائے گی ، اور بہر حال جب بچہ نے اعمال پر میں سے کسی کی وصیت کر دی تو ہمارے نزدیک اس کی وصیت باطل ہو جائے گی، امام شافعی اللہ کے خلاف ، اگر چہ اس میں ظاہر بچہ کا نفع ہو، اس لئے کہ میراث مورث کے نفع کے لئے مشروع کی گئی ہے، کیا نہیں دیکھتے کہ میراث بچہ کے حق میں مشروع ہے، اور میراث سے ایصاء کی طرف انتقال میں یقینا افضل کو ترک کرنا ہے، مگر یہ کہ ایصاء مشروع ہے بالغ کے حق میں جیسے اس کے لئے طلاق ، عتاق ، ہبہ اور قرض مشروع ہے، اور یہ بچہ کے حق میں مشروع نہیں ہے، اور اس کا بچہ پر
And on this basis we said regarding the [minor] that if he becomes an agent (wakil), the liability (uhdah) does not become incumbent upon him, and with the guardian's permission it becomes incumbent. As for when a minor makes a will (wasiyyah) of some acts of righteousness, his will is void according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i, even if there is apparent benefit in it, because inheritance was legislated for the benefit of the one leaving it (al-muwarith). Do you not see that it was legislated for the minor's right? And in transferring from it to will, there is inevitably leaving the superior. But it was legislated for the adult's right, just as divorce, manumission, gift, and loan were legislated for him, and these were not legislated for the minor, and no one else has authority over him regarding that, except for loan, for the judge has authority over it due to safety from loss through the authority of judiciary. As for apostasy, it does not admit forgiveness in the rulings of the afterlife. And what becomes incumbent upon him of worldly rulings—according to the two [Abu Hanifah and Muhammad], contrary to Abu Yusuf—it becomes incumbent on him as a ruling of its validity, not intentionally, so forgiveness of such a thing is not valid, just as when it is established on a subsidiary basis from his parents.
Translation: And on this basis we said regarding the minor under interdiction (sabi mahjur) that when he becomes an agent, liability does not become necessary upon him, and with the guardian's permission it becomes necessary. And in any case, when the child makes a will of some acts of righteousness, according to us his will is void, contrary to Imam Shafi'i, even if there is apparent benefit for the child. This is because inheritance was legislated for the benefit of the one leaving it. Do you not see that inheritance is legislated for the child's right? And transferring from inheritance to will inevitably involves leaving the superior. But will is legislated for the adult's right, just as divorce, manumission, gift, and loan are legislated for him, and these are not legislated for the child, and no one else has authority over him regarding that, except for loan, for the judge has authority over it due to safety from loss through the authority of judiciary. And as for apostasy, it does not admit forgiveness in the rulings of the afterlife. And what becomes incumbent upon him of worldly rulings—according to the two, contrary to Abu Yusuf—it becomes incumbent on him as a ruling of its validity, not intentionally, so forgiveness of such a thing is not valid, just as when it is established on a subsidiary basis from his parents.
Source pages p. 349

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of a minor's legal capacity. It states four rulings: (1) Agency: When a minor acts as an agent, he is not liable for the transaction unless the guardian permits; with permission, liability attaches. (2) Will: A minor's will for acts of righteousness is void in the Hanafi school, contrary to Shafi'i, because inheritance is designed for the testator's benefit, and moving from inheritance to will abandons a superior arrangement; will is only legislated for adults. (3) Loan: The judge can give a loan on behalf of a minor because judicial authority ensures safety. (4) Apostasy: A minor's apostasy does not carry the death penalty in worldly rulings according to Abu Hanifah and Muhammad, but Abu Yusuf disagrees. The text explains that apostasy rulings in the afterlife are not forgivable, but worldly penalties only apply as a consequence of validity, not intentionally, so repentance does not negate them. The passage uses the principle of deficient capacity to show that a minor cannot be fully liable in agency or will, but inheritance is established for their benefit without their intention.

Key Terms
وکالت (wakalah): Agency; a contract where one person appoints another to act on their behalf. Liability (uhdah) is not binding on the minor without guardian's permission.
وصیت (wasiyyah): Will; a disposition of property after death. A minor's will is void in Hanafi fiqh.
ارتداد (riddah): Apostasy; rejection of faith. For a minor, it does not entail capital punishment according to Abu Hanifah and Muhammad.
عهدة (uhdah): Liability or responsibility arising from a contract or agency. In the text, the minor is not bound by uhdah unless the guardian permits.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as presented in the text, what is the ruling on a minor's will (wasiyyah)?
A) It is valid if it benefits the minor.
B) It is void, even if there is apparent benefit.
C) It is valid only with guardian's permission.
D) It is valid for acts of righteousness.

Key Takeaway
A minor's deficient capacity (ahliyyah qasirah) determines the validity of his actions: agency requires guardian consent, will is void, and apostasy does not incur capital punishment.

Effect of Madness Duration on Makeup of Missed Prayers: The Hanafi Dispute
Explaining the effect of madness on salah makeup obligations with intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi intra-madhhab dispute between Imam Muhammad and the Two Shaykhs regarding the duration of madness that waives makeup of missed prayers, and apply the rule to a given scenario.

Core Idea
Makeup of missed prayers is waived only if madness covers more than five consecutive prayer times.

When a person becomes insane, the obligation to pray is lifted during the madness, but what about missed prayers after recovery? The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement based on how to measure the duration of madness: by counting prayer times or by day-and-night cycles. This lesson unpacks that dispute and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
Determine the exact point of dispute: under what condition does madness waive the obligation to make up missed prayers?
The core question is whether the duration is measured by the number of prayer times or by a full day and night cycle.
2
State each position
List the view of Imam Muhammad (count prayer times) and the view of the Two Shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) (consider the day-night period).
Imam Muhammad requires madness to cover six prayer times; the Two Shaykhs consider it sufficient if madness exceeds one day and night (about five prayers).
3
Examine the 'illa (cause)
Identify the underlying rationale (ta'lil) for each position. Imam Muhammad focuses on the number of obligatory prayers, while the Two Shaykhs focus on the continuity of the day-night cycle.
This difference in 'illa leads to different outcomes in borderline cases.
4
Apply to a concrete scenario
Work through the example from the text: a person becomes insane at noon today and recovers after noon tomorrow. Determine the ruling according to each view.
This scenario helps solidify the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).
5
Extract the usul principle
Consider how this dispute illustrates the Hanafi approach to ta'lil (causation) and the importance of precise definition of the 'illa in deriving rulings.
The dispute is not about the text but about the method of identifying the effective cause.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفيضُ الحجازي ۳۵۳ شرح اردو المنتخب الحسامي
ہیں، یعنی پانچ نمازوں سے بڑھ کر چھ نماز میں اس پر ہو جائے تو قضا ساقط ہو جائے گی ، اگر جنون پانچ نمازوں تک رہا، چھٹی نماز کے وقت میں جنون ختم ہو گیا، تو قضا ساقط نہ ہوگی ، اور شیخین رات دن سے بڑھنے کا لحاظ کرتے ہیں، لہذا ایک آدمی آج زوال سے مجنون ہوا اور دوسرے دن زوال کے بعد تک مجنون رہا تو شیخین کے نزدیک دن رات سے جنون بڑھ گیا لہذا نمازوں کی قضا نہ ہوگی ، امام محمد کے نزدیک چونکہ پانچ ہی نمازیں ہوئی ہیں، لہذا قضا واجب ہوگی ، ہاں اگر دوسرے دن کے عصر کا وقت بھی داخل ہو گیا تو چھ نمازیں ہوگئی اب قضا لازم نہ ہوگی، اور زکوۃ میں امتداد یہ ہے کہ پورا سال جنون کی حالت رہے، تو اس پر زکوۃ واجب نہ ہوگی، اور امام ابو یوسف نے آسانی کے لئے اکثر سال کوکل کے قائم مقام کیا ہے، لہذا اگر دس ماہ کے بعد جنون ختم ہو گیا تو طرفین کے نزدیک زکوۃ واجب ہوگی، کیونکہ پورے سال جنون نہیں ہے، اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک چونکہ اکثر سال جنون پایا گیا لہذا اس سال کی زکوۃ واجب نہ ہوگی۔ مصنف ع اللہ فرماتے ہیں کہ جو فعل ایسا حسن ہو کہ اس میں فتح کا احتمال نہ ہو جیسے ایمان یا ایسا فتیح ہو کہ اس میں حُسن کا احتمال نہ ہو جیسے کفر تو یہ چیزیں مجنون کے حق میں بھی ثابت ہوں گی ، لہذا اس کے ماں باپ کے تابع بنا کر مجنون کا ایمان اور ردت کا ثبوت ہو گا اگر اس کے والدین مومن ہیں تو مجنون بھی مومن ہوگا اور اگر اس کے والدین نعوذ باللہ مرتد ہو گئے تو مجنون بھی مرتد شمار کیا جائے گا کیونکہ بالقصد ایمان اور بالقصد روت کا صدور مجنون سے نہیں ہوسکتا لہذا اس کے حق میں ایمان تبعی اور ردت تنبعی کا اعتبار ہوگا۔
Al-Faiz al-Hijazi 353 Urdu commentary of al-Muntakhab al-Husami. They are: if it happens to him in more than five prayers, i.e., six prayers, then the makeup is dropped. If the madness lasted for five prayers and ended at the time of the sixth prayer, then the makeup is not dropped. The two Shaykhs consider the increase of night and day: thus if a person became insane today at noon and remained insane until after noon the next day, then according to the two Shaykhs the madness exceeded a day and night, so the makeup of prayers is not required. According to Imam Muhammad, since only five prayers occurred, makeup is obligatory. Yes, if the time of Asr of the next day also entered, then six prayers occurred, now makeup is not necessary. Regarding zakat, the continuance is that the state of madness lasts the entire year, then zakat is not obligatory upon him. Imam Abu Yusuf, for ease, has made the majority of the year equivalent to the whole. Thus if after ten months the madness ended, then according to both parties zakat is obligatory because the whole year is not [covered by] madness. But according to Imam Abu Yusuf, since the majority of the year was found with madness, zakat for that year is not obligatory. The author (may Allah have mercy on him) says: an act that is purely good such that there is no possibility of evil, like faith, or purely evil such that there is no possibility of good, like disbelief, these things will also be established for a mad person. Therefore, based on following his parents, the faith or apostasy of the mad person is established: if his parents are believers, then the mad person is also a believer; and if his parents (God forbid) become apostates, then the mad person is also considered an apostate, because intentional faith and intentional apostasy cannot occur from a mad person, so for him follow-up faith and follow-up apostasy are considered.
Source pages p. 354

Commentary
This passage discusses the rulings on madness (junun) as an impediment affecting obligations. It first addresses prayer (salah) makeup: if madness lasts for more than five prayers (i.e., six prayers), makeup is dropped; if exactly five prayers, makeup is still required. There is a dispute between the Two Shaykhs (Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf) who consider the duration of a day and night (24 hours), while Imam Muhammad counts the number of prayer times. For zakat, if madness covers the entire year, no zakat is due; but Imam Abu Yusuf relaxes this by considering the majority of the year as the whole year, so if madness persisted for more than six months, zakat is waived. Then the text establishes a principle: for acts that are either entirely good (like faith) or entirely evil (like apostasy), the mad person follows his parents in judgment, because he cannot perform these acts with intention. This is based on equity and parental guardianship in religious status.

Key Terms
جنون (junun): Madness or insanity that removes legal capacity (ahliyyah al-ada') for certain obligations when it persists beyond a duration.
قضاء (qada): Makeup of a missed obligatory act of worship performed after its prescribed time.
علة (illa): The effective cause that justifies a ruling in qiyas or ta'lil.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Two Shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), what condition must be met for the makeup of missed prayers to be waived due to madness?
A) Madness must cover exactly five prayer times.
B) Madness must cover a full day and night and extend into the next day.
C) Madness must cover the entire year.
D) Madness must cover more than six prayer times.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has internal divergence on whether to measure madness by prayer counts or by day-and-night unit for waiving makeup, reflecting different approaches to determining the 'illa.

Effect of Madness on Zakat Obligation: The Hanafi Dispute
Explaining the effect of madness on zakat obligation with intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on whether madness affects the obligation of zakat and apply the rule to a scenario where madness covers most of the year.

Core Idea
Zakat is obligatory unless madness covers the entire year; but Imam Abu Yusuf waives it if madness covers most of the year.

Zakat is a wealth-based obligation that requires full ownership of nisab throughout the year. Madness affects legal capacity but does it impact zakat? The Hanafi school has an internal dispute: the majority holds that zakat is still due unless insanity covers the whole year, while Imam Abu Yusuf provides a concession considering the majority of the year as equivalent to the whole. This lesson explores that dispute and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
The question is whether madness during the year affects the obligation to pay zakat at the end of the year.
Zakat requires complete ownership of nisab for the entire lunar year (hawl). Madness may break continuity.
2
State the positions
The Two Shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) say zakat is obligatory unless insanity covers the entire year. Imam Abu Yusuf says if insanity covers the majority of the year (more than six months), zakat is not obligatory.
The majority view is stricter; Abu Yusuf's is a concession for ease.
3
Examine the rationale
The Two Shaykhs consider that ownership remains intact during insanity, so the condition for zakat (full-year ownership) is satisfied. Abu Yusuf treats the majority as the whole, likening it to other cases where duration is considered.
Abu Yusuf uses istihsan (juristic preference) for ease.
4
Apply to a scenario
Take the example from the text: a person is insane for ten months of the year, then recovers. According to the Two Shaykhs, since the whole year is not covered by insanity, zakat is due. According to Abu Yusuf, since the majority of the year was insanity, no zakat is due.
Ten months is clearly the majority (over 6 months).
5
Derive the usul principle
This dispute illustrates the Hanafi principle of considering the prevailing condition (ghalaba) and using istihsan to avoid hardship.
Abu Yusuf's view is an application of the maxim 'al-mashaqqah tajlib al-taysir' (hardship begets ease).

Thus if after ten months the madness ended, then according to both parties zakat is obligatory because the whole year is not [covered by] madness. But according to Imam Abu Yusuf, since the majority of the year was found with madness, zakat for that year is not obligatory. The author (may Allah have mercy on him) says: an act that is purely good such that there is no possibility of evil, like faith, or purely evil such that there is no possibility of good, like disbelief, these things will also be established for a mad person. Therefore, based on following his parents, the faith or apostasy of the mad person is established: if his parents are believers, then the mad person is also a believer; and if his parents (God forbid) become apostates, then the mad person is also considered an apostate, because intentional faith and intentional apostasy cannot occur from a mad person, so for him follow-up faith and follow-up apostasy are considered.
Source pages p. 354

Commentary
This passage discusses the rulings on madness (junun) as an impediment affecting obligations. It first addresses prayer (salah) makeup: if madness lasts for more than five prayers (i.e., six prayers), makeup is dropped; if exactly five prayers, makeup is still required. There is a dispute between the Two Shaykhs (Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf) who consider the duration of a day and night (24 hours), while Imam Muhammad counts the number of prayer times. For zakat, if madness covers the entire year, no zakat is due; but Imam Abu Yusuf relaxes this by considering the majority of the year as the whole year, so if madness persisted for more than six months, zakat is waived. Then the text establishes a principle: for acts that are either entirely good (like faith) or entirely evil (like apostasy), the mad person follows his parents in judgment, because he cannot perform these acts with intention. This is based on equity and parental guardianship in religious status.

Key Terms
جنون (junun): Madness or insanity that removes legal capacity (ahliyyah al-ada') for certain obligations when it persists beyond a duration.
زكاة (zakat): Obligatory alms on wealth that meets nisab and completes one lunar year of ownership.
أكثر (akthar): Majority; more than half.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Two Shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), what condition must be met for zakat to be waived due to madness?
A) Madness must cover the majority of the year.
B) Madness must cover the entire year.
C) Madness must cover at least six months.
D) Madness always waives zakat regardless of duration.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school disagrees on whether insanity must cover the whole year or just the majority to waive zakat, reflecting a tension between strict conditionality and istihsan for ease.

Attribution of Faith and Apostasy to a Mad Person through Parental Status
Explaining the principle that a mad person's faith or apostasy follows his parents since he cannot intend such acts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi principle that a mad person's faith or apostasy is determined by his parents' status, and apply it to determine the legal status of a mad child.

Core Idea
A mad person's faith or apostasy follows his parents because he lacks the capacity for intentional belief or disbelief.

Faith (iman) and apostasy (riddah) are normally acts of intention (niyyah). Since a mad person cannot form such intentions, how do we determine his religious status? The Hanafi school establishes a principle: for purely good or purely evil acts, the mad person follows his parents. This lesson explains that principle and its application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal principle
The author states that acts which are purely good (like faith) or purely evil (like apostasy) are established for a mad person based on parental status.
Purely good and purely evil acts cannot be partially good/evil; they are defined by their essential nature.
2
Understand the rationale
A mad person cannot intentionally perform these acts (intention is a requirement for accountability). Therefore, their status is determined by following (taba'iyyah) the parents.
This is based on the principle that a child's legal status in such matters is derived from the parents.
3
Apply to scenarios
If parents are Muslim, the mad child is considered Muslim. If parents become apostates (God forbid), the child is also considered an apostate.
This has implications for inheritance, marriage, and burial rites.
4
Distinguish from other rulings
This principle applies only to acts that are unambiguously good or evil. For acts that can be mixed (like transactions), the mad person is not held accountable.
The text contrasts with the earlier discussion on worship obligations, where madness can waive liability.
5
Extract the usul maxim
The underlying maxim is that followership (taba'iyyah) applies in matters that cannot be initiated by the person himself due to incapacity.
This is similar to the status of minors in determining religion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفيضُ الحجازي ۳۵۳ شرح اردو المنتخب الحسامي
ہیں، یعنی پانچ نمازوں سے بڑھ کر چھ نماز میں اس پر ہو جائے تو قضا ساقط ہو جائے گی ، اگر جنون پانچ نمازوں تک رہا، چھٹی نماز کے وقت میں جنون ختم ہو گیا، تو قضا ساقط نہ ہوگی ، اور شیخین رات دن سے بڑھنے کا لحاظ کرتے ہیں، لہذا ایک آدمی آج زوال سے مجنون ہوا اور دوسرے دن زوال کے بعد تک مجنون رہا تو شیخین کے نزدیک دن رات سے جنون بڑھ گیا لہذا نمازوں کی قضا نہ ہوگی ، امام محمد کے نزدیک چونکہ پانچ ہی نمازیں ہوئی ہیں، لہذا قضا واجب ہوگی ، ہاں اگر دوسرے دن کے عصر کا وقت بھی داخل ہو گیا تو چھ نمازیں ہوگئی اب قضا لازم نہ ہوگی، اور زکوۃ میں امتداد یہ ہے کہ پورا سال جنون کی حالت رہے، تو اس پر زکوۃ واجب نہ ہوگی، اور امام ابو یوسف نے آسانی کے لئے اکثر سال کوکل کے قائم مقام کیا ہے، لہذا اگر دس ماہ کے بعد جنون ختم ہو گیا تو طرفین کے نزدیک زکوۃ واجب ہوگی، کیونکہ پورے سال جنون نہیں ہے، اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک چونکہ اکثر سال جنون پایا گیا لہذا اس سال کی زکوۃ واجب نہ ہوگی۔ مصنف ع اللہ فرماتے ہیں کہ جو فعل ایسا حسن ہو کہ اس میں فتح کا احتمال نہ ہو جیسے ایمان یا ایسا فتیح ہو کہ اس میں حُسن کا احتمال نہ ہو جیسے کفر تو یہ چیزیں مجنون کے حق میں بھی ثابت ہوں گی ، لہذا اس کے ماں باپ کے تابع بنا کر مجنون کا ایمان اور ردت کا ثبوت ہو گا اگر اس کے والدین مومن ہیں تو مجنون بھی مومن ہوگا اور اگر اس کے والدین نعوذ باللہ مرتد ہو گئے تو مجنون بھی مرتد شمار کیا جائے گا کیونکہ بالقصد ایمان اور بالقصد روت کا صدور مجنون سے نہیں ہوسکتا لہذا اس کے حق میں ایمان تبعی اور ردت تنبعی کا اعتبار ہوگا۔
Al-Faiz al-Hijazi 353 Urdu commentary of al-Muntakhab al-Husami. They are: if it happens to him in more than five prayers, i.e., six prayers, then the makeup is dropped. If the madness lasted for five prayers and ended at the time of the sixth prayer, then the makeup is not dropped. The two Shaykhs consider the increase of night and day: thus if a person became insane today at noon and remained insane until after noon the next day, then according to the two Shaykhs the madness exceeded a day and night, so the makeup of prayers is not required. According to Imam Muhammad, since only five prayers occurred, makeup is obligatory. Yes, if the time of Asr of the next day also entered, then six prayers occurred, now makeup is not necessary. Regarding zakat, the continuance is that the state of madness lasts the entire year, then zakat is not obligatory upon him. Imam Abu Yusuf, for ease, has made the majority of the year equivalent to the whole. Thus if after ten months the madness ended, then according to both parties zakat is obligatory because the whole year is not [covered by] madness. But according to Imam Abu Yusuf, since the majority of the year was found with madness, zakat for that year is not obligatory. The author (may Allah have mercy on him) says: an act that is purely good such that there is no possibility of evil, like faith, or purely evil such that there is no possibility of good, like disbelief, these things will also be established for a mad person. Therefore, based on following his parents, the faith or apostasy of the mad person is established: if his parents are believers, then the mad person is also a believer; and if his parents (God forbid) become apostates, then the mad person is also considered an apostate, because intentional faith and intentional apostasy cannot occur from a mad person, so for him follow-up faith and follow-up apostasy are considered.

Commentary
This passage discusses the rulings on madness (junun) as an impediment affecting obligations. It first addresses prayer (salah) makeup: if madness lasts for more than five prayers (i.e., six prayers), makeup is dropped; if exactly five prayers, makeup is still required. This is based on equity and parental guardianship in religious status.

Key Terms
جنون (junun): Madness or insanity that removes legal capacity (ahliyyah al-ada') for certain obligations when it persists beyond a duration.
تبعية (taba'iyyah): Following; legal followership where a person's status is derived from another (e.g., parent).
الإيمان التبعي (al-iman al-taba'i): Follow-up faith: faith attributed to a person not through his own intention but through followership of parents.
