The Divisibility of Emancipation: Abu Hanifa vs. the Sahibayn
Usul dispute on divisibility of itq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute on the divisibility of emancipation and apply the principle of causality (ta'lil) to distinguish between cause and effect in usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Emancipation removes ownership (divisible), not freedom itself (indivisible) — Abu Hanifa's key distinction.

This passage from Al-Faiz-ul-Hijaz presents a fundamental dispute in Hanafi usul: can the act of emancipating a slave be partial, or must it be a single indivisible act? The disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two chief disciples turns on whether the essence of emancipation is the removal of ownership (izalat al-milk) or the conferral of freedom (itq). Understanding this distinction is critical for grasping how Hanafi jurists define acts and their effects.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed concept
Recognise that the dispute concerns whether the act of emancipation (itq/‘itaq) is divisible (mutajazzi) or indivisible (ghayr mutajazzi).
The effect (freedom) is agreed to be indivisible; the disagreement is about the act itself.
2
Contrast the two positions
State Abu Hanifa's view (itq is divisible because it is removal of ownership) and the Sahibayn's view (itq is indivisible because it aims at establishing freedom).
Both positions rely on a definition of what itq essentially means.
3
Examine each side's definition of the cause
Identify how each side defines the cause (mu'aththir) of emancipation: removal of ownership vs. conferral of freedom.
The definition determines divisibility: ownership is divisible, freedom is not.
4
Follow the analogies
Analyse the qiyas provided: wudu limbs (divisible cause) lead to prayer permissibility (indivisible effect); divorce numbers (divisible) lead to severe prohibition (indivisible).
These analogies support Abu Hanifa's position that a divisible cause can have an indivisible effect.
5
Determine the practical consequence
Work out the thamarah al-khilaf: what happens if a master says 'half of you is free' according to each view.
Sahibayn: no freedom; Abu Hanifa: ownership removed but freedom suspended until full removal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَعْض حِصَّہ ساقِط ہو گیا تو عَلَّت کا نِصف حِصَّہ پایا گیا، پس عِتْق عَلَّت کی تَکمِیل تک مَوقُوف رہے گا اور یہ (اِسقاطِ مِلک) ایسا ہو گیا جیسے اَعضاء کا غُسل (عِلَّت ہے) نماز کی اَدائیگی کی اِباحَت کے لِئے، اور جیسے طلاق کے اَعداد (عِلَّت ہیں) تَحریم کے لِئے، اور یہ رِقّیَّت مال کی مِلکِیَّت کے مُنافی ہے مال ہونے کی حیثیت سے مَملُوکِیَّت کے قائِم مَقام ہونے کی وَجہ سے، یہاں تک کہ غُلام اور مُکاتَب (جِماع کے لِئے) تِسَتری (باندی رکھنے) کے مالِک نہ ہوں گے، اور ان دونوں کی جانب سے اسلام کا فریضہ حج صَحیح نہ ہوگا اَصل قُدرَت کے نہ ہونے کی وَجہ سے، اور قُدرَت وہ مَنافِع بدنیہ ہیں، اس لئے کہ مَنافِع آقا کے لئے ہیں، مگر ان بدنی عبادات میں جن کا اِستِثنا کر دیا گیا۔
تَشریح:- ساتواں عارِض رِقّیَّت (غُلام ہونا) ہے، رِقّیَّت ایک عَجز حُکمی ہے، یعنی غُلام بِحُکم شَرع عاجِز و مَجْبُور ہے، کِسی طرح کے تَصرُّفات کا مالِک نہیں ہے، غُلامی اِبتِدا اور اَصل وضع میں کُفر کی سزا ہے اور اللہ تَعَالٰی کا حق ہے، یعنی کفَّار نے اللہ تَعَالٰی کی عبادت اور غُلامی کو باعِث عار سمجھا تو اس کی پاداش میں اللہ تَعَالٰی نے ان کو اپنے غُلاموں (مسلمانوں) کا غُلام بنا دِیا، بہر حال غُلامی اِبتِدا چونکہ کُفر کی سزا ہے، اس لئے صِرف کُفَّار پر ثابت ہوتی ہے، مسلمانوں پر اِبتِدا رِقّیَّت ثابت نہیں ہو سکتی لیکن رِقّیَّت بقاء حق العبد ہے اور ایک حُکمی امر ہے یعنی سزا کے مَعنی کی رِعایَت کِئے بغیر شَرِیعَت کے دیگر اَحکام کی طرح یہ بھی محض ایک حُکم شَرعی کے طور پر جاری ہوتی ہے، اس غُلامی کے سبب آدمی ذِلَّت اور تَمَلُّک کا نِشانہ بنا رہتا ہے، حتی کہ غُلام اگر مسلمان بھی ہو گیا تب بھی وہ غُلام ہی رہے گا، جیسے خراج اِبتِدا مسلمان پر ثابت نہیں ہوتا، البتہ بقاءً ثابت ہوتا ہے، یعنی خراجی زمین خریدی تو خراج علی حالہ باقی رہے گا۔
رِقّیَّت ایک ایسا وصف ہے جس میں تَجَزِّی نہیں ہوتی، لہٰذا ایسا نہیں ہو سکتا ہے کہ انسان کا بعض حِصَّہ غُلام ہو، اور بعض حِصَّہ آزاد ہو، کیونکہ رِقّیَّت کُفر کی سزا ہے، اور کُفر میں تَجَزِّی نہیں ہے، ایسے ہی رِقّیَّت حق اللہ ہے، اور اللہ کے حق میں تَجَزِّی نہیں ہوتی ہے، البتہ رِقّیَّت پر جو مِلک مُرَتَّب ہوتی ہے یہ حق العبد ہے، اس میں تَجَزِّی ہوتی ہے، لہٰذا ایک غُلام کے آدھے آدھے حِصَّے کے دو آدمی مالِک ہو سکتے ہیں، آدمی اپنے غُلام کے نِصف حِصَّہ کو بیچ سکتا ہے۔ مُصَنِّف رِقّیَّت کے غَیر مُتَجَزِّی ہونے پر جامع کبیر کا ایک جُزئیہ پیش کرتے ہیں کہ اگر کوئی مَجْہُول النَّسب غُلام اِقرار کرے کہ اس کا نِصف حِصَّہ فلاں کا غُلام ہے، تو اگر یہ فلاں کی مِلکیت تو نِصف میں ثابت ہوگی، مگر غُلام شَہَادَت اور دیگر اَحکام میں کامل غُلام شمار کِیا جائے گا، ایسا نہ ہوگا کہ آدھا غُلام نہیں ہے، کیونکہ رِقّیَّت میں تَجَزِّی نہیں ہے، اور مِلک میں تَجَزِّی ہے، اس لئے مُقِرَّہ کے لئے نِصف حِصَّہ میں مِلک ثابت ہوگی۔ پھر جس طرح رِقّیَّت میں تَجَزِّی نہیں ہے، ایسے ہی عِتْق جو اس کی ضد ہے اس میں بھی تَجَزِّی نہیں ہے، لہٰذا بعض حِصَّہ آزاد ہو بعض حِصَّہ آزاد نہ ہوا ایسا نہیں ہو سکتا، اور صاحِبَین کے نزدیک اعْتاق میں بھی تَجَزِّی نہیں ہوتی، کیونکہ اعْتاق کہتے ہیں عِتْق ثابت کرنے کو، تو عِتْق اعْتاق کا اثر ہے، اور اثر یعنی عِتْق میں تَجَزِّی نہیں ہے، تو مُؤَثِّر یعنی اعْتاق میں بھی تَجَزِّی نہیں ہے۔ وَقَالَ أَبُو حَنِيْفَةَ: امام ابو حنیفہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اعْتاق میں تَجَزِّی ہوتی ہے، اگر چہ عِتْق میں تَجَزِّی نہیں ہے، اور دلیل یہ ہے کہ اعْتاق کہتے ہیں اِزالہ مِلک کو، اعْتاق رِقّیَّت کو ساقِط کرنے یا آزادی کو ثابت کرنے کا نام نہیں ہے، کیونکہ رِقّیَّت اور آزادی یہ اللہ کا حق ہے، اس میں بندہ کو تَصَرُّف کا کوئی حق نہیں ہے، کہ وہ رِقّیَّت کو ساقِط کرے یا آزادی کو ثابت کرے، بندہ صرف اپنے حق میں تَصَرُّف کر سکتا ہے اور مِلک اس کا حق ہے، تو جب بندہ اعْتاق کرے گا تو اس کا مطلب ہوا اِزالہ مِلک کرنا اور مِلک میں بِالاِتِّفاق تَجَزِّی ہے، تو اِزالہ مِلک میں بھی تَجَزِّی ہوگی، اَلغَرَض اعْتاق نام ہے مِلک زائل کرنے کا، یہ الگ بات ہے کہ اِزالہ مِلک کے نتیجہ میں رِقّیَّت زائل ہو جاتی ہے، اور زَوالِ رِقّیَّت کے واسطہ سے بالآخر عِتْق ثابت ہو جاتا ہے۔
بہر حال اعْتاق مِلک مُتَجَزِّی کو زائل کرنے کا نام ہے، (جس کے نتیجہ میں اس کے ساتھ عِتْق کا حُکم مُتعلِّق ہو جائے گا، یعنی مِلک زائل کرنے سے عِتْق کا ثبوت ہو جائے گا) مگر اس اِزالہ مِلک کے ساتھ جو حُکم عِتْق مُتعلِّق ہو گا وہ پوری مِلک کے ساقِط ہونے کے ساتھ مُتعلِّق ہوگا یعنی اِزالہ مِلک میں مِلک اگر چہ مُتَجَزِّی ہے مگر اس پر عِتْق جو غَیر مُتَجَزِّی ہے وہ اس وقت ثابت ہوگا جب غُلام سے پوری مِلک زائل ہو جائے، پس اگر کسی نے آدھا غُلام آزاد کیا یعنی نِصف مِلک کو زائل کیا تو عِتْق ثابت نہ ہوگا کیونکہ عِتْق کی عِلَّت پوری مِلک کو زائل کرنا ہے، اور یہاں آدھی عِلَّت پائی گئی، لہٰذا یہ نِصف عِلَّت تَکمیلِ عِلَّت تک مَوقُوف رہے گی اور جب عِلَّت مکمل ہو جائے گی یعنی پوری مِلک زائل ہو جائے گی تو عِتْق ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ مُصَنِّف کہتے ہیں کہ مِلک مُتَجَزِّی کے اِزالہ کا عِلَّت ہونا عِتْق غَیر مُتَجَزِّی کے لئے، یہ ایسا ہی ہے جیسے اَعضاءِ وُضو کا دھونا (جو تَجَزِّی ہے) عِلَّت ہے اِباحَتِ صلوۃ کے لئے (جو غَیر مُتَجَزِّی ہے) پس اگر کسی نے چہرہ یا ہاتھ دھوئے تو طَہارَت ثابت ہو جائے گی مگر اِباحَتِ صلوۃ ابھی نہ ہوگا (یعنی ابھی نماز نہیں پڑھ سکتا) اِباحَتِ صلوۃ کامل طَہارَت پر ہوگی اور وہ پورا وُضو ہے، تو یہاں عِلَّت یعنی غُسلِ اَعضاءِ وُضو مُتَجَزِّی ہے، اور حُکم یعنی اِباحَتِ صلوۃ غَیر مُتَجَزِّی ہے۔ اسی طرح جیسے اعدادِ طلاق میں تَجَزِّی ہے، ایک طلاق بھی ہو سکتی ہے، دو بھی اور تین بھی، مگر اس کا حُکم حُرمت غلیظہ یہ غَیر مُتَجَزِّی ہے، یعنی حُرمت غلیظہ مکمل تین طلاق سے ہوگی، اسی طرح اعْتاق میں جو اِزالہ مِلک ہے اس میں تَجَزِّی ہے مگر اس کا جو حُکم عِتْق ہے وہ غَیر مُتَجَزِّی ہے، جو مِلک کے کامل اِزالہ کے بغیر ثابت نہ ہوگا۔
خُلاصہ کلام یہ ہوا کہ صاحِبَین کے نزدیک اعْتاق کا مقصد اصلی اثباتِ عِتْق ہے، اور اِزالہ مِلک ضِمنًا ہے، اس لئے
If a part is dropped, then half of the cause is found, so emancipation will be suspended until the completion of the cause. This (removal of ownership) is like washing the limbs (which is a cause) for the permissibility of performing prayer, and like the numbers of divorce (are causes) for prohibition. And this slavery is contrary to ownership of property because it stands in place of being owned as property, to the extent that a slave and a mukatab will not own a female slave (for intercourse), and from both of them the obligatory Hajj of Islam will not be valid due to lack of actual capacity, and capacity is bodily benefits, because benefits are for the master, except in those bodily acts of worship that are exempted. Explanation: The seventh obstacle is slavery. Slavery is a legal incapacity, meaning the slave is legally incapable and compelled, he does not own any type of disposition. Slavery initially and in its original establishment is a punishment for disbelief and a right of Allah, i.e. the disbelievers considered worship of Allah and servitude a disgrace, so as punishment Allah made them slaves of His own slaves (Muslims). In any case, since slavery initially is a punishment for disbelief, it is only established upon disbelievers; it cannot be established upon Muslims initially. But slavery by continuation is a right of the slave and a legal matter, i.e., without considering the meaning of punishment, it continues as a mere legal ruling like other rulings of Shariah. Due to this slavery, a person remains subject to humiliation and ownership, even if the slave becomes Muslim he will remain a slave, just as kharaj is not established upon a Muslim initially but is established by continuation, i.e., if one buys kharaj land, the kharaj remains as it was. Slavery is an attribute that is not divisible, so it is not possible that part of a person is slave and part free, because slavery is a punishment for disbelief and disbelief is not divisible; similarly slavery is a right of Allah, and Allah's right is not divisible. However, the ownership that is attached to slavery is a right of the slave, and it is divisible, so two persons can own half shares of a slave, and a person can sell half of his slave. The author presents a case from al-Jami' al-Kabir on slavery being indivisible: if a slave of unknown lineage confesses that half of him is the slave of so-and-so, then ownership of that half will be established for that person, but in testimony and other rulings the slave will be considered a complete slave; it will not be that he is half slave, because slavery is not divisible and ownership is divisible, so ownership is established in half for the confessor. Then just as slavery is not divisible, likewise emancipation which is its opposite is also not divisible, so it is not possible that some part is free and some not. And according to the Two Companions, emancipation is also not divisible, because emancipation means establishing freedom, so freedom is the effect of emancipation, and the effect (freedom) is not divisible, so the cause (emancipation) is also not divisible. Abu Hanifa said: Imam Abu Hanifa says that emancipation is divisible, although freedom is not divisible. The proof is that emancipation means removal of ownership; it is not called removing slavery or establishing freedom, because slavery and freedom are rights of Allah, in which the slave has no right to dispose. The slave can only dispose in his own right, and ownership is his right. So when a slave emancipates, it means removal of ownership, and ownership is unanimously divisible, so removal of ownership is also divisible. In short, emancipation is the name of removing ownership; it is another matter that as a result of removing ownership, slavery is removed, and through removal of slavery eventually freedom is established. In any case, emancipation is removing divisible ownership (as a result of which the ruling of freedom becomes attached to it, i.e., from removing ownership, freedom is established). But the ruling of freedom that becomes attached to this removal of ownership is attached only when full ownership is removed. That is, in removal of ownership, although ownership is divisible, the freedom which is indivisible will only be established when all ownership from the slave is removed. So if someone frees half a slave, i.e., removes half ownership, freedom will not be established because the cause of freedom is removing all ownership, and here half the cause is found. Therefore this half cause will be suspended until completion of the cause, and when the cause is completed, i.e., all ownership is removed, then freedom is established. The author says that the removal of divisible ownership being a cause for indivisible freedom is like washing the limbs of wudu (which is divisible) being a cause for permissibility of prayer (which is indivisible). So if someone washes his face or hands, purification is established but permissibility of prayer is not yet (he cannot pray). Permissibility of prayer is upon complete purification, which is full wudu. So here the cause (washing limbs of wudu) is divisible, and the ruling (permissibility of prayer) is indivisible. Similarly, just as the numbers of divorce are divisible (one, two, three divorces can be given), but its ruling of severe prohibition (hurmah ghalizah) is indivisible, i.e., severe prohibition occurs only with three complete divorces, similarly in emancipation, the removal of ownership is divisible, but its ruling of freedom is indivisible, which will not be established without complete removal of ownership. The conclusion is that according to the Two Companions, the main purpose of emancipation is to establish freedom, and removal of ownership is incidental, therefore...
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage from Al-Faiz-ul-Hijaz (Urdu Sharh of Al-Muntakhab Al-Husami) discusses the seventh obstacle to full legal capacity: slavery (riqq). The author clarifies that riqq is a legal incapacity (ajz hukmi) that prevents the slave from having full rights, originally a punishment for disbelief, but it persists as a legal status even after embracing Islam. The key principle is that riqq is indivisible (ghayr mutajazzi)—a person cannot be partially slave and partially free—because it is a divine punishment and a right of Allah. However, ownership (milk) over a slave is divisible, so two people can co-own a slave. The text then presents a dispute (ikhtilaf) between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the nature of emancipation (itq/‘itaq). The Sahibayn argue that itq is indivisible because its result (freedom) is indivisible, applying the principle that the cause inherits the characteristics of the effect. Imam Abu Hanifa counters that itq is not about directly establishing freedom; rather, it is the removal of ownership (izalat al-milk). Since ownership is divisible, the act of removing ownership is also divisible. However, he acknowledges that the legal effect (freedom) is not achieved until the entire ownership is removed. This is illustrated through analogical reasoning (qiyas) with wudu: washing individual limbs (divisible cause) does not grant permission to pray until the full wudu is completed (indivisible effect). Similarly, individual divorces (divisible cause) do not produce the severe prohibition of remarriage until three are pronounced (indivisible effect). The passage thus exemplifies how Hanafi usul uses causal reasoning and analogy to resolve differences within the madhhab. The authority weight of the positions: the Sahibayn's view is from Zahir al-Riwayah, while Abu Hanifa's is also foundational; however, the relied-upon fatwa (al-mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is that emancipation is indivisible (the Sahibayn's position), as it aligns with the principle that effects determine the nature of causes in matters of divine rights.

Key Terms
رِقّیَّت (riqqiyyah): A legal incapacity that renders a person unable to own property or act independently; originally a punishment for disbelief, it continues as a legal status.
عِتْق (itq): Freedom/emancipation; the legal effect of removing ownership from a slave, resulting in freedom.
تَجَزِّی (tajazzi): Divisibility; the capacity to be divided into parts.
اِزالہ مِلک (izalat al-milk): Removal of ownership; the act of relinquishing one's right to a slave, which is deemed the essence of emancipation according to Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is the essence of emancipation (itq)?
A) Establishing freedom by divine right
B) Removing ownership from the slave
C) Cancelling the punishment of disbelief
D) Making the slave a free Muslim

Key Takeaway
Emancipation is the removal of ownership, which is divisible; the resulting freedom is indivisible and occurs only upon complete removal.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
Divisibility of Emancipation: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Explains the disagreement over whether 'itq' is divisible in its cause.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi debate on tajazzi al-itq and apply the qiyas with wudu to distinguish between divisible causes and indivisible effects.

Core Idea
Emancipation is removal of ownership (divisible), not establishment of freedom (indivisible).

This passage examines a key intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions, the Sahibayn, on whether emancipation (itq) is divisible in its cause. The disagreement hinges on how 'itq' is defined—whether it is primarily the removal of ownership (which is divisible) or the establishment of freedom (which is indivisible). Understanding this debate sharpens your ability to analyze cause-effect relationships in usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disagreement
State the core question: Is emancipation (itq) divisible (tajazzi) in its cause? That is, can a person partially free a slave with legal effect?
The dispute is about the nature of the cause, not the effect.
2
State the Sahibayn's position
The Sahibayn hold that itq is indivisible because its primary objective is establishing freedom, which is indivisible. Therefore, the cause must also be indivisible.
They reason that an indivisible effect cannot arise from a divisible cause.
3
State Imam Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa defines itq as removal of ownership (izalat al-milk). Since ownership is divisible by consensus, removal of ownership is also divisible. The effect (freedom) is indivisible but arises only upon completion of the cause.
He distinguishes between the cause and its completion; partial removal is a valid but incomplete cause.
4
Analyze the analogies
Abu Hanifa supports his view with analogies: wudu (washing limbs is divisible, permissibility of prayer is indivisible) and divorce (numbers divisible, irrevocable prohibition indivisible). In both, a divisible cause leads to an indivisible effect upon completion.
The analogy highlights that the effect is not tied to partial cause but to complete cause.
5
Extract the practical difference
If someone frees half of his slave: according to Abu Hanifa, the act is valid as a partial removal of ownership, and freedom is established when the remaining half is freed. According to the Sahibayn, the act is invalid because partial freedom is impossible.
This difference (thamarah al-khilaf) shows the real-world impact of the theoretical debate.

Source Text

کہتے ہیں عشق ثابت کرنے کو تو عنق اعتقاق کا اثر ہے، اور اثر یعنی عشق میں تجربی نہیں ہے، تو مؤثر یعنی اعتاق میں بھی تجربی نہیں ہے۔ وقال ابو حنيفة : - امام ابو حنیفہ اللہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اعتاق میں تجزی ہوتی ہے ، اگر چہ عشق میں تجری نہیں ہے، اور دلیل یہ ہے کہ اعتاق کہتے ہیں ازالہ ملک کو ، اعتاق رقیت کو ساقط کرنے یا آزادی کو ثابت کرنے کا نام نہیں ہے، کیونکہ رقیت اور آزادی یہ اللہ کا حق ہے ، اس میں بندہ کو تصرف کا کوئی حق نہیں ہے ، کہ وہ رقیت کو ساقط کرے یا آزادی کو ثابت کرے، بندہ صرف اپنے حق میں تصرف کر سکتا ہے اور ملک اس کا حق ہے ، تو جب بندہ اعتاق کرے گا تو اس کا مطلب ہوا ازالہ ملک کرنا اور ملک میں بالاتفاق تجری ہے، تو ازالہ ملک میں بھی تجربی ہوگی ، الغرض اعتناق نام ہے ملک زائل کرنے کا، یہ الگ بات ہے کہ ازالہ ملک کے نتیجہ میں رقیت زائل ہو جاتی ہے، اور زوال رقیت کے واسطہ سے بالاخر عشق ثابت ہو جاتا ہے۔
بہر حال اعتاق ملک متجری کو زائل کرنے کا نام ہے، ( جس کے نتیجہ میں اس کے ساتھ عشق کا حکم متعلق ہو جائے گا، یعنی ملک زائل کرنے سے عشق کا ثبوت ہو جائے گا ) مگر اس ازالہ ملک کے ساتھ جو حکم عتق متعلق ہو گا وہ پوری ملک کے ساقط ہونے کے ساتھ متعلق ہوگا یعنی ازالہ ملک میں ملک اگر چہ متجری ہے مگر اس پر عتق جو غیر متجری ہے وہ اس وقت ثابت ہوگا جب غلام سے پوری ملک زائل ہو جائے ، پس اگر کسی نے آدھا غلام آزاد کیا یعنی نصف ملک کو زائل کیا تو عتق ثابت نہ ہوگا کیونکہ عشق کی علت پوری ملک کو زائل کرنا ہے، اور یہاں آدھی علت پائی گئی ، لہذا یہ نصف علت تکمیل علت تک موقوف رہے گی اور جب علت مکمل ہو جائے گی یعنی پوری ملک زائل ہو جائے گی تو عتق ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ مصنف کہتے ہیں کہ ملک متجزی کے ازالہ کا علت ہو نا عتق غیر منتجوی کے لئے، یہ ایسا ہی ہے جیسے اعضاء وضو کا دھونا ( جو تجری ہے) علت ہے اباحت صلوۃ کے لئے ( جو غیر متجری ہے) پس اگر کسی نے چہرہ یا ہاتھ دھوئے تو طہارت ثابت ہو جائے گی مگر اباحت صلوۃ ابھی نہ ہوگا (یعنی ابھی نماز نہیں پڑھ سکتا ) اباحت صلوۃ کامل طہارت پر ہوگی اور وہ پورا وضو ہے، تو یہاں علت یعنی غسل اعضاء وضو متجری ہے، اور حکم یعنی اباحت صلوۃ غیر متجری ہے۔ اسی طرح جیسے اعداد طلاق میں تجزی ہے، ایک طلاق بھی ہو سکتی ہے ، دو بھی اور تین بھی ،مگر اس کا حکم حرمت غلیظہ یہ غیر متجری ہے، یعنی حرمت غلیظہ مکمل تین طلاق سے ہوگی ، اسی طرح اعتاق میں جو ازالہ ملک ہے اس میں تجربی ہے مگر اس کا جو حکم عشق ہے وہ غیر متجری ہے، جو ملک کے کامل ازالہ کے بغیر ثابت نہ ہوگا۔
خلاصہ کلام یہ ہوا کہ صاحبین کے نزدیک اعتناق کا مقصد اصلی اثبات عشق ہے، اور ازالہ ملک ضمنا ہے، اس لئے
ان کے نزدیک اعتاق میں تجری نہیں ہے اور امام صاحب کے نزدیک اعتاق در حقیقت ازالہ ملک کا نام ہے، اور اثبات عشق ضمناً ہورہا ہے، اس لئے امام صاحب کے نزدیک اعتاق میں تجزی ہے۔
They say that for establishing freedom, 'itq' is the cause, and the effect (freedom) is not divisible; therefore the cause (emancipation) is also not divisible. Abu Hanifa said: Imam Abu Hanifa states that emancipation is divisible, even if freedom is not. The proof is that 'itq' refers to the removal of ownership; it is not called nullifying slavery or establishing freedom, because slavery and freedom are rights of Allah, in which the slave has no right to intervene. The slave can only act within his own right, and ownership is his right. So when the slave emancipates, it means removing ownership, and ownership is unanimously divisible. Therefore removal of ownership is also divisible. In short, 'itq' is the name for removing ownership; it is separate that as a result of removing ownership, slavery is removed, and through removal of slavery, freedom is ultimately established. So emancipation is the removal of divisible ownership (which results in the ruling of freedom being attached to it, i.e., freedom is established by removing ownership). However, the ruling of freedom attached to this removal of ownership is connected to the removal of complete ownership. So in removal of ownership, even though ownership is divisible, freedom (which is indivisible) will be established only when complete ownership is removed from the slave. So if someone freed half a slave, i.e., removed half the ownership, freedom is not established because the cause of freedom is removing all ownership, and here half the cause is found. Therefore this half of the cause will pause until the cause is completed, and when the cause is completed (all ownership removed), freedom is established. The author says that the removal of divisible ownership being the cause for indivisible freedom is like washing the limbs of wudu (which is divisible) being the cause for permissibility of prayer (which is indivisible). So if someone washes his face or hands, purification is established but permissibility of prayer is not yet (cannot pray). Permissibility of prayer depends on complete purification, which is the full wudu. So here the cause (washing limbs) is divisible, and the ruling (permissibility of prayer) is indivisible. Similarly, divorce numbers are divisible (one, two, or three), but its ruling of irrevocable prohibition (hurmat al-ghaliza) is indivisible, occurring only with three divorces. Likewise, in emancipation, removal of ownership is divisible, but the ruling of freedom is indivisible, not established without complete removal of ownership. In summary, according to the Sahibayn, the primary objective of 'itq' is establishing freedom, and removal of ownership is incidental, so in their view emancipation is not divisible. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, 'itq' in reality is the removal of ownership, and establishing freedom is incidental, so in his view emancipation is divisible.
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage is a dispute (ikhtilaf) in usul al-fiqh between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the nature of emancipation ('itq). The question is whether 'itq' is divisible (mutajazzi) or indivisible. The Sahibayn argue that since the effect (freedom) is indivisible, the cause must also be indivisible. Imam Abu Hanifa counters that 'itq' is defined as the removal of ownership (izalat al-milk), and ownership is divisible by consensus. Thus, the removal of ownership is also divisible. The ruling of freedom, however, is indivisible and depends on complete removal of ownership. So partial emancipation (e.g., freeing half a slave) does not produce freedom immediately; rather, it pauses the process, and freedom is established when the remaining ownership is removed. The author likens this to wudu: washing limbs is divisible, but the permissibility of prayer depends on complete wudu. Similarly, divorce numbers are divisible, but irrevocable prohibition requires three divorces. This dispute has practical implications: according to Imam Abu Hanifa, if someone frees half his slave, the slave becomes partially free only upon full emancipation, whereas the Sahibayn hold that partial freedom is impossible, so the act is invalid. The commentary follows the author's order, first presenting the Sahibayn's position, then Abu Hanifa's with analogical proofs, and finally the conclusion.

Key Terms
تجزی (tajazzi): Divisibility of a cause or action into parts; here, whether emancipation can be performed partially.
اعتاق (itq): Emancipation of a slave, which is the removal of ownership by the master.
علت (illah): Cause or effective reason for a ruling; here, the removal of ownership is the cause for freedom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is the true nature of 'itq' (emancipation)?
A) Establishing freedom
B) Nullifying slavery
C) Removal of ownership
D) A combination of removing ownership and establishing freedom

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a divisible cause can produce an indivisible effect upon completion, as shown by Abu Hanifa's redefinition of itq.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

The Principle of a Slave's Valid Actions: First Self-Affecting Rule
Establishes usul rule for slave's capacity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that a slave's actions are valid when they first affect himself and apply it to iqrar, aman, and testimony cases.

Core Idea
A slave's act is valid if it first imposes an obligation on him before affecting his master.

The Sharh al-Husami presents a key usul principle resolving an apparent paradox: a slave lacks general guardianship (wilayah), yet certain actions like granting aman or confessing to theft are accepted. The resolution is that such actions first impose an obligation on the slave himself; secondary effects on others are incidental. This principle is then applied to iqrar (confession), testimony, and unintended crimes, with an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the ma'jur slave's theft confession.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Rule
State the basic Hanafi rule: a slave has no wilayah (guardianship) over others – cannot marry, judge, or testify in a representative capacity. This is the default.
The rule is based on the slave's limited legal capacity (ahliyyah).
2
Recognize the Apparent Counterexample
Consider the case of a slave authorized for jihad giving aman to an enemy. This seems like an act of wilayah. Extract why it is valid: the slave first secures his own right to spoils, so the action primarily affects himself.
The text uses this to introduce the qualification.
3
Extract the Qualification Principle
From the counterexample, derive the principle: an action of a slave is valid if it first imposes an obligation on him or affects his own right, and only secondarily affects others (e.g., the master).
The principle is qiyas-based, derived from the aman and testimony examples.
4
Apply to Iqrar Cases
Apply the principle to iqrar (confession): a slave's confession to hudud, qisas, or theft is valid because it primarily exposes him to hadd or liability, and the master's loss is secondary.
Distinguish between ma'dhun (authorized) and ma'jur (hired) slaves for theft.
5
Analyze the Ikhtilaf for Ma'jur Slave
Study the intra-Hanafi dispute on ma'jur slave's theft confession when master denies. Compare Abu Hanifa (both hadd and return), Abu Yusuf (hadd now, guarantee later), and Muhammad (neither now, guarantee later). Each reflects a different weighting of the principle.
The ikhtilaf shows the principle's boundaries.

Source Text

دوسروں پر بھی ولایت نہیں ہوسکتی ہے، لہذا غلام نہ کسی کا نکاح کر سکتا ہے، نہ قاضی بن سکتا ہے، نہ گواہ بن سکتا ہے۔ ایک سوال ہے کہ جب غلام سے ہر طرح کی ولایت منقطع ہے، تو عید ماذون فی الجہاد کے لئے کا فر کو امان دینا کیسے صحیح ہے جب کہ یہ بھی ایک ولایت ہے، کیونکہ وہ کافر مسلمانوں کا غلام بنے گا اور اس کا مال غنیمت ہوگا، مگر اس کو امان دیگر اس پر مسلمانوں کا حق ساقط کر دیا تو یہ غیر پر تصرف ہوا جس کو ولایت کہتے ہیں۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ جب مولی نے غلام کو جہاد کی اجازت دیدی، تو غلام بھی دوسرے مجاہدین کی طرح مالِ غنیمت میں شریک ہو گیا، اگر چہ غنیمت کا کامل حصہ نہ سہی عطیہ اور رضخ ہی سہی ، مگر ہے تو فی الجملہ مال غنیمت ہی ،اب جب وہ کا فر کو امان دے گا تو اولا اس نے اپنے حق میں تصرف کیا، پھر دوسروں کے حق میں اس کا اثر ضمنا پڑا، لہذا یہ باب ولایت میں سے شمار نہ ہوگا، اور یہ ایسا ہی ہے جیسے غلام رمضان کے چاند کی گواہی دے تو اس کی گواہی صحیح ہے اگر چہ وہ اہل ولایت میں سے نہیں ہے ، مگر پھر بھی شہادت اس لئے قبول ہے کہ اولاً وہ اپنے اوپر روزہ لازم کر رہا ہے پھر ضمنا اور تبعا یہ حکم دوسروں کی طرف متعدی ہو رہا ہے ، پس غلام کا ہر وہ فعل جو پہلے غلام کو متاثر کرے، پھر ضمناً آقا کی ملکیت کو ضائع کرے تو وہاں غلام کا فعل معتبر ہوگا۔
وعلى هذا الاصل يصح : - اسی اصول پر کہ غلام کا وہ فعل جو اولاً اس پر لازم ہو، تو پھر وہ تبعا دوسروں کی طرف معتدی ہوسکتا ہے۔ غلام اگر حدود اور قصاص کا اقرار کرے تو صحیح ہے، اور یہ اعتراض لازم نہ آئے گا کہ غلام کے اقرار سے مولی کا حق ضائع ہو رہا ہے، یعنی غلام کا ملک رقبہ جو قصاص سے ضائع ہوگا، کیونکہ اولا غلام نے اپنا حق تلف کیا، اور اس کے ضمن میں مولی کا حق تلف ہو رہا ہے ، اور یہ درست ہے کہ اولاً غلام پر کوئی چیز لازم ہو پھر وہ دوسروں کی طرف متعدی ہو، اسی طرح غلام اگر چوری کا اقرار کرے تو درست ہے، چاہے مال مسروق ہلاک ہو گیا ہو یا موجود ہو، غلام ماذون ہو یا مجور، بہر صورت اقرار درست ہے، اب اگر مال مسروق ہلاک ہو گیا تو صرف ہاتھ کٹے گا، ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا، کیونکہ قطع ید اور ضمان دونوں سزائیں ایک ساتھ نہیں ہوتی ہیں ، اور اگر مال مسروق موجود ہے تو جس سے چرایا ہے اس کو واپس کرنا ضروری ہے اور ہاتھ بھی کٹے گا، یہ غلام ماذون کے بارے میں حکم ہے، اور غلام مجور میں ائمہ کا اختلاف ہے، اگر غلام مجور چوری کرے تو دیکھیں گے کہ مال مسروق موجود ہے یا ہلاک ہو گیا، اگر ہلاک ہو گیا تو قطع ید ہوگا ، اور اگر مال باقی ہے، تو دیکھیں گے کہ آقا اس کی تصدیق کرتا ہے یا تکذیب ، اور مولی تصدیق کرتا ہے تو غلام مجور کا ہاتھ بھی کٹے گا اور مال لوٹا نا بھی ضروری ہے، اور اگر تکذیب کرتا ہے تو امام ابوحنیفہ اللہ کے نزدیک اس صورت میں بھی قطع ید اور مال کو لوٹانا دونوں ضروری ہیں ، امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک ہاتھ تو ابھی کٹے گا مگر ، مال مسروق کا ضمان اس کے آزاد ہونے کے بعد واجب ہوگا ، اور امام محمد کے نزدیک ابھی نہ اس کا ہاتھ کٹے گا نہ مال کو لوٹانا واجب ہوگا ، البتہ اس کے آزاد ہونے کے بعد اس پر مال کا ضمان واجب ہوگا۔ وعلى هذا قلنا فى جناية العبد - چونکہ رقیت مالکیت مال کے منافی ہے، اس بنیاد پر یہ کی ہے کہ اگر غلام نے خطا کوئی جنایت کی جیسے خطا کسی کوقتل کردیا تو چونکہ غلام کے پاس نہ مال ہے، نہ اس میں مالکیت کی اہلیت ہے، تو بجائے اس پر مال واجب کرنے کے اسی کی گردن کو جنایت کا عوض قرار دیا جائے گا، اور اس کو مقتول کے حوالہ کیا جائے گا ، ہاں اگر مولی اس کا فدیہ دینا منظور کرلے تو اب غلام جنایت کا عوض نہ ہوگا، بلکہ بقول امام ابوحنیفہ واجب اصلی کی طرف حکم لوٹ آئے گا، کیونکہ امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک واجب اصلی فدیہ دینا ہے یعنی دیت، مگر چونکہ غلام قادر نہیں ہوتا ، اس لئے اس کے رقبہ کو عوض قرار دیا گیا، اب جب مولی فدیہ دینے پر راضی ہو گیا، تو حکم اصل کی طرف لوٹ آئے گا، حتی کہ اگر مولی مفلس بھی ہو گیا تو اس کے افلاس کی وجہ سے فدیہ اور دیت کا وجوب باطل نہ ہوگا ، اور حکم اس کے رقبہ کی طرف عود نہ کرے گا۔
اور صاحبین کے نزدیک فدیہ دینا حوالہ کے درجہ میں ہے یعنی اصل وجوب غلام پر ہے، اس نے مولی کے حوالہ کر دیا، اور حوالہ میں یہ بات ہے کہ اگر محتال علیہ اداء حق سے عاجز ہو جائے تو محیل اور اصیل بری نہیں ہوتا ہے، لہذا مولی اگر مفلس ہو گیا، تو دیت غلام کے ذمہ میں ہوگی اور اس کے لئے غلام کا رقبہ حوالہ کیا جائے گا۔
A slave cannot have guardianship over others; thus a slave cannot marry anyone, cannot be a judge, cannot be a witness. A question arises: since all guardianship is severed from a slave, how is it correct for a slave authorized for jihad to give aman to a disbeliever, since this is also a guardianship? The answer: when the master gave permission for jihad, the slave shared in the spoils like other mujahidin, even if not a full share. When he gives aman, he first acts in his own right, and its effect on others is secondary. So this is not counted under guardianship. Similarly, if a slave testifies about the Ramadan moon, his testimony is accepted because he first imposes fasting on himself, and then the ruling extends to others secondarily. Thus every action of a slave that first affects himself and then secondarily causes loss to the master's property is valid. Upon this principle, if a slave confesses to hudud or qisas, it is valid, because he first forfeits his own right and the master's right is forfeited secondarily. Similarly, if a slave confesses to theft, it is valid, whether the stolen property is destroyed or extant, whether the slave is authorized (ma'dhun) or hired (ma'jur). If the stolen property is destroyed, only the hand is cut, no guarantee, because amputation and guarantee cannot combine. If extant, return is required and hand cut. This is the ruling for a ma'dhun slave. For a ma'jur slave there is ikhtilaf: if stolen property destroyed, only amputation; if extant, if master confirms, both amputation and return; if master denies, according to Abu Hanifa both are necessary, according to Abu Yusuf amputation now and guarantee after emancipation, according to Muhammad neither now but guarantee after emancipation. Upon this we said regarding a slave's unintentional crime: since slavery contradicts ownership of property, if a slave commits an unintentional murder, he has no property and no capacity for ownership, so instead of imposing a monetary penalty, his person is made the compensation and handed to the victim's family. If the master chooses to pay ransom, then according to Abu Hanifa the ruling returns to the original obligation (diyah), but since the slave was unable, his person was substitute. When master agrees to pay, the ruling returns to the original, even if the master becomes insolvent. According to the Sahibayn, paying ransom is like a transfer of debt (hawalah); the original obligation remains on the slave but is transferred to the master. If the master becomes insolvent, the diyah is on the slave and his person is the collateral.
Source pages p. 371

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Husami addresses a key usul principle regarding the legal capacity of slaves. The text opens by stating the general rule: a slave has no guardianship (wilayah) over others—cannot marry, judge, or testify in a representative capacity. However, a difficulty arises: a slave authorized for jihad can grant aman (safe conduct) to an enemy, which appears to be an act of guardianship. The resolution is that the slave first acts in his own interest (sharing in spoils), and only secondarily affects others. This distinguishes the action from true guardianship. The principle is then generalized: any act of a slave that first imposes an obligation on himself and only secondarily affects the master's rights is valid. Examples follow: a slave's testimony about the moon is accepted (he first obliges himself to fast); a slave's confession to hudud or qisas is valid (he first forfeits his own self, and the master's property right is lost secondarily). The text then details the ruling for theft confession by a ma'dhun (authorized) slave: if stolen property destroyed, only hand cut; if extant, return and hand cut. For a ma'jur (hired) slave, the Imams differ when the master denies the theft. Abu Hanifa rules both amputation and return immediately; Abu Yusuf rules amputation now and guarantee after emancipation; Muhammad rules neither now but guarantee later. Finally, the passage discusses unintentional crime (jinaayah) by a slave. Since a slave cannot own property, the default is that his person becomes the compensation. If the master chooses to ransom him, Abu Hanifa sees the ransom as the original obligation (diyah) revived, so even if the master becomes insolvent, the slave's person is not reverted to compensation. The Sahibayn view the ransom as a hawalah (transfer), so if the master cannot pay, the obligation returns to the slave and his person is collateral. This illustrates how the Hanafi school consistently applies the principle that the slave's actions are valid when they first affect himself.

Key Terms
غلام (ghulam): A male slave who is the property of a master, lacking full legal capacity for ownership and guardianship.
ماذون (ma'dhun): A slave authorized by his master to engage in trade; he has capacity to conduct business and incur liabilities within the scope of permission.
مجور (ma'jur): A slave hired out by his master to work for others; his earnings belong to the master and he has limited capacity to incur obligations.
اقرار (iqrar): A confession or admission of a right or liability; valid if it first imposes a duty on the confessant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is a slave's testimony about the Ramadan moon accepted?
A) Because the slave has full guardianship over religious matters.
B) Because the slave first obligates himself to fast, and the ruling extends to others secondarily.
C) Because the master's permission is always implied.
D) Because the moon sighting is a matter of necessity.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul principle that a slave's action is valid if it first affects himself and only secondarily affects his master governs cases of iqrar, aman, testimony, and jinaayah, with intra-school ikhtilaf reflecting different applications.

Suspicion of Will in Sick Person's Transactions
Explaining the legal concept of shubha wasiyya

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the concept of shubha wasiyya and apply the Hanafi rule that quality becomes compensable in ribawi exchanges due to suspicion of will, using qiyas to similar cases.

Core Idea
A sick person's exchange with an heir is examined for tuhma; quality difference becomes compensable even where normally irrelevant.

In this lesson, we explore the Hanafi principle of shubha wasiyya (suspicion of will). The passage shows how a sick person's transaction that outwardly appears as a sale or acknowledgment may be treated as a will if it unduly benefits an heir. This is an expansion probe: the author extends a normal usul rule (quality difference is not compensable in ribawi exchanges) by creating an exception due to tuhma. Through qiyas (analogy to a guardian's dealings), the rule is broadened to restrict such transactions.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish real will from shubha wasiyya
Identify the two categories: clear verbal bequest (real will) versus a transaction that in meaning is a will (shubha wasiyya). Examples include acknowledging a debt without evidence or exchanging ribawi goods of different quality.
2
Identify the specific scenario and default rule
Focus on the exchange of same-type ribawi goods with a quality difference. Normally, in such exchanges, quality is irrelevant and the transaction is permissible. Note the default: jawdat is not considered.
3
Apply the exception due to shubha wasiyya
Because the sick person may intend to benefit the heir through the quality difference, the transaction becomes impermissible. The quality difference becomes compensable (mutaqawwim) to block the hidden benefit.
This is a case of sadd al-dharai' (blocking the means to evil).
4
Trace the qiyas to the guardian rule
The author compares this to the rule that a father or guardian cannot trade a child's superior property for his own inferior property. In both cases, tuhma (suspicion) makes quality compensable.
The illa is the potential for self-dealing.
5
Formulate the operative rule
Generalize: In any transaction by a sick person with an heir, if the transaction involves ribawi goods and a quality difference, the quality difference must be compensated; otherwise, the transaction is invalid. This applies also to acknowledgments of debt.
The rule prevents circumventing the prohibition of bequest to an heir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
معنی وصیت :- یہ ہے کہ مریض وارث کے لئے قرض کا اقرار کرے کہ فلاں وارث کا میرے ذمہ اتنا قرض ہے، یا یوں کہے کہ صحت کے زمانہ مین جو میرا قرض فلاں وارث کے ذمہ تھا وہ میں نے وصول کر لیا ہے، تو یہ صورۃ تو اقرار ہے مگر معنی وصیت ہے کہ مریض اس طرح اس وارث کو مالی فائدہ پہنچانا چاہتا ہے یہ امکان ہے۔ حقیقی وصیت یہ ہے کہ مریض کسی وارث کے لئے کھلے الفاظ میں وصیت کرے۔ شبہ وصیت یہ ہے کہ مریض اموال ربویہ میں اپنا جید مال اسی کے جنس کا ردی مال لیکر کسی وارث کو نیچے، جیسے ایک کیل عمدہ گیہوں ایک کیل ردی گیہوں کے بدلہ نیچے، تو یہ نا جائز ہوگا کیونکہ شہبۂ وصیت موجود ہے، ممکن ہے کہ مریض اپنے وارث کو جود وعمدگی کا نفع پہنچانا چاہتا ہے، حالانکہ دو ایک جنس کی چیزوں میں عمدہ اور ردی کی بچ جائز ہے،ربو نہیں ہے، اس میں جودت کا اعتبار نہیں ہے لیکن یہاں رفع تہمت کے لئے جودت متقوم ہوگی ، ردی کے مقابلہ میں جودت کی الگ سے قیمت معتبر ہوگی، جیسے باپ یا وصی کو یہ اختیار نہیں ہے کہ بچہ کی عمدہ چیزا اپنی گھٹیا چیز سے بیچ کریں، کیونکہ بچوں کے حق میں بھی جودت متقوم ہے، الگ سے اس کی قیمت ہوگی ، حالانکہ عام معاملات میں جودت غیر متقوم ہے، مگر یہاں تہمت کی وجہ سے جودت متقوم ہوگی ، اس کا اعتبار ہوگا۔
Meaning of will: It is that a sick person acknowledges a debt for an heir, saying that a certain heir has such a debt upon me, or he says that during health my debt which was upon a certain heir, I have received it. So this form is an acknowledgment but in meaning a will, because the sick person intends by this to give financial benefit to that heir, it is possible. Real will is that the sick person makes a will for an heir in clear words. Suspicion of will is that a sick person in ribawi goods gives his good quality goods to an heir in exchange for bad quality goods of the same type, like one measure of good wheat for one measure of bad wheat, then this is impermissible because the suspicion of will exists; it is possible that the sick person wants to give the benefit of quality to his heir, whereas in two things of the same type, exchange of good and bad is permissible, there is no riba, quality is not considered in it. But here to remove suspicion, quality becomes compensable; the price of quality is considered separately against the bad, just as a father or guardian does not have the authority to sell the child's good quality thing for his own inferior thing, because with respect to children too quality is compensable, its price is separate, whereas in general transactions quality is not compensable. But here due to suspicion, quality becomes compensable, it will be considered.
Source pages p. 376

Commentary
This passage explains the concept of 'shubha wasiyya' (suspicion of will) as applied to a sick person's transactions with an heir. The author distinguishes between a real will (where the sick person explicitly bequeaths something to an heir) and a transaction that is formally a sale or acknowledgment but is treated as a will because it gives undue benefit to an heir, especially during terminal illness. Two examples are given: acknowledging a debt to an heir without evidence, and exchanging good quality goods for bad quality goods of the same type in a ribawi transaction. In the latter, normally barter of same goods with quality difference is allowed, but due to the suspicion that the sick person intends to benefit the heir, the quality difference becomes legally compensable. The author analogizes this to the rule for guardians (father or executor) who cannot trade a child's superior property for their own inferior property, because in both cases the potential for self-dealing is present. This ruling is based on the principle of preventing harm through legal devices (sadd al-dharai).

Key Terms
شبہ وصیت (shubha wasiyya): A transaction that appears to be a sale or acknowledgment but is treated as a will because of the suspicion that the sick person intends to benefit an heir unjustly.
جودت (jawdat): Quality or goodness of a commodity; normally not compensable in ribawi exchanges, but becomes compensable in this context due to suspicion.
متقوم (mutaqawwim): Having a recognized monetary value; here, the quality difference is considered as having value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the exchange of good quality wheat for bad quality wheat between a sick person and his heir considered impermissible?
A) Because riba is always prohibited in wheat exchanges.
B) Because there is a suspicion that the sick person intends to give a benefit to his heir through the quality difference.
C) Because quality can never be compensated in any transaction.
D) Because the sick person is not allowed to sell anything.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, shubha wasiyya causes quality difference in ribawi exchanges to become compensable when the seller is terminally ill and the buyer is an heir, based on the illa of tuhma and qiyas on guardian restrictions.

Deriving Rulings from Milk al-Nikah: Spousal Washing
Ruling with Shafi'i dispute via talil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to derive the Hanafi ruling on spousal washing of the deceased from the concept of milk al-nikah and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Marriage ownership persists for the husband's needs after his death, but ends for the wife at her death.

This passage addresses a specific fiqh issue with deep usul roots: who may wash the deceased spouse? The Hanafi ruling differentiates based on the concept of milk (ownership) in marriage. By analyzing the text, we uncover how a single legal concept generates asymmetric rulings, and how Imam Shafi'i challenges this asymmetry. Our task is to trace the Hanafi istinbat (derivation) and understand the point of ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hukm for each scenario
Extract the two rulings: wife may wash husband during her 'iddah; husband may not wash wife. Note the asymmetry.
The text explicitly states the husband cannot wash her.
2
Find the 'illa (effective cause)
The Hanafi reasoning: husband is owner (malik) of the marriage contract (milk al-nikah); wife is owned (mamluka). Ownership persists after husband's death for his needs (washing). For the wife, death ends her capacity to be owned.
The 'illa is the persistence of milk al-nikah for the husband's needs.
3
Refine the 'illa using tanqih al-manat
Is the 'illa simply 'ownership' or 'ownership that continues after death'? The text specifies 'especially in matters of need' – so the 'illa is persisting ownership for necessities.
The Shafi'i objection challenges the asymmetry.
4
Map the Shafi'i position
Imam Shafi'i holds that both spouses can wash each other. What is his basis? He likely argues that marriage creates mutual rights of service that survive death, without the ownership distinction.
Our text does not give Shafi'i's proof, but we can infer.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Hanafi, husband cannot wash wife; under Shafi'i, he can. This affects funeral arrangements. The dispute arises from different usul approaches to milk al-nikah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اسی لئے عورت شوہر کے انتقال کے بعد اپنی عدت میں اس کو غسل دے سکتی ہے، اس لئے کہ شوہر مالک ہے،ملک نکاح کا، لہذا عدت ختم ہونے تک ملکیت باقی رہے گی ، خاص کر ان چیزوں میں جس میں شوہر کو احتیاج ہے، اور غسل اس کی احتیاج وضرورت ہے، ہاں اگر بیوی مرگئی تو شوہر اس کو فنسل نہیں دے سکتا ہے، کیونکہ بیوی مملوکہ ہوتی ہے، اور موت کی وجہ سے مملوکیت کی اہل نہیں رہی۔ امام شافعی اللہ فرماتے ہیں کہ شوہر بھی اپنی مرحومہ بیوی کو غسل دے سکتا ہے جیسے بیوی شوہر کو دے سکتی ہے،
For this reason a woman can wash her husband after his death during her 'iddah, because the husband is the owner, owner of the marriage contract, so ownership remains until the 'iddah ends, especially in matters where the husband needs it, and washing is his need and necessity. Yes, if the wife dies, the husband cannot wash her, because the wife is owned, and because of death she is no longer eligible for ownership. Imam Shafi'i says that a husband can also wash his deceased wife just as the wife can wash her husband.
Source pages p. 382

Commentary
This passage presents a Hanafi ruling on spousal washing of the deceased, along with the Shafi'i position. The Hanafi ruling: a wife may wash her deceased husband during her 'iddah because the marriage contract's ownership persists until the 'iddah ends, and washing is a necessary service. Conversely, the husband cannot wash his deceased wife because she was 'owned' (mamluka) and death terminates her capacity to be owned. Imam Shafi'i disagrees, treating both equally. The reasoning is based on the concept of ownership (milk) in marriage and its survival after death for certain needs. The word 'mamluka' here refers to the wife's status as an object of ownership in the marriage contract, which ends with her death.

Key Terms
عدت ('iddah): The waiting period a woman observes after her husband's death, during which she cannot remarry.
ملک نکاح (milk al-nikah): Ownership of the marriage contract, which includes rights and duties.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) Because the husband is considered a mahram after death.
D) Because the wife is required to perform ghusl for the husband as part of her 'iddah obligations.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on spousal washing is derived from the concept of milk al-nikah, which creates an asymmetry based on the direction of ownership.

Qisas and Diyah: Who Owns the Right to Retaliation?
Textual analysis of the ruling on qisas and diyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that qisas is initially established for the heirs, not the deceased, and explain the change in ruling when qisas converts to diyah.

Core Idea
Qisas serves the heirs' need, not the deceased's; diyah as substitute becomes part of the deceased's estate.

This passage from Al-Husami explores a subtle distinction in the fourth category of rulings concerning the deceased. It explains that qisas (retaliation) is fundamentally for the benefit of the heirs, not the deceased, because the deceased lacks capacity after death. However, when the heirs agree to accept blood money (diyah) instead, that money is treated as part of the deceased's estate—debts are paid, will executed, and the remainder goes to heirs. Understanding this shift is crucial for correctly applying inheritance and criminal law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category of ruling
Recognize that the passage is classifying qisas under the fourth category of worldly rulings (rights that do not serve the deceased's need). This sets the stage for analyzing its legal effect.
The deceased's rights after death are only those fulfilling his needs (like debts and will).
2
Analyze the reasoning (ta'lil) for qisas being for heirs
The passage gives multiple reasons: (a) qisas becomes obligatory only after death, when the deceased has no legal capacity; (b) no need of the deceased is fulfilled by execution; (c) the purpose is to cool the hearts of the heirs and deter evil; (d) the killer wronged the heirs by ending their benefit from the deceased's life.
Each reason reinforces that qisas is inherently for the heirs, not the deceased.
3
Trace the conversion scenario
When heirs compromise with the killer and accept diyah (blood money) instead of execution, the ruling changes. The diyah is now treated as property belonging to the deceased's estate, used first for debts and will.
This is the practical legal transformation: from a personal right of heirs to a financial asset of the estate.
4
Extract the underlying usul principle
The general principle is that after death, only rights that serve the deceased's needs (e.g. payment of debts, execution of will) attach to the estate. Qisas cannot serve any need of the deceased, so it goes directly to the heirs as a separate category.
This principle is used by Hanafi jurists to differentiate between types of rights.
5
Compare with the opposing school (Shafi'i)
The Shafi'i school holds that qisas is initially established for the deceased and then inherited by the heirs. This leads to practical differences, e.g. whether the deceased can forgive qisas before death (Hanafi: yes, because the wrong is against him; Shafi'i: also yes, but based on ownership).
Understanding the ikhtilaf sharpens your application of the Hanafi rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
میت کا حق بقدر حاجت باقی رہتا ہے، اس لئے مقتول کا حق دیت سے متعلق ہو جائے گا جب کہ قصاص مال سے بدل جائے، یعنی اگر کسی نے عمداً کسی کو قتل کر دیا تو قاتل پر قصاص ہے، لیکن مقتول کے ورثہ نے مال کی کسی مقدار پر صلح کر لی، یا بعض ورثہ نے قصاص معاف کر دیا، اور بعض مال واجب کیا تو اس مال کا وہی حکم ہو گا جو میت کے دوسرے اموال کا ہے، چنانچہ اس مال دیت سے مقتول کا قرض ادا کیا جائے گا، اس کی وصیت نافذ ہوگی پھر جو بچے گا وہ ورثہ کو ملے گا۔ وان كان الاصل : - احکام دنیا کی چوتھی قسم کا بیان ہے، یعنی وہ حق جو میت کی حاجت پوری کرنے کی صلاحیت نہ رکھے، جیسے قصاص ، یہ میت کی حاجت پوری کرنے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتا ہے، کیوں کہ قصاص اولاً ورثہ کے لئے ثابت ہوتا ہے، ایسا نہیں ہے کہ اولاً میت کے لئے ثابت ہو، پھر منتقل ہوکر ورثہ کے لئے ثابت ہو، کیونکہ قصاص مقتول کی زندگی کے ختم پر واجب ہوتا ہے، اور موت سے اس کی اہلیت ہی نہیں رہتی ، پس قصاص سے اس کی کوئی حاجت متعلق نہیں ہوتی ہے، حالانکہ اس وقت اس کے لئے وہی چیز ثابت ہوگی جس کی طرف اس کی حاجت ہو، لہذا قصاص ابتداء ورثہ کے لئے ہوگا، کیونکہ قصاص کا مقصد قاتل کے شر کو دفع کرنا، اور اس سے بدلہ لینا ہے، جس سے مقتول کے اولیاء کا دل ٹھنڈا ہو، تو قصاص کی حاجت ورثہ سے متعلق ہوئی، نیز قاتل نے مقتول کو قتل کر کے اولیاء کے حق میں جنایت کی کہ مقتول کی زندگی سے اولیاء کا انتفاع ختم کر دیا، اس جہت سے بھی قصاص کی حاجت ورثہ سے متعلق ہوئی ،مگر چونکہ قصاص ایسے سب سے ہوا ہے جو مورث کے لئے منعقد ہوا ہے، کیونکہ مورث کی جان کا بدلہ ہے، تو اس جہت سے جنایت مقتول کے حق میں ہوئی، اس لئے اگر مرنے سے پہلے مقتول قاتل کو معاف کرنا چاہے تو معاف کرسکتا ہے، اور چونکہ اصلاً قصاص ورثہ کے لئے مشروع ہوا ہے ، اس لئے ورثہ زخمی مقتول کی موت سے پہلے قاتل کو معاف کر سکتے ہیں۔ بہر حال قصاص ابتداء ورثہ کے لئے ثابت ہوتا ہے، البتہ اگر یہ قصاص مال سے بدل جائے یعنی قصاص کے بدلہ میں مقتول کے اولیاء قاتل سے مال لینا طے کریں تو اب حکم بدل جائے گا، اب اس مال ودیت کے ساتھ اولا میت کا حق متعلق ہوگا، جیسے ماقبل میں آپ نے پڑھا۔
The right of the deceased remains to the extent of need, therefore the right of the slain is connected to the blood money when retaliation is replaced by property. That is, if someone intentionally kills another, the killer is subject to retaliation, but if the heirs of the slain compromise on some amount of property, or some heirs forgive retaliation and others impose property, then that property has the same ruling as the other properties of the deceased. So from that property (blood money), the debt of the slain will be paid, his will executed, and what remains goes to the heirs. And if the original (qisas) is of the fourth category of worldly rulings, i.e., a right that does not have the capacity to fulfill the deceased's need, like qisas—this does not have the capacity to fulfill the deceased's need, because qisas is established initially for the heirs. It is not that it is first established for the deceased and then transferred to the heirs, because qisas becomes obligatory upon the end of the slain person's life, and with death his capacity is gone. So no need of his is connected to qisas, whereas at that time only that which serves his need is established for him. Therefore, qisas is initially for the heirs, because the purpose of qisas is to repel the evil of the killer and to take revenge, which cools the hearts of the slain's guardians, so the need of qisas is connected to the heirs. Also, by killing the slain, the killer committed a wrong against the guardians by ending their benefit from his life, so from this aspect too the need of qisas is connected to the heirs. However, since qisas arises from the one who harmed the deceased, it is a compensation for the life of the deceased, so from this aspect the wrong was against the deceased. Therefore, if before death the slain wished to forgive the killer, he can forgive. And since originally qisas is legislated for the heirs, they can forgive the killer before the death of the injured slain. In any case, qisas is initially established for the heirs. But if this qisas is replaced by property, i.e., the guardians of the slain agree to take property from the killer in exchange for qisas, then the ruling changes: now this property (blood money) first attaches to the deceased's right, as you read previously.
Source pages p. 382

Commentary
This passage discusses the fourth category of worldly rulings concerning the deceased: rights that do not serve the deceased's need. Qisas (retaliation) is such a right. The key point is that qisas is not established for the deceased at all; it is directly for the heirs. The reasoning: qisas becomes obligatory only after death, when the deceased no longer has legal capacity. Its purpose is to benefit the heirs by satisfying their need for vengeance and deterring evil. Thus, qisas cannot fulfill any need of the deceased. However, if the heirs convert qisas into diyah (blood money), that property becomes part of the deceased's estate and is used first to pay off debts and execute the will. The text also notes an exception: the deceased himself can forgive qisas before death because the wrong is against him. The distinction between qisas and diyah is crucial: qisas is for the heirs, diyah (as substitute) is for the deceased's estate.

Key Terms
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation against the killer, typically execution. In this lesson, it is identified as a right that serves the heirs' need, not the deceased's.
دیت (diyah): Blood money paid as compensation for homicide. When substituted for qisas, it becomes part of the deceased's estate, used for debts and will first.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Qisas is for heirs because the deceased has no need for it; but when converted to diyah, the money serves the deceased's financial obligations.

Hanafi Refutation of Shafi'i on Qasamah and One Witness plus Oath
Criticizing Shafi'i rulings on oaths and witness-plus-oath

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi dalil (Quran 2:282 and the hadith 'al-bayyinah') used to reject Shafi'i positions on qasamah and one-witness-plus-oath, and apply the usul principle that general Quranic commands take precedence over specific Prophetic actions unless proven to be exceptions.

Core Idea
General Quranic and Hadith principles override limited Prophetic precedents in Hanafi usul.

This passage presents a classic Hanafi refutation of two Shafi'i rulings: the use of collective oaths (qasamah) to impose diyah, and the acceptance of one witness plus an oath as sufficient evidence. The Hanafi commentator argues that both rulings contradict explicit Quranic injunctions (2:282) and the well-known hadith 'al-bayyinah ala al-muddai...'. This lesson will break down the dispute and the Hanafi usul reasoning, focusing on how the Hanafi school prioritizes general textual evidence over specific Prophetic actions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two disputed rulings
First, identify exactly what Imam al-Shafi'i permits that the Hanafis reject: (1) Qasamah: fifty oaths from the locality when there is enmity or signs of murder, leading to diyah on them. (2) One witness plus oath: judgment based on a single witness accompanied by the plaintiff's oath.
Shafi'i relies on Prophetic practice for both, while Hanafis rely on general Quranic and Hadith texts.
2
State the Hanafi counterarguments
For each ruling, state the specific evidence the Hanafis cite: Against qasamah, they say it contradicts the established sunnah (the Prophet's practice in similar cases). Against one witness plus oath, they quote Quran 2:282 requiring two men or one man and two women, and the hadith 'al-bayyinah ala al-muddai wa al-yamin ala man ankara' (proof is on the claimant, oath on the denier).
These texts are general and unambiguous, according to Hanafis.
3
Analyze the usul principle at stake
The core usul principle is that a general (amm) text from the Quran or sunnah mutawatirah cannot be overridden by a specific (khass) Prophetic action unless that action is proven to be an exception (takhsis) with equal or stronger authority. Hanafis argue that Shafi'i's proof (prophetic precedent) is either weak in transmission or specific to a context that does not extend to general application.
This is a classic Hanafi usul rule: al-amm yakhussu bi-dalil aqwa, but here the opposing dalil is not strong enough.
4
Examine the tarjih and adab
The text declares the Hanafi position as correct and Shafi'i's as 'rejected' (mardud). The commentator adds a caution that such harsh words are from earlier scholars and should not be taken as disrespect to the imam. This shows that even in refutation, adab (etiquette) is important.
The tarjih here is based on the strength of the general text over a specific action.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ہوگی ۔ امام شافعی اللہ کا قول جدید یہ ہے کہ اگر اہل محلہ اور میت کے درمیان عداوت ہو یا اور کوئی قتل کی علامت ہو تو صلى الله عليه وسلم مقتول کے اولیا اہل محلہ سے پچاس قسمیں لیں گے، اگر اہل محلہ قسم کھالیں تو مدعا علیہ پر دیت واجب ہوگی، دعوی چاہے قتل عمد کا ہو یا قتل خطا کا ہمارا امام شافعی سے اختلاف ان کے قول قدیم کی صورت میں ہے، امام شافعی نے کا یہ قول سنت مشہورہ کے خلاف ہے، لہذار د ہوگا۔ اسی طرح امام شافعی کہتے ہیں کہ کسی کے پاس اگر ایک ہی گواہ ہو تو دوسرے گواہ کی جگہ اس سے قسم لیکر فیصلہ کیا جاسکتا ہے ان کے نزدیک ایک گواہ اور ایک قسم سے فیصلہ جائز ہے، کیونکہ حضور صلی ایام نے ایسا کیا ہے ،مگر احناف کہتے ہیں کہ یہ مذہب کتاب الله واستشهدوا شهدين من رجالكم فان لم يكونا رجلين فرجل وامرأتان“ کے خلاف ہے اور حديث مشهور " البينة على المدعى واليمین علی من انکر“ کے خلاف ہے، لہذا یہ رد ہوگا۔ انتباہ: اس جگہ ائمہ مجتہدین کی شان میں باطل مردود وغیرہ جو الفاظ ہیں ، وہ سلف کے ذکر کردہ ہیں، ہم نے صرف نقل کیا ہے، نقل کفر کفر نباشد ہم ایسے سخت الفاظ کہنے کی اور ان عظیم المرتبت مجتہدین کے مذہب کو مبنی بر جہل کہنے کی ہرگز جرات نہیں کر سکتے ، یہ تو انہیں کو حق ہیں جو ان کے ہم پلہ ہیں۔
It will happen. Imam Shafi'i's new opinion is that if there is enmity between the people of the locality and the deceased, or any other sign of murder, then the heirs of the slain will take fifty oaths from the people of the locality. If the people of the locality take the oath, then diyah will be obligatory on the defendant, whether the claim is for intentional murder or manslaughter. Our difference with Imam Shafi'i is in the case of his old opinion. Imam Shafi'i's this opinion is against the well-known sunnah, therefore it is rejected. Similarly, Imam Shafi'i says that if someone has only one witness, then in place of a second witness, an oath can be taken from him and judgment can be passed. According to him, judgment with one witness and one oath is permissible, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) did this. But the Hanafis say that this opinion is against the Book of Allah: 'And call to witness two men from among you. And if two men be not there, then one man and two women' (2:282) and against the famous hadith: 'Proof is on the claimant, and the oath is on the denier.' Therefore, it is rejected. Warning: At this place, the words like false and rejected etc. regarding the dignity of the imams of ijtihad are those mentioned by the predecessors; we have only narrated them. Quoting disbelief is not disbelief. We cannot dare to say such harsh words or call the madhhab of these great imams based on ignorance; this right belongs only to those who are their peers.
Source pages p. 387

Commentary
This passage is a madhhab dispute in which the Hanafi commentator refutes two rulings of Imam al-Shafi'i. First, regarding qasamah (compurgation): Shafi'i's view that fifty oaths are taken from the people of the locality when there is enmity or signs of murder is rejected by Hanafis as contrary to the established sunnah (presumably the practice of the Prophet which limited qasamah to cases of lawth or strong suspicion). Second, regarding combining one witness with an oath: Shafi'i permits judgment on this basis citing a Prophetic precedent, but the Hanafis argue this contradicts the Quranic verse requiring two male witnesses (or one male and two females) for financial claims, and the general principle that proof is on the claimant while the oath is for the defendant. The commentator adds a cautionary note that the harsh terms used (like 'rejected') are from earlier scholars and should not be taken as disrespect.

Key Terms
قسامة (qasamah): A collective oath taken by the people of a locality to deny responsibility for a murder, leading to liability for diyah if they refuse
شهادة (shahadah): Testimony; in this context, the requirement of two male witnesses or one male and two females for financial claims
اليمين (al-yamin): Oath; a binding declaration by the defendant (usually) to deny a claim, or by the plaintiff in some cases

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafis in this passage, why is the ruling of one witness plus oath rejected?
A) Because the Prophet never did it
B) Because it contradicts the Quranic requirement of two witnesses or one man and two women
C) Because it is based on weak hadith
D) Because it was only for a specific case

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a general text from the Quran or sunnah mutawatirah cannot be overridden by a specific Prophetic action unless the action is proven to be an equally authoritative general rule.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
10 min
Types of Ignorance (Jahl) and Their Legal Effects: Mawdi' Ijtihad and Udhr
Explains third and fourth types of jahl with examples from Hanafi fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the third and fourth types of jahl in Hanafi usul, classify examples into mawdi' ijtihad, mawdi' ishtibah, or excusable ignorance (udhr), and explain why some ignorance is excused while other is not.

Core Idea
Not all ignorance excuses – only jahl in matters of valid ijtihad, genuine doubt, or when knowledge was impossible.

In Hanafi usul, ignorance is not a blanket excuse. This passage from Al-Faidh al-Hijaz classifies two more types of jahl: one that creates doubt (shubha) and one that serves as a valid excuse in transactions and family law. Understanding these distinctions helps determine when penalties like hadd and kaffara are averted, and when rights are preserved despite ignorance. We'll work through the examples to see how the Hanafi school balances legal liability with subjective culpability.

Guided Path
1
Define the third type of jahl
Identify that the third type is 'jahl capable of becoming shubha' and occurs either in a place of valid ijtihad (mawdi' ijtihad) or in a place of genuine doubt (mawdi' ishtibah). Note its effect: it averts hadd and kaffara.
Shubha here means a doubt that clouds the certainty of prohibition.
2
Analyze the examples for third type
Classify the cupping example (jahl fi mawdi' ijtihad because Imam al-Awza'i differs) and the zina with father's slave woman example (jahl fi mawdi' ishtibah because of common property usage). Explain why each constitutes shubha.
The cupping example shows that valid ikhtilaf among mujtahids creates shubha.
3
Define the fourth type of jahl
Understand that the fourth type is 'jahl that is a valid excuse (udhr) in non-hadd/kaffara matters', where the person could not have known without negligence. It preserves rights and exempts from liability.
Examples range from agency to marriage and slave laws.
4
Work through the examples for fourth type
List each example from the passage: ignorance of appointment/revocation (wakeel/ma'dhun), ignorance of sale by pre-emptor (shafi'), ignorance of slave's crime by master, ignorance of marriage by virgin girl, ignorance of khiyar al-itiq by slave woman. For each, explain why it is an excuse.
Notice the common thread: the person was unaware and had no reasonable way to know at the time.
5
Distinguish excusable from inexcusable ignorance
Contrast the slave woman's ignorance of khiyar al-itiq (excused due to preoccupation) with the free woman's ignorance of khiyar al-bulugh (not excused because she could have learned). Identify the principle: negligence when knowledge is accessible makes jahl inexcusable.
This highlights the Hanafi concern for actual capability and fault.
